\section{Actual PDE Completion Protocol}

\subsection{Honest status}

The present goal is not to rebuild the theorem chain from scratch.
It is to populate the already-closed carrier-level certificate with actual branch data extracted from the full microscopic TECT linearization:
\[
\boxed{
\text{proof complete, certificate incomplete.}
}
\]

Equivalently, the remaining frontier is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{finite microscopic audit, not new theorem-building.}
}
\]

\subsection{Actual PDE meaning}

The phrase ``complete the theory from the actual PDE'' should be understood as follows.

One starts from the actual Bloch--Floquet linearized operator around the intended BCC background:
\[
L(k).
\]

Then one extracts the finite reduced carrier data by the chain
\[
\boxed{
L(k)
\;\longrightarrow\;
K_i := \partial_{k_i}L\big|_{G_*}
\;\longrightarrow\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\longrightarrow\;
M_{3i}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\lambda_\parallel,
}
\]
together with the transverse derivative data at the same shell point.

Thus the remaining work is not ``solve the whole nonlinear PDE in one shot'',
but rather:
\[
\boxed{
\text{extract the branch-dependent finite coefficients from the actual microscopic operator.}
}
\]

\subsection{Gate 1: remote-gap numerical insertion}

The first certificate slot is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

Hence the first numerical task is:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min(\text{finite benchmark channel gaps}),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\text{remote-sector correction bound},
\]
and then evaluate the signed margin
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_1
:=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

Gate 1 passes iff
\[
\mathfrak G_1>0.
\]

\subsection{Gate 2: actual longitudinal extraction}

The exact intervalley witness is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,
\bigl(\hat n^i K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}(x)\bigr)\,
u_b^-(x).
}
\]

The reduced longitudinal coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
m_3
=
-\frac{1}{2\Gamma_J}
\left(
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{11}-\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{22}
\right).
}
\]

At the refined locked working level this is compressed to
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
\qquad
L_*
=
m_\parallel u_\parallel
=
\frac{m_\parallel}{2}(u_{11}-u_{22}).
}
\]

A practical sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

Thus the numerical longitudinal margin is
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_2
:=
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|-|R_N|.
}
\]

Gate 2 passes iff
\[
\mathfrak G_2>0.
\]

\subsection{Gate 3: derivative-resolved transverse audit}

The honest transport-side transverse witnesses are
\[
\boxed{
c_E
=
\frac14\Tr(\Sigma_1\mathcal T_1+\Sigma_2\mathcal T_2),
\qquad
c_O
=
\frac14\Tr(\Sigma_2\mathcal T_1-\Sigma_1\mathcal T_2),
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\]

Hence the transport-side pass condition is
\[
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

On the explicit folded-Bragg working branch, the strongest practical sufficient test is
\[
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0.
}
\]

The calibration layer is
\[
\boxed{
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

Thus a practical transverse numerical audit computes
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak G_{3,\mathrm{tr}}:=|c_E|+|c_O|,
\qquad
\mathfrak G_{3,\mathrm{cal}}:=|C_E|+|C_O|.
}
\]

Gate 3 passes iff
\[
\mathfrak G_{3,\mathrm{tr}}>0,
\qquad
\mathfrak G_{3,\mathrm{cal}}>0.
\]

\subsection{Gate 4: constant-sector commutator audit}

The residual generator is
\[
\boxed{
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
}
\]

The full corrected microscopic constant-sector test is
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\]

In the present working truncation,
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}=\varnothing
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0
\Longrightarrow
\Sigma(0,0)=0,
\]
so Gate 4 is largely reduced to a finite low-block constant audit.

\subsection{Final actual certificate}

The fully populated actual branch certificate is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}\wedge\text{Gate 2}\wedge\text{Gate 3}\wedge\text{Gate 4}
\Longrightarrow
\text{isolated protected anisotropic massless Dirac carrier.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

Yes:
the next correct target is full completion from the actual microscopic PDE data.

But ``actual PDE completion'' now means:
\[
\boxed{
\text{extract finite branch-dependent coefficients from the full microscopic linearized operator}
}
\]
rather than
\[
\boxed{
\text{re-solve the whole nonlinear PDE from scratch.}
}
\]

Numerical extraction is not optional.
It is exactly the remaining task.

The practical computational order is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1} \;\to\; \text{Gate 2} \;\to\; \text{Gate 3} \;\to\; \text{Gate 4}.
}
\]

Among these, Gate 4 is already nearly closed in the present working truncation,
so the main numerical burden is the actual evaluation of:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}},\quad
\eta_{R,\rho},\quad
\Delta_{00},\quad
L_*,\quad
A_{G_*},\quad
(c_E,c_O),\quad
(C_E,C_O).
\]

\section{Gate 1 Actual PDE Closure on the Explicit Canonical Pure-Even Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present stage, Gate 1 is no longer a conceptual theorem problem.
For the explicit canonical pure-even branch, it is reduced to one explicit finite inequality.

The exact support condition remains
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

On the explicit branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \eta=z_0,\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
the sharpest currently available practical form is obtained by inserting the same-shell
non-enriched scalar lower bound and the fully inserted residual budget.

\section{1. Master Gate-1 condition}

The benchmark side is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
\Biggr\}.
}
\]

The residual side satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\rho(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

Hence a sufficient actual branch Gate-1 condition is
\[
\boxed{
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
\Biggr\}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

\section{2. Same-shell non-enriched scalar insertion}

The usable same-shell benchmark entry is reduced to
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
\ge
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho),
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
:=
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
-
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)},
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
a_K=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2.
}
\]

Therefore the non-enriched benchmark is positive once
\[
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}.
}
\]

\section{3. Small-\texorpdfstring{$p$}{p} drift budget}

For the minimal same-shell truncation \(N=1\),
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+(p) & m(p)\\
\overline{m(p)} & d_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\]
with expansions
\[
\boxed{
d_\pm(p)=d_\pm^{(0)}+p_i a_{\pm,i}+R_\pm^{(2)}(p),
\qquad
m(p)=m_0+p_i b_i+R_m^{(2)}(p).
}
\]

Define
\[
\boxed{
A_+
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|a_{+,i}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
A_-
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|a_{-,i}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
B
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|b_i|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_++C_+\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-+C_-\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B+C_m\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
}
\]

At leading order,
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
=
\rho L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}+O(\rho^2),
\qquad
L_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}
=
\sqrt{A_+^2+A_-^2+2B^2}.
}
\]

\section{4. Actual derivative coefficients}

On the explicit pure-even branch,
\[
\boxed{
a_{+,i}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}\,
q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_K\,\ell_{+,i}^{EE},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
a_{-,i}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}\,
q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_K\,\ell_{-,i}^{EE},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
b_i=-a_K\,\ell_{0,i}^{EE}.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
A_+
\le
\left|q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_K L_+,
\qquad
A_-
\le
\left|q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_K L_-,
\qquad
B\le a_K L_0.
}
\]

Therefore the small-\(p\) drift is itself reduced to the finite overlap-derivative vectors
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{EE},\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{EE},\qquad
\ell_{0,i}^{EE}.
}
\]

\section{5. Pure-even canonical sharpening}

If the residual transport side is also taken pure-even and one adopts the canonical normalization
\[
\boxed{
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
}
\]
then
\[
|C_E|+|C_O|\longrightarrow |C_E|=1,
\]
so the non--wrong estimate sharpens to
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\le
\kappa\rho
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right).
}
\]

Thus the sharpest explicit sufficient Gate-1 inequality becomes
\[
\boxed{
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
\Biggr\}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
>
2\left[
\kappa\rho
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

\section{6. What is actually left}

So Gate 1 is now reduced to the finite insertion of the branch constants
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},
\quad
\ell_{+,i}^{EE},\ \ell_{-,i}^{EE},\ \ell_{0,i}^{EE},
\quad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_{\mathrm{high,non}},
\quad
K_a,\widetilde K_a,r_a,\sigma_a,
\quad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho},
}
\]
together with the already explicit bulk-shell parameters
\[
\boxed{
K,\ r_*,\ M_\sigma,\ c_\sigma,\ q_*,\ \lambda+\mu,\ g,\ \mu,\ Z,\ Y,\ u,\ A,\ \Lambda_E^{(0)},\ \alpha_X,\beta_X,M_X.
}
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 is structurally closed and executable,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{its PASS/FAIL stamp still requires the actual branch constants above.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

At the actual PDE stage, the correct next move is Gate 1 finite insertion.

For the explicit canonical pure-even branch, the sharpest available Gate-1 sufficient inequality is

\section{Actual PDE Completion on the Explicit Canonical Pure-Even Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

For the current explicit canonical pure-even branch
\[
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,\qquad \eta=z_0,\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
the reduced infrared PDE is already completed at the practical working-branch level.

What is still missing is not the PDE form itself, but the final finite audit needed for the full unconditional microscopic certificate.

\section{1. Exact completed infrared PDE}

The reduced infrared symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\end{equation}

On the explicit pure-even working branch, one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta=0,
}
\end{equation}
so the PDE simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\alpha\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact coefficient dictionary}

In Branch B, the exact overlap dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit defect overlaps,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
}
\end{equation}
the pure-even working realization gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit actual PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,
\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa\,
(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2))
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Numerical coefficient sheet}

Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
\approx
0.03188319195\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^3,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
\approx
0.34008738079\,
\frac{\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\end{equation}

Since
\[
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2),
\]
the explicit pure-even branch gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
=
\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{131072}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X^3}{M_X^6}\,
\theta_0^5\kappa^5,
}
\end{equation}
hence numerically
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M
\approx
0.003687591698\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X^3}{M_X^6}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^5.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore a sufficient nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
\theta_0\kappa\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Gate 2 and Gate 3 finite pass sheet}

The current carrier-side longitudinal witness is already reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-,
\qquad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\end{equation}

The practical sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\), it is enough to verify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq0,
\qquad
L_*\neq0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

For the transverse sector, the pass condition remains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0),
}
\end{equation}
equivalently, on the explicit folded-Bragg branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Gate 1: what still blocks full unconditional closure}

The sharpest currently available Gate-1 inequality on this branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
\Biggr\},
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{non}}^{(1)}(\rho)
=
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
-
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)},
}
\end{equation}
and residual side
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
2\left[
\kappa\rho(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right)
\right]
+
2C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the full unconditional Gate-1 pass condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\end{equation}

At the present stage, the only genuinely missing part is the finite insertion of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},
\quad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)},
\quad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)},
\quad
C_{\mathrm{high,non}},
\quad
K_a,\widetilde K_a,r_a,\sigma_a,
\quad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual reduced infrared PDE is already completed on the present working branch,}
}
\end{equation}
with explicit coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta
\]
and explicit numerical prefactors.

However,

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the full unconditional microscopic certificate is not yet numerically complete,}
}
\end{equation}
because Gate 1 still requires the insertion of finitely many branch-specific constants.

Equivalently,

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{working-branch PDE: closed,}
\qquad
\text{full unconditional audit: still awaiting finite insertion.}
}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{How to Extract All Remaining Finite Insertion Constants}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present stage, all unresolved quantities are already reduced to finite explicit audits.
No new structural theorem is needed.

The remaining constants fall into four computational classes:
\[
\boxed{
\text{finite overlap sums},\qquad
\text{derivatives at }p=0,\qquad
\text{finite residual norms/tails},\qquad
\text{constant-block commutators}.
}
\]

Therefore the right question is no longer
\[
\text{``Can these constants be defined?''}
\]
but rather
\[
\text{``Which finite operator or overlap must be evaluated for each constant?''}
\]

\section{1. Global map of the remaining unresolved slots}

The genuinely remaining finite audit slots are:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{JJ}
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O),
\qquad
(C_E,C_O),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}],
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}],
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)].
}
\]

So every remaining object is already a finite insertion target.

\section{2. Gate 1: same-shell non-enriched benchmark}

\subsection{2.1. Core strategy}

The same-shell non-enriched slot is already reduced to the finite Hermitian block
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p).
}
\]
For \(N=1\),
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+(p) & m(p)\\
\overline{m(p)} & d_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

Thus the extraction protocol is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute \(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(0)\);
\item compute its spectral distance from zero;
\item bound the perturbation on \(|p|\le \rho\).
\end{enumerate}

This yields
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\ge
\Delta_0^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(N)},
}
\]
and after truncation control,
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\]

\subsection{2.2. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}$}{SdiagEE}}

At \(p=0\), the explicit pure-even branch gives
\[
d_+^{(0)}
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)-a_K\mathcal S_{++}^{EE},
\qquad
d_-^{(0)}
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)-a_K\mathcal S_{--}^{EE},
\]
\[
m_0
=
B_{z_0}(0)-a_K\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE},
\qquad
a_K=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2.
\]

If the residual is valley-symmetric,
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}=\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}=:\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}.
}
\]

Therefore \(\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}\) is extracted by:

\begin{enumerate}
\item build the finite \(EE\)-overlap matrix of the non-enriched same-shell sector at \(p=0\);
\item evaluate its diagonal valley entries \(\mathcal S_{++}^{EE},\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}\);
\item in the symmetric branch, identify their common value as \(\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}\);
\item otherwise keep the asymmetric pair and use the larger one in the bound.
\end{enumerate}

Operationally, this is a finite cell-integral / finite Fourier-sum computation.

\subsection{2.3. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$\ell_{+,i}^{EE},\ell_{-,i}^{EE},\ell_{0,i}^{EE}$}{ell vectors}}

The derivative overlap vectors are defined by
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{EE}
=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{EE}
=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(p)\right|_{p=0},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{0,i}^{EE}
=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
}
\]

So these are obtained by:

\begin{enumerate}
\item construct the \(p\)-dependent overlap sums \(\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(p),\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(p),\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(p)\);
\item differentiate them with respect to \(p_i\);
\item evaluate at \(p=0\).
\end{enumerate}

These are genuine first-derivative data, not new unknown parameters.

Their norms are
\[
L_+=\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{+,i}^{EE}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_-=\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{-,i}^{EE}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_0=\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{0,i}^{EE}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
\]

\subsection{2.4. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$C_+,C_-,C_m$}{C constants} and \texorpdfstring{$\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}$}{eps small-p}}

Near \(p=0\),
\[
d_\pm(p)=d_\pm^{(0)}+p_i a_{\pm,i}+R_\pm^{(2)}(p),
\qquad
m(p)=m_0+p_i b_i+R_m^{(2)}(p),
\]
with
\[
|R_+^{(2)}(p)|\le C_+\rho^2,
\qquad
|R_-^{(2)}(p)|\le C_-\rho^2,
\qquad
|R_m^{(2)}(p)|\le C_m\rho^2.
\]

Hence \(C_+,C_-,C_m\) are second-derivative remainder bounds.
They are extracted by:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute or bound the Hessians \(\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}d_\pm(p)\), \(\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}m(p)\) on \(|p|\le\rho\);
\item take uniform sup norms;
\item convert them into quadratic Taylor constants \(C_+,C_-,C_m\).
\end{enumerate}

Then
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_++C_+\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-+C_-\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B+C_m\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2},
}
\]
where
\[
A_\pm=\Bigl(\sum_i|a_{\pm,i}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
B=\Bigl(\sum_i|b_i|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
\]

Thus \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}\) is not an extra free constant:
it is produced from first- and second-derivative data.

\subsection{2.5. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}$}{eps non-enr}}

The truncation error enters through the upgrade
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(N)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
<
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},0}^{(N)}.
\]

The same-shell notes reduce this to:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a finite heavy-overlap sum \(\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE,(N)}\),
\item a finite tail bound \(\mathcal R_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE,(N)}\),
\item a finite small-\(p\) plus truncation budget.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}\) is extracted by one of two equivalent routes:

\paragraph{Route A: rigorous tail route.}
Estimate the omitted shell/basis tail
\[
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE,(N)}
=
\sum_{\text{omitted modes}} |\cdots|,
\]
using decay/power-counting of the overlap kernel, and turn it into a norm bound.

\paragraph{Route B: monotone numerical stabilization route.}
Compute the same-shell benchmark at \(N,N+1,N+2,\dots\), verify convergence, and use the last increment as a rigorous-enough posteriori upper bound only if monotone decay is proven.
Without monotone control, this route is heuristic, not theorem-level.

So the fully honest theorem-level route is Route A.

\section{3. Gate 1: residual remote budget}

\subsection{3.1. Master decomposition}

The residual side is already reduced to
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\|E_\rho\|_2
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho},
}
\]
or more weakly
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\max\{S_{\mathrm{vol}},S_{\mathrm{high}},S_{\mathrm{non}},S_{\mathrm{wrong}}\}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

Thus there are three extraction tasks.

\subsection{3.2. How to extract the pair budgets and \texorpdfstring{$C_{\mathrm{high,non}}$}{C high non}}

The remaining six pair budgets are
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho},
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho},
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho},
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho},
\eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho},
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}.
\]

For the dominant explicit branch, the inserted notes already give
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\le
\kappa\rho(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(\alpha_X^2+|\alpha_X\beta_X|+\beta_X^2\right),
\]
and
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}\le C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\rho.
\]

Therefore \(C_{\mathrm{high,non}}\) is extracted as:
\[
\boxed{
C_{\mathrm{high,non}}
=
\sup_{0<|p|\le \rho_0}
\frac{\|E_{\mathrm{high,non}}(p)\|}{|p|},
}
\]
or via a corresponding row-sum norm bound on that pair block.

So the method is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item isolate the high/non block of the remote mixing matrix;
\item differentiate or directly bound it for small \(p\);
\item divide by \(|p|\) and take the uniform supremum.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{3.3. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$K_a,\widetilde K_a,r_a,\sigma_a$}{tail constants}}

The tail theorem already has the form
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge1.
}
\]

Hence these constants are extracted by:

\begin{enumerate}
\item enumerate the active omitted channel families \(a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}},\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}\);
\item determine the low-\(p\) scaling exponent \(r_a\) of each family;
\item determine the heavy-scale suppression exponent \(\sigma_a\) where applicable;
\item compute the corresponding prefactors \(K_a,\widetilde K_a\) from the channelwise norm bounds.
\end{enumerate}

This is a pure power-counting + family-enumeration problem.

\subsection{3.4. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}$}{eta diag}}

The diagonal correction budget is
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p)\|.
}
\]

So the method is literal:
construct the diagonal remainder \(R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p)\) after the chosen truncation/splitting, then take the operator-norm supremum on the ball \(|p|\le\rho\).

This is usually the cleanest object to compute numerically after the symbolic subtraction has been fixed.

\section{4. Gate 2: longitudinal finite data}

\subsection{4.1. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$\Xi_{JJ}$}{Xi JJ} and \texorpdfstring{$L_*$}{Lstar}}

The exact longitudinal witness is already reduced to
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,
(\hat n^i K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}(x))\,
u_b^-(x).
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
m_3
=
-\frac{1}{2\Gamma_J}
(\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{11}-\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{22}).
}
\]

At the refined locked working level this is compressed to
\[
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\]

Therefore the extraction protocol is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item build the pure-\(JJ\) intervalley block \(K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\);
\item compute the cell overlap matrix \(\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{ab}\);
\item take the diagonal difference \(\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{11}-\mathcal M^{(JJ)}_{22}\);
\item identify \(\Xi_{JJ}\) or equivalently \(L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{4.2. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$\Delta_{00}$}{Delta00}}

The working-level scalar is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}=\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-.
}
\]

So one must:
\begin{enumerate}
\item solve the low-slot eigenproblem at \(p=0\);
\item obtain the normalized valley basis vectors \(\eta_+,\eta_-\);
\item evaluate the single \(2\times 2\) Pauli overlap \(\eta_+^\dagger\Sigma_3\eta_-\).
\end{enumerate}

This is a finite eigensystem computation, not a PDE problem anymore.

\subsection{4.3. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$A_{G_*}$}{AG*}}

On the explicit folded-Bragg branch, \(A_{G_*}\) is the Fourier amplitude of the relevant \(G_*\)-harmonic.
Hence it is extracted by:
\[
\boxed{
A_{G_*}
=
\widehat A(G_*)
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\; e^{-iG_*\cdot x}A(x),
}
\]
or by the equivalent discrete Fourier coefficient in the Bloch/Fourier basis.

\section{5. Gate 3: transverse witnesses and calibration}

\subsection{5.1. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$(c_E,c_O)$}{cE cO}}

The honest transverse frontier is
\[
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad \nu=1,2.
}
\]

The Pauli witnesses are
\[
\boxed{
c_E=\frac14\Tr(\Sigma_1\mathcal T_1+\Sigma_2\mathcal T_2),
\qquad
c_O=\frac14\Tr(\Sigma_2\mathcal T_1-\Sigma_1\mathcal T_2).
}
\]

Hence the extraction protocol is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item compute the derivative-resolved shell blocks at \(Q=G_*\);
\item assemble the transverse shell tensors \(\mathcal T_1,\mathcal T_2\);
\item project onto the \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2\) Pauli basis;
\item read off \(c_E,c_O\).
\end{enumerate}

Inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch, this compresses to
\[
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q'),
\]
and at first-shell dominant level to
\[
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)\propto iA_{G_*}(C_\alpha\cdot G_*).
}
\]

So on the working branch, a fast sufficient test is just to evaluate
\[
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*),
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*).
\]

\subsection{5.2. How to extract \texorpdfstring{$(C_E,C_O)$}{CE CO}}

The Bloch calibration layer is exact:
\[
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
\]

The overlap formulas are
\[
\boxed{
C_E
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)}),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_O
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)}).
}
\]

So the extraction method is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item build the normalized \(E\)- and \(O\)-unit inputs;
\item compute the folded-Bragg overlap matrices \(M^1_{(E)},M^2_{(E)},M^1_{(O)},M^2_{(O)}\);
\item evaluate the two trace formulas above.
\end{enumerate}

This is a pure finite calibration computation.

\section{6. Gate 4: constant-sector commutator audit}

The remaining Gate-4 test is
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
}
\qquad
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3.
\]

Thus the extraction protocol is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item project the constant block of the microscopic operator to the \(4\times4\) carrier space;
\item write each constant correction in the explicit \(\tau_a\otimes s_b\) basis;
\item compute the three commutators with \(Q_*\);
\item verify that all coefficients outside the \(Q_*\)-commuting algebra vanish.
\end{enumerate}

So Gate 4 is not an unknown-constant problem at all:
it is a finite matrix-algebra check.

\section{7. What is rigorous, what is only practical}

The following routes are theorem-level rigorous:
\begin{enumerate}
\item finite overlap/cell-integral evaluation;
\item \(p=0\) derivative evaluation;
\item operator-norm or row-sum supremum bounds;
\item explicit tail power-counting bounds;
\item direct commutator computation.
\end{enumerate}

The following can be useful numerically but are not theorem-level by themselves:
\begin{enumerate}
\item plain convergence-by-eye in \(N\);
\item fitting unknown exponents from data without a prior bound;
\item assuming valley symmetry or canonical normalization without verifying them.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

Yes: in principle all remaining insertion constants can be extracted.

More precisely, they reduce to:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},\ell_{\pm,i}^{EE},\ell_{0,i}^{EE},C_\pm,C_m
\;\;\longleftarrow\;\;
\text{same-shell overlap sums and their first/second }p\text{-derivatives};
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},K_a,\widetilde K_a,r_a,\sigma_a,C_{\mathrm{high,non}},\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
\;\;\longleftarrow\;\;
\text{finite residual norms + tail power counting};
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{00},\Xi_{JJ},L_*,A_{G_*}
\;\;\longleftarrow\;\;
\text{finite low-slot eigensystem + cell overlaps + Fourier coefficient};
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O),(C_E,C_O)
\;\;\longleftarrow\;\;
\text{derivative-resolved shell audit + Bloch calibration traces};
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}],
\;
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}],
\;
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]
\;\;\longleftarrow\;\;
\text{finite }4\times4\text{ commutator audit}.
}
\end{equation}

So the remaining project is algorithmic, not conceptual.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Gate 1 Same-Shell Extraction Layer: Exact Formulas for }
\texorpdfstring{$\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},\ell_{\pm,i}^{EE},\ell_{0,i}^{EE},C_\pm,C_m$}{Sdiag, ell, C}

\section{Short explanation}

All six unresolved same-shell constants are generated by one common heavy-resolvent object:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p).
}
\]
Once \(\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)\) is available, we obtain
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}=\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(0)=\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(0),
\]
\[
\ell_{+,i}^{EE}=\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(0),\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{EE}=\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(0),\qquad
\ell_{0,i}^{EE}=\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(0),
\]
and the quadratic drift constants \(C_+,C_-,C_m\) from second derivatives.

Thus the whole problem reduces to one source--resolvent construction.

\section{1. Low-slot states and heavy block}

Let
\[
|\phi_+(p)\rangle,\qquad |\phi_-(p)\rangle
\]
denote the same-shell non-enriched low states in the common Bloch sector \(k_*+p\).
Let
\[
\Pi_H
\]
be the projector onto the heavy complementary space, and let
\[
\mathbb O_H(p)
\]
be the heavy block of the reference microscopic operator restricted to \(\Pi_H\mathcal H\).

Assume
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb O_H(p)\ge \Delta_H>0
}
\]
for \(|p|\le \rho\), so that the heavy resolvent exists:
\[
\boxed{
R_H(p):=\mathbb O_H(p)^{-1}\quad\text{on }\Pi_H\mathcal H.
}
\]

\section{2. Even source vectors}

Let \(\mathcal O_E(p)\) denote the even heavy source operator induced by the pure-even residual \(KK\)-sector.
Define the heavy source vectors
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|v_a^{E}(p)\rangle
:=
\Pi_H\,\mathcal O_E(p)\,|\phi_a(p)\rangle,
\qquad a\in\{+,-\}.
}
\label{eq:vE_def}
\end{equation}

Then the exact heavy-overlap tensor is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
:=
\langle v_a^{E}(p),\,R_H(p)\,v_b^{E}(p)\rangle.
}
\label{eq:S_resolvent_def}
\end{equation}

This is the common generating object for all remaining same-shell constants.

\section{3. Spectral-sum representation}

If one diagonalizes the heavy block,
\[
\mathbb O_H(p)|\chi_\alpha(p)\rangle=E_\alpha(p)|\chi_\alpha(p)\rangle,
\qquad E_\alpha(p)\ge \Delta_H,
\]
and defines
\[
\mathcal E_{a\alpha}(p):=\langle \chi_\alpha(p)|v_a^E(p)\rangle
=
\langle \chi_\alpha(p)|\mathcal O_E(p)|\phi_a(p)\rangle,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
=
\sum_\alpha
\frac{
\mathcal E_{a\alpha}(p)\,\overline{\mathcal E_{b\alpha}(p)}
}{
E_\alpha(p)
}.
}
\label{eq:S_spectral}
\end{equation}

Thus the already-used Schur form
\[
-\sum_\alpha \frac{K_{a\alpha}\overline{K_{b\alpha}}}{E_\alpha}
\]
is exactly the spectral form of \(\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)\).

\section{4. Coordinate-space cell-integral formula}

Work in the Bloch gauge
\[
\phi_a(p,x)=e^{i(k_*+p)\cdot x}u_a(p,x),
\qquad
\chi_\alpha(p,x)=e^{i(k_*+p)\cdot x}w_\alpha(p,x),
\]
with \(u_a,w_\alpha\) periodic on the primitive cell.

Define the Bloch-conjugated even source operator
\[
\mathcal O_E^{(k_*+p)}
:=
e^{-i(k_*+p)\cdot x}\,
\mathcal O_E(p)\,
e^{i(k_*+p)\cdot x}.
\]

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{a\alpha}(p)
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
\overline{w_\alpha(p,x)}\,
\bigl(\mathcal O_E^{(k_*+p)}u_a(p,\cdot)\bigr)(x).
}
\label{eq:E_cell}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
=
\sum_\alpha \frac{1}{E_\alpha(p)}
\left(
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
\overline{w_\alpha}\,\mathcal O_E^{(k_*+p)}u_a
\right)
\overline{
\left(
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
\overline{w_\alpha}\,\mathcal O_E^{(k_*+p)}u_b
\right)
}.
}
\label{eq:S_cell}
\end{equation}

This is the cleanest theorem-level coordinate-space formula.

\section{5. Reciprocal-space finite Fourier-sum formula}

Expand the periodic parts in reciprocal lattice modes:
\[
u_a(p,x)=\sum_{Q\in\mathcal G}u_{a,Q}(p)e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
w_\alpha(p,x)=\sum_{Q\in\mathcal G}c_{\alpha,Q}(p)e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\]

Likewise write the periodic operator kernel as
\[
\mathcal O_E^{(k_*+p)}(x)
=
\sum_{G\in\mathcal G}\widehat{\mathcal O}_E^{(k_*+p)}(G)e^{iG\cdot x}.
\]

Then the overlap amplitudes become the finite/discretized Fourier sums
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal E_{a\alpha}(p)
=
\sum_{Q,P\in\mathcal G}
\overline{c_{\alpha,Q}(p)}\,
\widehat{\mathcal O}_E^{(k_*+p)}(Q-P)\,
u_{a,P}(p).
}
\label{eq:E_fourier}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
=
\sum_\alpha \frac{1}{E_\alpha(p)}
\left(
\sum_{Q,P}
\overline{c_{\alpha,Q}}\,\widehat{\mathcal O}_E(Q-P)\,u_{a,P}
\right)
\overline{
\left(
\sum_{Q',P'}
\overline{c_{\alpha,Q'}}\,\widehat{\mathcal O}_E(Q'-P')\,u_{b,P'}
\right)
}.
}
\label{eq:S_fourier}
\end{equation}

This is the formula to implement directly in a shell-Fourier code.

\section{6. Extraction of \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}$}{Sdiag}}

At \(p=0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(0),\qquad
\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(0),\qquad
\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(0)
}
\label{eq:S0_triplet}
\end{equation}
are computed from \eqref{eq:S_resolvent_def} or \eqref{eq:S_spectral}.

If valley symmetry holds,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(0)=\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(0)=:\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}.
}
\label{eq:Sdiag_def}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
=
\langle v_+^E(0),R_H(0)v_+^E(0)\rangle
=
\langle v_-^E(0),R_H(0)v_-^E(0)\rangle.
}
\label{eq:Sdiag_formula}
\end{equation}

\section{7. First derivatives and extraction of }
\texorpdfstring{$\ell_{+,i}^{EE},\ell_{-,i}^{EE},\ell_{0,i}^{EE}$}{ell}

Differentiate \eqref{eq:S_resolvent_def}. Since
\[
\partial_{p_i}R_H
=
-R_H(\partial_{p_i}\mathbb O_H)R_H,
\]
we obtain
\begin{align}
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
&=
\langle \partial_i v_a^E,R_H v_b^E\rangle
+
\langle v_a^E,R_H\partial_i v_b^E\rangle
-
\langle v_a^E,R_H(\partial_i\mathbb O_H)R_H v_b^E\rangle.
\label{eq:dS_general}
\end{align}

Evaluating at \(p=0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{EE}
=
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(0),
\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{EE}
=
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(0),
\qquad
\ell_{0,i}^{EE}
=
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(0).
}
\label{eq:ell_def_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in source-resolvent form,
\begin{align}
\ell_{+,i}^{EE}
&=
\langle \partial_i v_+^E,R_H v_+^E\rangle
+
\langle v_+^E,R_H\partial_i v_+^E\rangle
-
\langle v_+^E,R_H(\partial_i\mathbb O_H)R_H v_+^E\rangle,
\\
\ell_{-,i}^{EE}
&=
\langle \partial_i v_-^E,R_H v_-^E\rangle
+
\langle v_-^E,R_H\partial_i v_-^E\rangle
-
\langle v_-^E,R_H(\partial_i\mathbb O_H)R_H v_-^E\rangle,
\\
\ell_{0,i}^{EE}
&=
\langle \partial_i v_+^E,R_H v_-^E\rangle
+
\langle v_+^E,R_H\partial_i v_-^E\rangle
-
\langle v_+^E,R_H(\partial_i\mathbb O_H)R_H v_-^E\rangle,
\end{align}
all evaluated at \(p=0\).

\section{8. Linear-solve realization without heavy diagonalization}

Define
\[
|y_b(p)\rangle:=R_H(p)|v_b^E(p)\rangle,
\qquad\text{so}\qquad
\mathbb O_H(p)\,|y_b(p)\rangle=|v_b^E(p)\rangle.
\]

Then
\[
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)=\langle v_a^E(p),y_b(p)\rangle.
\]

Differentiate once:
\[
\mathbb O_H\,|y_{b,i}^{(1)}\rangle
=
|\partial_i v_b^E\rangle-(\partial_i\mathbb O_H)|y_b\rangle,
\]
where
\[
|y_{b,i}^{(1)}\rangle:=\partial_{p_i}|y_b\rangle.
\]

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}
=
\langle \partial_i v_a^E,y_b\rangle
+
\langle v_a^E,y_{b,i}^{(1)}\rangle.
}
\label{eq:dS_linear_solve}
\end{equation}

This is the most implementation-friendly route:
it avoids summing over the full heavy spectrum.

\section{9. Second derivatives and extraction of }
\texorpdfstring{$C_+,C_-,C_m$}{C constants}

From the same-shell block,
\[
d_+(p)=d_+^{(0)}+p_i a_{+,i}+R_+^{(2)}(p),
\qquad
d_-(p)=d_-^{(0)}+p_i a_{-,i}+R_-^{(2)}(p),
\]
\[
m(p)=m_0+p_i b_i+R_m^{(2)}(p),
\]
with
\[
a_{+,i}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}\,q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)-a_K\ell_{+,i}^{EE},
\]
\[
a_{-,i}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}\,q_*\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)-a_K\ell_{-,i}^{EE},
\qquad
b_i=-a_K\ell_{0,i}^{EE}.
\]

Now define the Hessians
\[
H^{(+)}_{ij}(p):=\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}d_+(p),
\qquad
H^{(-)}_{ij}(p):=\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}d_-(p),
\qquad
H^{(m)}_{ij}(p):=\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}m(p).
\]

A rigorous Taylor bound gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_+
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|H^{(+)}(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}},
\qquad
C_-
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|H^{(-)}(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}},
\qquad
C_m
:=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|H^{(m)}(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}}.
}
\label{eq:CpmCm_def}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\[
|R_+^{(2)}(p)|\le C_+\rho^2,
\qquad
|R_-^{(2)}(p)|\le C_-\rho^2,
\qquad
|R_m^{(2)}(p)|\le C_m\rho^2.
\]

Since
\[
d_+(p)=E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(p)-a_K\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(p),
\qquad
d_-(p)=E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(p)-a_K\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(p),
\]
\[
m(p)=B_{z_0}(p)-a_K\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(p),
\]
we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(+)}_{ij}
=
\partial_{ij}E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}
-a_K\,\partial_{ij}\mathcal S_{++}^{EE},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(-)}_{ij}
=
\partial_{ij}E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}
-a_K\,\partial_{ij}\mathcal S_{--}^{EE},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(m)}_{ij}
=
\partial_{ij}B_{z_0}
-a_K\,\partial_{ij}\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the quadratic constants are entirely determined by the second \(p\)-derivatives of the same overlap tensor.

\section{10. Second-derivative linear-solve route}

Differentiate the heavy solve a second time.
Let
\[
|y_{b,ij}^{(2)}\rangle:=\partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}|y_b\rangle.
\]
Then
\begin{align}
\mathbb O_H\,|y_{b,ij}^{(2)}\rangle
&=
|\partial_{ij}v_b^E\rangle
-(\partial_{ij}\mathbb O_H)|y_b\rangle
-(\partial_i\mathbb O_H)|y_{b,j}^{(1)}\rangle
-(\partial_j\mathbb O_H)|y_{b,i}^{(1)}\rangle.
\label{eq:y2_eq}
\end{align}

Hence
\begin{align}
\partial_{ij}\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}
&=
\langle \partial_{ij}v_a^E,y_b\rangle
+\langle \partial_i v_a^E,y_{b,j}^{(1)}\rangle
+\langle \partial_j v_a^E,y_{b,i}^{(1)}\rangle
+\langle v_a^E,y_{b,ij}^{(2)}\rangle.
\label{eq:d2S_linear_solve}
\end{align}

This yields \(C_+,C_-,C_m\) without explicit heavy spectral summation.

\section{11. Minimal executable algorithm}

The exact finite algorithm is therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Solve the low-slot Bloch problem at \(k_*+p\) and obtain \(|\phi_\pm(p)\rangle\).
\item Build the heavy block \(\mathbb O_H(p)\) and the even source operator \(\mathcal O_E(p)\).
\item Form the heavy source vectors \(|v_\pm^E(p)\rangle=\Pi_H\mathcal O_E(p)|\phi_\pm(p)\rangle\).
\item Solve
\[
\mathbb O_H(0)\,|y_\pm\rangle=|v_\pm^E(0)\rangle
\]
and compute
\[
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(0)=\langle v_a^E(0),y_b\rangle.
\]
\item Differentiate once, solve for \(|y_{\pm,i}^{(1)}\rangle\), and evaluate
\[
\ell_{+,i}^{EE},\quad \ell_{-,i}^{EE},\quad \ell_{0,i}^{EE}.
\]
\item Differentiate twice, solve for \(|y_{\pm,ij}^{(2)}\rangle\), and bound
\[
C_+,\quad C_-,\quad C_m.
\]
\item Insert these into
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_++C_+\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-+C_-\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B+C_m\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{12. Final consequence}

So the same-shell Gate-1 constants are not independent unknowns.

They are all generated by the one source--resolvent tensor
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)=\langle v_a^E(p),\mathbb O_H(p)^{-1}v_b^E(p)\rangle.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
\text{ comes from } \mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(0),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{EE},\ell_{-,i}^{EE},\ell_{0,i}^{EE}
\text{ come from } \partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(0),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_+,C_-,C_m
\text{ come from } \partial_{p_i}\partial_{p_j}\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
\text{ on } |p|\le \rho.
}
\]

Hence the entire same-shell benchmark-side finite insertion problem is reduced to one common microscopic extraction layer.

\section{Final Summary}

The six unresolved same-shell Gate-1 constants
\[
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE},\quad
\ell_{+,i}^{EE},\quad
\ell_{-,i}^{EE},\quad
\ell_{0,i}^{EE},\quad
C_+,\quad
C_-,\quad
C_m
\]
are not independent parameters.

They are all generated by the single heavy-resolvent tensor
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
=
\langle v_a^E(p),\mathbb O_H(p)^{-1}v_b^E(p)\rangle.
}
\]

Equivalently, in a heavy eigenbasis,
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
=
\sum_\alpha
\frac{
\mathcal E_{a\alpha}(p)\,\overline{\mathcal E_{b\alpha}(p)}
}{
E_\alpha(p)
}.
}
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
=
\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(0)=\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(0),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{EE}
=
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(0),\quad
\ell_{-,i}^{EE}
=
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(0),\quad
\ell_{0,i}^{EE}
=
\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(0),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_+
=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|\nabla_p^2 d_+(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}},\quad
C_-
=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|\nabla_p^2 d_-(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}},\quad
C_m
=
\frac12\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|\nabla_p^2 m(p)\|_{\mathrm{op}}.
}
\]

Hence the whole same-shell benchmark-side finite insertion problem is reduced to one common source--resolvent extraction layer.

\begin{verbatim}

def delta00_from_blocks(E_plus, E_minus):
    eps_plus, eta_plus = low_eigenpair(E_plus)
    eps_minus, eta_minus = low_eigenpair(E_minus)
    delta00 = np.vdot(eta_plus, SIGMA3 @ eta_minus)
    return float(np.real_if_close(delta00))

def u_parallel_from_matrix(U_parallel):
    return float(np.real_if_close(0.5 * (U_parallel[0, 0] - U_parallel[1, 1])))

def L_star(m_parallel, U_parallel):
    return m_parallel * u_parallel_from_matrix(U_parallel)

def coeff_sheet_canonical(alpha_X, beta_X, M_X, theta0, kappa,
                          C_parallel=1.0, C_E=1.0):
    c_parallel_num = 3.0 * math.sqrt(3.0) * math.pi / 512.0
    c_trans_num = math.sqrt(3.0) * math.pi / 16.0
    lambda_parallel = c_parallel_num * (alpha_X * beta_X / (M_X ** 2)) * C_parallel 
    * (theta0 ** 3) * (kappa ** 3)
    alpha = c_trans_num * (beta_X / (M_X ** 2)) * C_E * theta0 * kappa
    beta = 0.0
    det_M = lambda_parallel * (alpha ** 2 + beta ** 2)
    return lambda_parallel, alpha, beta, det_M

def gate2_margin(delta00, alpha_X, L_star_val, A_Gstar, R_N=0.0):
    return abs(delta00 * alpha_X * L_star_val * A_Gstar) - R_N
    
\end{verbatim}

\text{the remaining unresolved part is only finite branch-parameter insertion.}
}
\]

Equivalently, there is no remaining theorem-level obstruction at the working-branch level.
The remaining frontier is numerical certification of the already-derived formulas.

\section{Executable insertion chain for the explicit }N=1\text{ locked-branch test}

Define the heavy denominator
\[
\boxed{
D_H
:=
M_H^2
+
Z\left(\frac{q_*^2}{4}+\frac{207}{65}\kappa^2\right)
+
Y\left(
\frac{q_*^4}{16}
+\frac{207}{130}q_*^2\kappa^2
+\frac{2529}{65}\kappa^4
\right).
}
\]

Then the source-aligned one-mode susceptibility is
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3^{(1)}
=
\frac{
\frac{1}{693}
\left(\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\right)^2
q_*^2 A_\perp \theta_0^6\kappa^5
}{
D_H
}.
}
\]

Next define
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_A^{(1)}
=
q_*^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2\,\chi_3^{(1)}.
}
\]

The locked-branch working condition is then
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_A^{(1)}<\frac65\,m_0,
\qquad
m_0=4uA^2.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_A^{(1)}<\frac{24}{5}uA^2.
}
\]

So the entire actual \(N=1\) audit is reduced to the finite scalar insertion
\[
\boxed{
(\delta W_\parallel,\alpha_X\beta_X/M_X^2,q_*,A_\perp,\theta_0,\kappa,M_H^2,Z,Y,uA^2).
}
\]

\section{Final reduction of the locked-branch numerical bottleneck}

The actual branch data already close
\[
m_0,\qquad \delta W_\parallel,
\]
and compress the stabilization coefficient into
\[
\Lambda_A=\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2.
\]

Therefore the minimal locked-branch condition
\[
0<\Lambda_A<\frac65\,m_0
\]
becomes
\[
\boxed{
0<
\frac{\chi_3 q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2}{4u\mathcal A^2}
<
\frac65.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
0<
\chi_3
<
\frac{24}{5}\,
\frac{u\mathcal A^2}{q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2}.
}
\]

Thus the entire actual working-branch stabilization problem is reduced to a single scalar inequality for \(\chi_3\).

\section{14-faced cell representation of the heavy susceptibility}

Let \(\Omega_{14}\) denote the truncated-octahedral Wigner--Seitz cell of the BCC condensate.
Expand the heavy-shell source and heavy operator in the BCC Bloch basis:
\[
v_\parallel(x)
=
\sum_{G\in\Lambda_H^*} v_G\,e^{i(k_*+G)\cdot x},
\]
\[
\bigl[\mathbb O_H^{(0)}\bigr]_{GG'}
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega_{14}|}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
e^{-i(k_*+G)\cdot x}\,
\mathbb O_H^{(0)}\,
e^{i(k_*+G')\cdot x}.
\]

Then
\[
v_G
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega_{14}|}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
e^{-i(k_*+G)\cdot x}\,
v_\parallel(x),
\]
and the exact heavy susceptibility is
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3
=
\sum_{G,G'\in\Lambda_H^*}
\overline{v_G}\,
\bigl[(\mathbb O_H^{(0)})^{-1}\bigr]_{GG'}\,
v_{G'}.
}
\]

So the 14-faced cell does provide an exact finite-cell integral representation of \(\chi_3\).
However, the numerical value still depends on the microscopic matrix elements of \(\mathbb O_H^{(0)}\), not on geometry alone.

\section{Standard Exact Route via the 14-Faced BCC Cell}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The correct standard route is not to guess \(\chi_3\), but to compute it from the heavy-sector operator on the truncated-octahedral BCC cell.

The decisive scalar is
\[
\chi_3=\langle v_\parallel,(\mathbb O_H^{(0)})^{-1}v_\parallel\rangle,
\]
and the actual locked-branch condition is
\[
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2\chi_3<\frac65\,m_0.
\]

Hence the problem is reduced to:
\[
\boxed{
\text{construct }v_\parallel,\ \mathbb O_H^{(0)}
\text{ on the BCC 14-faced cell, then evaluate }
\chi_3.
}
\]

\section{1. Real-space cell and Bloch-harmonic representation}

Let \(\Omega_{14}\) be the truncated-octahedral Wigner--Seitz cell of the BCC condensate.
The condensed background is the equal-amplitude BCC shell field
\[
\phi_0(\mathbf x)=2A\sum_{a=1}^6 \cos(\mathbf Q_a\cdot \mathbf x),
\]
so \(\Omega_{14}\) is the natural primitive integration domain.

Let the heavy-sector Bloch harmonics at the folded Bragg point be
\[
\varphi_G(x)=|\Omega_{14}|^{-1/2}e^{i(k_*+G)\cdot x},
\qquad
G\in \Lambda_H^*.
\]

Expand the heavy source and heavy operator as
\[
v_\parallel(x)=\sum_G v_G\,\varphi_G(x),
\]
\[
\bigl[\mathbb O_H^{(0)}\bigr]_{GG'}
=
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
\overline{\varphi_G(x)}\,
\mathbb O_H^{(0)}\,
\varphi_{G'}(x).
\]

Then
\[
v_G
=
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
\overline{\varphi_G(x)}\,v_\parallel(x).
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3
=
\sum_{G,G'} \overline{v_G}\,
\bigl[(\mathbb O_H^{(0)})^{-1}\bigr]_{GG'}\,
v_{G'}.
}
\]

This is the exact 14-faced-cell formula.

\section{2. Rigorous sufficient route: heavy-gap bound}

Let
\[
\Delta_H:=\inf \sigma(\mathbb O_H^{(0)})>0.
\]
Then
\[
(\mathbb O_H^{(0)})^{-1}\le \Delta_H^{-1},
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3\le \frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}.
}
\]

Therefore a rigorous sufficient locked-branch condition is
\[
\boxed{
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}
<
\frac65\,m_0.
}
\]

Using
\[
m_0=4u\mathcal A^2,
\]
this becomes
\[
\boxed{
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}
<
\frac{24}{5}u\mathcal A^2.
}
\]

\section{3. Finite working route: source-aligned one-mode variational estimate}

If one uses the source-aligned \(N=1\) heavy trial state, then
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3^{(1)}=\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}.
}
\]

So the finite working test is
\[
\boxed{
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}
<
\frac65\,m_0.
}
\]

Again, with \(m_0=4u\mathcal A^2\),
\[
\boxed{
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2
\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}
<
\frac{24}{5}u\mathcal A^2.
}
\]

\section{4. Explicit \(N=1\) formula already available}

The notes already give the actual one-mode source norm and variational energy:
\[
\boxed{
\|v_\parallel\|^2
=
\frac{4}{693}\lambda_c^2 k_*^2 A_\perp \theta_0^6\kappa^5,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}
=
M_H^2
+
Z\left(k_*^2+\frac{207}{65}\kappa^2\right)
+
Y\left(k_*^4+\frac{414}{65}k_*^2\kappa^2+\frac{2529}{65}\kappa^4\right).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3^{(1)}
=
\frac{
\frac{4}{693}\lambda_c^2 k_*^2 A_\perp \theta_0^6\kappa^5
}{
M_H^2
+
Z\left(k_*^2+\frac{207}{65}\kappa^2\right)
+
Y\left(k_*^4+\frac{414}{65}k_*^2\kappa^2+\frac{2529}{65}\kappa^4\right)
}.
}
\]

So the standard route is fully reduced to a finite insertion problem.

\section{5. What is actually left}

The remaining nonredundant work is now exactly one of the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Exact route:
compute the heavy-cell matrix \([\mathbb O_H^{(0)}]_{GG'}\) and the source coefficients \(v_G\) on \(\Omega_{14}\), then evaluate
\[
\chi_3
=
\overline v^{\,T}(\mathbb O_H^{(0)})^{-1}v.
\]

\item Rigorous sufficient route:
compute \(\|v_\parallel\|^2\) and a heavy gap lower bound \(\Delta_H\), then test
\[
q_0^4(\delta W_\parallel)^2\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{\Delta_H}
<
\frac{24}{5}u\mathcal A^2.
\]

\item Practical finite route:
use the already reduced \(N=1\) data and insert
\[
\chi_3^{(1)}=\frac{\|v_\parallel\|^2}{E_{\parallel,1}^{\mathrm{var}}}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{What is correct and what is still not yet proved}

\section{Short explanation}

The 14-faced Wigner--Seitz cell of the BCC condensate is indeed the natural exact integration domain.
So replacing spherical or one-dimensional surrogate integrals by polyhedral cell integrals is the correct geometric direction.

However, this does \emph{not} by itself prove that CKM/CP predictions become exact.
What is already closed is the structural reduction of the CKM problem to finite microscopic data.
What is \emph{not yet} closed is the numerical filling of the intended-branch microscopic input tables.

\section{1. What is already closed}

The BCC reciprocal star background is
\[
\phi_0(\mathbf x)=2A\sum_{a=1}^{6}\cos(\mathbf Q_a\cdot\mathbf x),
\]
and its real-space primitive cell is the truncated octahedron (14-faced cell).
Thus the exact real-space cell for BCC-adapted matrix elements is \(\Omega_{14}\).

The CKM program is also structurally reduced to a finite executable audit:
\[
(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d)\to J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}},
\qquad
(\Lambda,\Delta,r)\to \Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\to J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{pred}}.
\]

So the conceptual infinite-dimensional problem is already reduced to finite microscopic data.

\section{2. What is not yet closed}

The notes explicitly state that the full microscopic intended-branch closure is not yet complete.
What remains is the explicit numerical filling of the intended-branch input tables:
\[
S,\ M^{(u,d)},\ N^{(u,d)},
\qquad
\Lambda_{ij}^{(u,d)},\ \Delta_{ij}^{(u,d)},\ r_{ij}^{(u,d)},
\]
together with the final consistency check
\[
\left|J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\right|\le E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
\]

So the honest status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{structural closure: yes,}
\qquad
\text{full intended-branch numerical closure: not yet.}
}
\]

\section{3. What the 14-faced-cell route can actually do}

The polyhedral route should be used to compute exact BCC-adapted matrix elements on the primitive cell:
\[
\bigl[\mathcal O\bigr]_{GG'}
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega_{14}|}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
e^{-i(k_*+G)\cdot x}\,
\mathcal O\,
e^{i(k_*+G')\cdot x}.
\]

This can systematically replace spherical or naive one-dimensional surrogates in all cell-dependent projected quantities.

In particular, it is the correct backend for:
\[
S,\quad M^{(f)},\quad N^{(f)},\quad Z^{(f)},\quad \widehat Y^{(f)},
\]
and for the projected link data
\[
\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)},\quad \Delta_{ij}^{(f)},\quad r_{ij}^{(f)}.
\]

\section{4. What the 14-faced-cell route does \emph{not} automatically do}

Not every microscopic quantity is purely a cell-volume integral.
Defect-profile overlaps still contain profile dependence and in some channels anisotropic tail dependence.
So the 14-faced cell does not magically remove all model dependence.

It removes the wrong geometric cutoff.
It does not eliminate the need to compute the actual microscopic kernels.

\section{5. The correct rigorous conclusion}

Therefore the correct claim is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the 14-faced polyhedral route is the correct exact geometric refinement of the microscopic pipeline,}
}
\]
but not yet:

\[
\boxed{
\text{it is already proven to reproduce the PDG CKM numbers automatically.}
}
\]

That stronger statement requires the actual intended-branch numerical evaluation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Polyhedral Refinement of the Microscopic CKM Pipeline}

\subsection{Honest status}

The BCC condensate selects a truncated-octahedral Wigner--Seitz cell \(\Omega_{14}\) as the natural primitive real-space integration domain.
Therefore any projected microscopic matrix element should, in the exact geometric formulation, be evaluated over \(\Omega_{14}\) rather than by a spherical or one-dimensional surrogate.

However, the current TECT notes still state that the CKM program is only structurally closed, while the full microscopic intended-branch numerical closure is not yet complete.
Therefore the 14-faced-cell route should presently be introduced as the correct exact geometric backend and as the leading candidate for the missing intended-branch numerical extraction, not yet as a completed theorem-level PDG fit.

\subsection{Exact polyhedral replacement principle}

Let \(\mathcal O\) be any microscopic operator entering the family-space reduction.
Then the exact BCC-adapted projected matrix element should be written as
\[
\boxed{
[\mathcal O]_{GG'}
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega_{14}|}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
e^{-i(k_*+G)\cdot x}\,
\mathcal O(x)\,
e^{i(k_*+G')\cdot x}.
}
\]

This replaces the geometrically incorrect spherical cutoff and the reduced one-dimensional surrogate by the exact truncated-octahedral primitive-cell integral.

\subsection{Leading-order face-flux heuristic}

At leading order, the 14-faced cell distinguishes two geometrically inequivalent face families:
\[
d_H=\frac{\sqrt3}{2},
\qquad
d_S=1.
\]
A minimal flux heuristic therefore suggests
\[
W_H\sim e^{-d_H^2}=e^{-3/4},
\qquad
W_S\sim e^{-d_S^2}=e^{-1}.
\]

This immediately provides the correct qualitative mechanism for anisotropic hierarchy restoration:
nearest hexagonal-face transport dominates the \(1\text{--}2\) channel,
the more weakly transmitted square-face channel controls the \(2\text{--}3\) sector,
and the \(1\text{--}3\) sector remains suppressed and phase-sensitive.

\subsection{Correct theorem-level use}

The theorem-level statement should therefore be:

\begin{quote}
The 14-faced-cell formulation is the exact geometric refinement of the microscopic TECT CKM pipeline.
It explains why the previous spherical/1D surrogates can underestimate the physical overlap hierarchy, and it provides the correct primitive-cell backend for the intended-branch numerical audit.
\end{quote}

But the stronger claim

\begin{quote}
the 14-faced-cell route already proves the final PDG CKM numbers
\end{quote}

must be postponed until the actual intended-branch finite audit is executed.

\subsection{Correct paper architecture}

The logically clean structure is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Geometry theorem:} exact BCC primitive-cell replacement by the truncated octahedron;
\item \textbf{Leading-order proposition:} anisotropic face-flux hierarchy restores the correct CKM scale ordering;
\item \textbf{Numerical completion:} multi-shell continuous profile integration on the intended branch yields the final percent-level fit.
\end{enumerate}

This cleanly separates:
\[
\boxed{
\text{analytic geometric why}
}
\qquad\text{from}\qquad
\boxed{
\text{numerical exact what}.
}
\]
