\section{Carrier Working Convention for } \theta_0,\kappa

\section{1. Fixed profile choice}

For the carrier block, freeze the defect profile to the standard localized even profile
\[
\boxed{
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa\xi).
}
\]

This is the profile already used in the explicit overlap and heavy-susceptibility derivations.

\section{2. Effective invariant}

Because the leading overlaps satisfy
\[
I_\theta\propto \theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\propto \theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
and more generally
\[
I_{2n+1}=O((\theta_0\kappa)^{2n+1}),
\qquad
J_{2n-1}=O((\theta_0\kappa)^{2n-1}),
\]
the natural carrier-side invariant is
\[
\boxed{
x:=\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

Thus the leading carrier audit should be organized in terms of \(x\), not \(\theta_0\) and \(\kappa\) separately.

\section{3. Width convention}

To eliminate one redundant degree of freedom, adopt the shell-matched width convention
\[
\boxed{
\kappa = q_0.
}
\]

This identifies the defect-width scale with the selected shell momentum scale.
It is not yet a theorem of TECT, but it is a legitimate frozen working convention for the carrier block.

Then
\[
\boxed{
\theta_0 = \frac{x}{q_0}.
}
\]

So every occurrence of \(\theta_0,\kappa\) is replaced by the single dimensionless carrier parameter \(x=\theta_0 q_0\).

\section{4. Immediate consequences}

Under \(\kappa=q_0\),
\[
\boxed{
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,x,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,x^3.
}
\]

Likewise,
\[
\boxed{
\|v_\parallel\|^2
=
\frac{4}{693}\lambda_c^2\,A_\perp\,q_0^7\,\theta_0^6
=
\frac{4}{693}\lambda_c^2\,A_\perp\,q_0\,x^6,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\chi_3^{(1)}
=
\frac{
\frac{4}{693}\lambda_c^2\,A_\perp\,q_0\,x^6
}{
M_H^2
+
Z\left(q_0^2+\frac{207}{65}q_0^2\right)
+
Y\left(q_0^4+\frac{414}{65}q_0^4+\frac{2529}{65}q_0^4\right)
}.
}
\]

Therefore the carrier-side \(N=1\) numerical test becomes a one-parameter problem in \(x=\theta_0 q_0\), once \(A_\perp,M_H^2,\lambda_c\) are fixed.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Immediate frozen execution}

\section{Current carrier status}

\[
\boxed{
\text{proof complete, certificate incomplete.}
}
\]

\section{Frozen audit order}

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}\to\text{Gate 2}\to\text{Gate 3}\to\text{Gate 4}.
}
\]

\section{Immediate next task}

The next nonredundant task is the Gate-1 finite audit:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

With the current benchmark decomposition,
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\]

Thus the only genuinely unresolved Gate-1 quantities are:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}+\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}+\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

Therefore the correct next move is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute the same-shell non-enriched slot first,}
}
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute the residual remote norm budget,}
}
\]
and only then stamp Gate 1 PASS/FAIL.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Gate 2 Practical Finish Sheet}

\section{Goal}

The remaining carrier question is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit finite audit of whether the primitive longitudinal channel survives:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
v_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{Shortest executable route}

Rather than separately re-running all four conceptual layers
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}\to c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\to J_\parallel^{(3)}\to C_c,
\]
the practical route is to use the already reduced projected-matrix extraction.

\section{Step 1: valley blocks}

Compute the two \(2\times2\) Hermitian valley blocks
\[
E_+(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_+ & c_+\\
\overline{c_+} & b_+
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
E_-(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
a_- & c_-\\
\overline{c_-} & b_-
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then
\[
\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}
=
\frac{a_\pm+b_\pm}{2}
-
\sqrt{\left(\frac{a_\pm-b_\pm}{2}\right)^2+|c_\pm|^2},
\]
and
\[
r_\pm=-\frac{c_\pm}{a_\pm-\varepsilon_\pm^{(\mathrm{low})}}.
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}
=
\frac{1-\overline{r_+}r_-}
{\sqrt{(1+|r_+|^2)(1+|r_-|^2)}}.
}
\]

\section{Step 2: shell-normal \(J\)-block}

Compute
\[
U_\parallel
=
\hat n^j\mathcal U_j(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u_{11} & u_{12}\\
u_{21} & u_{22}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
u_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\Sigma_3U_\parallel)
=
\frac12(u_{11}-u_{22}),
}
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel.
}
\]

\section{Step 3: direct survival test}

The practical sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|.
}
\]

In the ultra-minimal truncation \(R_N=0\),
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{00}\neq 0,
\qquad
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha_X\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}\neq 0
}
\]
is sufficient.

\section{What is actually still unknown}

Therefore the remaining carrier-side finite inputs are only
\[
\boxed{
a_\pm,\ b_\pm,\ c_\pm,\ u_{11},\ u_{22},\ m_\parallel.
}
\]

Once these are inserted, the practical longitudinal survival audit is finished.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Carrier Practical Finish}

Take the explicit longitudinal seed
\[
(B_\parallel)^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
(B_\parallel)^1_{ij}=(B_\parallel)^2_{ij}=0.
\]

With the shell covector
\[
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}=\hat n_i\hat n_j\delta_{a3},
\]
the longitudinal overlap is
\[
\ell_\parallel(B_\parallel)
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j(B_\parallel)^3_{ij}
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\hat n_i\hat n_j
=
1.
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
}
\]

Since
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
it follows that
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore the longitudinal primitive slot survives on the explicit Class II seed branch.
Combined with the already realized transverse channel, the carrier problem is solved at the practical branch level.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Frozen CKM Microscopic Backend: 14-Faced Cell + Solitonic Profile}

\section{1. Real-space primitive domain}

Let \(\Omega_{14}\) denote the truncated-octahedral Wigner--Seitz cell of the BCC condensate.
The BCC background is frozen as
\[
\phi_0(\mathbf x)=2A\sum_{a=1}^{6}\cos(\mathbf Q_a\cdot \mathbf x),
\]
so \(\Omega_{14}\) is the exact primitive integration domain for all projected microscopic matrix elements.

\section{2. Solitonic defect profile}

Replace ad hoc Gaussian or one-dimensional surrogate tails by the exact defect profile used in the microscopic TECT derivation:
\[
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)=-\theta_0\kappa\,\sech(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi).
\]

Hence the microscopic overlap kernels are generated by products of
\[
\sech(\kappa\xi),\qquad
\sech^2(\kappa\xi),\qquad
\sech^4(\kappa\xi),
\]
according to the channel.

\section{3. Exact polyhedral replacement}

For any microscopic operator \(\mathcal O_f\) entering the flavor reduction, define the exact BCC-adapted projected matrix element by
\[
\boxed{
[\mathcal O_f]_{GG'}
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega_{14}|}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
e^{-i(k_*+G)\cdot x}\,
\mathcal O_f[\phi_0,\theta](x)\,
e^{i(k_*+G')\cdot x}.
}
\]

This replaces the surrogate one-dimensional overlap integral
\[
\mathcal J_{\nu_f}(s_{AB})
\]
by an exact polyhedral cell integral.

\section{4. Microscopic family data from the same backend}

The finite intended-branch input tables are then computed from the same backend:
\[
S_{ab}=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\widetilde\psi_b\rangle_{\Omega_{14}},
\]
\[
M^{(f)}_{ab}
=
\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle_{\Omega_{14}},
\qquad
N^{(f)}_{ab}
=
\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal Y_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle_{\Omega_{14}}.
\]

Likewise, the off-diagonal links are no longer inserted through a reduced surrogate,
but through the exact polyhedral overlaps
\[
\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)},\qquad
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)},\qquad
r_{ij}^{(f)}
\]
computed on the same \(\Omega_{14}\)-based branch.

\section{5. Final exact / microscopic routes}

From the same backend one computes
\[
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2},
\qquad
\widehat Y^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}N^{(f)}S^{-1/2},
\]
hence
\[
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{1}{2\mathcal V_u\mathcal V_d}
\cdot
\frac{1}{3i}\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr),
\]
and in parallel
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr).
\]

The program is then closed only when the same intended branch satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\left|J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\right|\le E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\]

\section{Frozen Microscopic CKM Backend on the 14-Faced BCC Cell}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

From now on, the CKM block should no longer use Gaussian or one-dimensional surrogate overlaps as its defining backend.
The frozen backend is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{BCC 14-faced Wigner--Seitz cell } \Omega_{14}
\quad+\quad
\text{exact solitonic defect profile}
}
\]

All microscopic input tables
\[
S,\quad M^{(f)},\quad N^{(f)},\quad
\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)},\quad
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)},\quad
r_{ij}^{(f)}
\]
must be recomputed from this same backend.

\section{1. Frozen background}

Freeze the real-space condensate background to the equal-amplitude BCC shell:
\[
\boxed{
\phi_0(\mathbf x)=2A\sum_{a=1}^{6}\cos(\mathbf Q_a\cdot\mathbf x),
}
\]
with primitive real-space cell
\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{14}=\text{truncated-octahedral Wigner--Seitz cell of the BCC condensate}.
}
\]

The reciprocal-shell vectors are
\[
\mathbf Q_1=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0),\quad
\mathbf Q_2=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,-1,0),\quad
\mathbf Q_3=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,0,1),
\]
\[
\mathbf Q_4=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,0,-1),\quad
\mathbf Q_5=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(0,1,1),\quad
\mathbf Q_6=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(0,1,-1).
\]

\section{2. Frozen solitonic profile}

Freeze the defect profile to the exact localized solitonic form
\[
\boxed{
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa \xi),
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)=-\theta_0\kappa\,\sech(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi).
}
\]

Thus all channel-dependent microscopic kernels are generated from products of
\[
\sech(\kappa\xi),\qquad
\sech^2(\kappa\xi),\qquad
\sech^4(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(\xi),\qquad
\theta'(\xi)^2,
\]
rather than from Gaussian proxy tails.

\section{3. Exact 14-faced projected matrix elements}

For any microscopic operator \(\mathcal O_f[\phi_0,\theta]\) entering the flavor reduction, define the exact BCC-adapted cell matrix element by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[\mathcal O_f]_{GG'}
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega_{14}|}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
e^{-i(k_*+G)\cdot x}\,
\mathcal O_f[\phi_0,\theta](x)\,
e^{i(k_*+G')\cdot x}.
}
\label{eq:Omega14_operator_matrix}
\end{equation}

This replaces all spherical-cutoff and one-dimensional surrogate backends.

\section{4. Family-space overlap, kinetic, and Yukawa tables}

Let \(\{\phi_A\}_{A=1}^3\) be the common left-handed family basis on the intended branch.
Define the primitive overlap Gram matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{AB}
:=
\langle \phi_A,\phi_B\rangle_{\Omega_{14}}
=
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
\overline{\phi_A(x)}\,\phi_B(x).
}
\label{eq:Omega14_S}
\end{equation}

Define the kinetic and reduced family operator tables by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(f)}_{AB}
:=
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle_{\Omega_{14}},
\qquad
N^{(f)}_{AB}
:=
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal Y_f\phi_B\rangle_{\Omega_{14}}.
}
\label{eq:Omega14_MN}
\end{equation}

Then the canonically normalized family operators are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2},
\qquad
\widehat Y^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}N^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
}
\label{eq:Omega14_ZYhat}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Exact CKM route from the same frozen backend}

Once \(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d\) are constructed from \eqref{eq:Omega14_ZYhat}, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{1}{3i}\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal V_u=\prod_{i<j}(y_i^{(u)}-y_j^{(u)}),
\qquad
\mathcal V_d=\prod_{i<j}(y_i^{(d)}-y_j^{(d)}),
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}}{2\mathcal V_u\mathcal V_d}.
}
\label{eq:Omega14_Jexact}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Microscopic link route with polyhedral solitonic kernels}

The former one-dimensional kink overlap
\[
\mathcal J_{\nu_f}(s_{AB})
\]
is now replaced by an exact channel-dependent polyhedral integral on \(\Omega_{14}\).

For each ordered pair \((A,B)\), define the channel kernel
\[
\mathcal T_{AB}^{(f)}(x)
\]
from the appropriate solitonic tensor built out of \(\theta,\theta',\phi_0\).
Then the exact microscopic off-diagonal links are frozen as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{AB}^{(f)}
=
\mathcal C_{AB}^{(f)}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
\overline{\phi_A(x)}\,
\mathcal T_{AB}^{(f)}(x)\,
\phi_B(x).
}
\label{eq:Omega14_Lambda}
\end{equation}

Likewise the diagonal seed/gap data are frozen as cell integrals of the diagonal \(OO\)-sector moments:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\bigl(N^{(f)}_{jj}-N^{(f)}_{ii}\bigr)
+
\Delta_{ij,\mathrm{res}}^{(f)},
}
\label{eq:Omega14_Delta}
\end{equation}
and the residual normalized links are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\frac{\Lambda_{ij,\mathrm{res}}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
}
\label{eq:Omega14_r}
\end{equation}

Define the normalized microscopic links
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\frac{\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}+r_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}},
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{ij}=L_{ij}^{(d)}-L_{ij}^{(u)}.
}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\frac12L_{12}^{(d)}L_{23}^{(d)}
+\frac12L_{12}^{(u)}L_{23}^{(u)}
-
L_{12}^{(u)}L_{23}^{(d)},
}
\end{equation}
and the microscopic CP core becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:Omega14_Ximic}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Exact/microscopic consistency test}

The CKM block is considered numerically closed only when the same intended branch satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\right|\le E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\label{eq:Omega14_consistency}
\end{equation}

Thus the 14-faced-cell + solitonic backend is not merely a heuristic refinement.
It is the common frozen backend for both the exact route \eqref{eq:Omega14_Jexact} and the microscopic route \eqref{eq:Omega14_Ximic}.

\section{8. What changes operationally}

From this point on, the CKM block does \emph{not} use:
\[
\text{Gaussian basis branch as defining backend,}
\qquad
\text{1D surrogate }\mathcal J_\nu(s)\text{ as final backend.}
\]

Instead, all numbers must be extracted from the same frozen primitive-cell geometry:
\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{14}
\quad+\quad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\sech(\kappa\xi).
}
\]

This makes the CKM numerical program backend-stable:
once \(S,M,N,\Lambda,\Delta,r\) are computed on the intended branch, no later reinterpretation of the integration geometry is allowed.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact \texorpdfstring{$\Omega_{14}$}{Omega14} Backend for }S,\ M^{(f)},\ N^{(f)},\ \Lambda^{(f)},\ \Delta^{(f)},\ r^{(f)}

\section{Short explanation}

The correct way to avoid repeated re-computation is not to perform new raw integrals for every matrix element.
Instead, we freeze a single primitive-cell backend on the BCC truncated-octahedral cell \(\Omega_{14}\), compute its Fourier kernel tables once, and generate all microscopic CKM inputs from the same tables.

\section{1. Frozen BCC primitive-cell background}

Fix the BCC shell condensate
\[
\boxed{
\phi_0(\mathbf x)=2A\sum_{a=1}^{6}\cos(\mathbf Q_a\cdot\mathbf x),
}
\]
with reciprocal shell
\[
\mathbf Q_1=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0),\quad
\mathbf Q_2=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,-1,0),\quad
\mathbf Q_3=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,0,1),
\]
\[
\mathbf Q_4=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,0,-1),\quad
\mathbf Q_5=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(0,1,1),\quad
\mathbf Q_6=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(0,1,-1),
\]
and let \(\Omega_{14}\) be the corresponding truncated-octahedral Wigner--Seitz cell.

Fix the exact defect profile
\[
\boxed{
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\sech(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)=-\theta_0\kappa\,\sech(\kappa\xi)\tanh(\kappa\xi).
}
\]

\section{2. Bloch-harmonic family basis}

Let the intended-branch family states be expanded in a frozen shell/Bloch basis:
\[
\boxed{
\phi_A(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal S_N} c_{A,G}\,e^{i(k_*+G)\cdot x},
\qquad A=1,2,3.
}
\]

All microscopic operators entering the flavor problem are expanded in reciprocal harmonics:
\[
\mathcal K_f(x)=\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\widehat{\mathcal K}_f(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\mathcal Y_f(x)=\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\widehat{\mathcal Y}_f(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x},
\]
and likewise for each channel kernel
\[
\mathcal T_{AB}^{(f)}(x)=\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\widehat{\mathcal T}_{AB}^{(f)}(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\]

\section{3. Primitive-cell orthogonality}

Because \(\Omega_{14}\) is the primitive cell of the frozen BCC branch,
\[
\boxed{
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;e^{iK\cdot x}
=
|\Omega_{14}|\,\delta_{K,0},
\qquad K\in\Lambda^*.
}
\]

Therefore all projected matrix elements collapse to discrete convolution sums.
This is the key reason the 14-faced backend is computationally stable.

\section{4. Exact overlap Gram matrix}

The overlap matrix is
\[
S_{AB}
=
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
\overline{\phi_A(x)}\,\phi_B(x).
\]

Substituting the Bloch expansions and using primitive-cell orthogonality,
\[
\boxed{
S_{AB}
=
|\Omega_{14}|
\sum_{G\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{A,G}}\,c_{B,G}.
}
\]

So \(S\) is obtained from the family Bloch coefficients alone.

\section{5. Exact kinetic and Yukawa family tables}

For the kinetic family operator,
\[
M^{(f)}_{AB}
=
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
\overline{\phi_A(x)}\,\mathcal K_f(x)\,\phi_B(x).
\]

Expanding \(\mathcal K_f\) and using primitive-cell orthogonality gives
\[
\boxed{
M^{(f)}_{AB}
=
|\Omega_{14}|
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{A,G}}\,c_{B,G'}\,
\widehat{\mathcal K}_f(G-G').
}
\]

Likewise,
\[
N^{(f)}_{AB}
=
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
\overline{\phi_A(x)}\,\mathcal Y_f(x)\,\phi_B(x),
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
N^{(f)}_{AB}
=
|\Omega_{14}|
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{A,G}}\,c_{B,G'}\,
\widehat{\mathcal Y}_f(G-G').
}
\]

\section{6. Exact microscopic off-diagonal links}

Replace the former one-dimensional surrogate overlap by the exact polyhedral channel integral
\[
\Lambda_{AB}^{(f)}
=
\mathcal C_{AB}^{(f)}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
\overline{\phi_A(x)}\,\mathcal T_{AB}^{(f)}(x)\,\phi_B(x).
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{AB}^{(f)}
=
\mathcal C_{AB}^{(f)}\,|\Omega_{14}|
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{A,G}}\,c_{B,G'}\,
\widehat{\mathcal T}_{AB}^{(f)}(G-G').
}
\]

This is the exact 14-faced-cell replacement of the former reduced overlap factor \(\mathcal J_{\nu_f}(s_{AB})\).

\section{7. Gap and residual link data}

Once \(N^{(f)}\) and \(\Lambda^{(f)}\) are known, define
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\bigl(N^{(f)}_{jj}-N^{(f)}_{ii}\bigr)+\Delta_{ij,\mathrm{res}}^{(f)},
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
r_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\frac{\Lambda_{ij,\mathrm{res}}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
}
\]

Then the normalized microscopic links are
\[
\boxed{
L_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\frac{\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}+r_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
}
\]

\section{8. Exact and microscopic CKM routes from one backend}

The canonically normalized family operators are
\[
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2},
\qquad
\widehat Y^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}N^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
}
\]

From these one computes
\[
\boxed{
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{1}{2\mathcal V_u\mathcal V_d}
\cdot
\frac{1}{3i}\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr).
}
\]

In parallel, define
\[
S_{ij}=L_{ij}^{(d)}-L_{ij}^{(u)},
\]
\[
C_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\frac12L_{12}^{(d)}L_{23}^{(d)}
+\frac12L_{12}^{(u)}L_{23}^{(u)}
-
L_{12}^{(u)}L_{23}^{(d)},
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr).
}
\]

The backend is numerically closed only if the same intended branch satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\left|J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\right|\le E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\]

\section{9. Operational consequence}

After freezing the 14-faced BCC cell and the solitonic profile, all CKM microscopic data are generated from the three Fourier kernel tables
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal K}_f(Q),\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal Y}_f(Q),\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal T}_{AB}^{(f)}(Q),
}
\]
together with the family Bloch coefficients
\[
\boxed{
c_{A,G}.
}
\]

So the repeated recomputation problem disappears:
one backend table, many projected outputs.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{CKM Microscopic Backend Freeze on the 14-Faced BCC Cell}

\section{Current Stage}

The CKM block is now frozen to the following microscopic backend:
\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{14}\ \text{(truncated-octahedral BCC Wigner--Seitz cell)}
\quad+\quad
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa \xi).
}
\]

This means that the previous Gaussian or one-dimensional surrogate overlap backend is no longer used as the defining microscopic engine.
From this point on, all intended-branch CKM quantities must be computed from the same primitive-cell polyhedral backend.

\section{Frozen BCC Background}

The frozen equal-amplitude BCC shell condensate is
\[
\phi_0(\mathbf x)=2A\sum_{a=1}^{6}\cos(\mathbf Q_a\cdot \mathbf x),
\]
with reciprocal-shell vectors
\[
\mathbf Q_1=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0),\quad
\mathbf Q_2=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,-1,0),\quad
\mathbf Q_3=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,0,1),
\]
\[
\mathbf Q_4=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(1,0,-1),\quad
\mathbf Q_5=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(0,1,1),\quad
\mathbf Q_6=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}(0,1,-1).
\]

The real-space primitive cell is the truncated octahedron
\[
\Omega_{14}.
\]

\section{Frozen Solitonic Profile}

The defect profile is frozen to
\[
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\,\sech(\kappa \xi),
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)=-\theta_0\kappa\,\sech(\kappa \xi)\tanh(\kappa \xi).
\]

Hence all microscopic kernels are generated from the solitonic tensor family
\[
\sech(\kappa\xi),\qquad
\sech^2(\kappa\xi),\qquad
\sech^4(\kappa\xi),\qquad
\theta'(\xi),\qquad
\theta'(\xi)^2,
\]
rather than from Gaussian proxy tails.

\section{Primitive-Cell Harmonic Backend}

Let the intended-branch family states be expanded as
\[
\phi_A(x)=\sum_{G\in\mathcal S_N} c_{A,G}\,e^{i(k_*+G)\cdot x},
\qquad A=1,2,3.
\]

For any microscopic operator \(\mathcal O_f(x)\), define the primitive-cell harmonic matrix element
\[
[\mathcal O_f]_{GG'}
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega_{14}|}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
e^{-i(k_*+G)\cdot x}\,
\mathcal O_f(x)\,
e^{i(k_*+G')\cdot x}.
\]

Because \(\Omega_{14}\) is the primitive BCC cell,
\[
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;e^{iK\cdot x}
=
|\Omega_{14}|\,\delta_{K,0},
\]
so all projected matrix elements reduce to discrete convolution sums.

\section{Exact Family Tables}

The overlap Gram matrix becomes
\[
\boxed{
S_{AB}
=
|\Omega_{14}|
\sum_{G\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{A,G}}\,c_{B,G}.
}
\]

The kinetic and Yukawa family tables are
\[
\boxed{
M^{(f)}_{AB}
=
|\Omega_{14}|
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{A,G}}\,c_{B,G'}\,
\widehat{\mathcal K}_f(G-G'),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
N^{(f)}_{AB}
=
|\Omega_{14}|
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{A,G}}\,c_{B,G'}\,
\widehat{\mathcal Y}_f(G-G').
}
\]

The canonically normalized family operators are then
\[
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2},
\qquad
\widehat Y^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}N^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
}
\]

\section{Exact CKM Route}

From the normalized Yukawa operators, define
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{1}{3i}\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr),
\]
\[
\mathcal V_u=\prod_{i<j}(y_i^{(u)}-y_j^{(u)}),
\qquad
\mathcal V_d=\prod_{i<j}(y_i^{(d)}-y_j^{(d)}),
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}}{2\mathcal V_u\mathcal V_d}.
}
\]

\section{Microscopic Link Route}

For each ordered pair \((A,B)\), replace the old one-dimensional overlap by the exact polyhedral channel kernel
\[
\mathcal T_{AB}^{(f)}(x)
=
\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\widehat{\mathcal T}_{AB}^{(f)}(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\]

Then the off-diagonal microscopic links are
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_{AB}^{(f)}
=
\mathcal C_{AB}^{(f)}\,|\Omega_{14}|
\sum_{G,G'\in\mathcal S_N}
\overline{c_{A,G}}\,c_{B,G'}\,
\widehat{\mathcal T}_{AB}^{(f)}(G-G').
}
\]

Next define
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\bigl(N_{jj}^{(f)}-N_{ii}^{(f)}\bigr)
+
\Delta_{ij,\mathrm{res}}^{(f)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
r_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\frac{\Lambda_{ij,\mathrm{res}}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}},
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
L_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\frac{\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}+r_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
}
\]

From these,
\[
S_{ij}=L_{ij}^{(d)}-L_{ij}^{(u)},
\]
\[
C_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\frac12L_{12}^{(d)}L_{23}^{(d)}
+\frac12L_{12}^{(u)}L_{23}^{(u)}
-
L_{12}^{(u)}L_{23}^{(d)},
\]
and finally
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr).
}
\]

\section{Backend-Stable Consistency Target}

The CKM block is numerically closed only when the same intended branch satisfies
\[
\boxed{
\left|J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\right|\le E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\]

This is now the unique backend-stable target.
No later reinterpretation of the integration geometry is allowed.

\section{What Was Actually Implemented}

A primitive-cell convolution engine was implemented for:
\[
S_{AB},\quad M^{(f)}_{AB},\quad N^{(f)}_{AB},
\]
and extended to the microscopic link route
\[
\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)},\quad
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)},\quad
r_{ij}^{(f)},\quad
L_{ij}^{(f)},\quad
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}.
\]

In the backend sanity demo:
\[
N(G_*)=4
\quad\text{for }G_*=(1,1,0),
\]
which matches the exact BCC first-shell pair-counting fact.

The toy run produced a nontrivial \(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d\), and both the exact route and microscopic route executed without backend ambiguity.
The mismatch between \(J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}\) and \(\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\) in that demo is not a failure of the backend.
It simply reflects that the inserted kernels were toy data, not the actual intended-branch microscopic kernels.

\section{What Remains}

The backend engine is now complete.
The remaining frontier is no longer geometric.
It is the actual intended-branch insertion of
\[
\boxed{

\widehat{\mathcal K}_f(Q),\qquad

Once those are supplied from the frozen \(\Omega_{14}\)+soliton branch, the CKM exact route and microscopic route can be compared on the same intended branch without any further backend revision.

\section{Final Summary}

The CKM microscopic backend is now frozen to
\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{14}\text{ (BCC truncated-octahedral primitive cell)}
\quad+\quad

A single primitive-cell convolution engine has been implemented to compute

S_{AB},\quad M^{(f)}_{AB},\quad N^{(f)}_{AB},

Thus the repeated re-derivation problem is removed:
one frozen backend, many projected outputs.

The exact route

\section{Polyhedral-Soliton Channel Kernel on the 14-Faced BCC Cell}

\section{Short explanation}

The CKM microscopic backend is now advanced one real step beyond the toy-kernel stage.

Instead of inserting arbitrary complex numbers for the channel kernels
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T}_{AB}^{(f)}(Q),
\]
we directly computed a frozen prototype table from the exact 14-faced BCC primitive cell \(\Omega_{14}\) and a solitonic overlap tensor.

The computed kernel is
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal T}(Q)
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega_{14}|}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;

\sech^\nu(\kappa(\xi+s/2)),

with
\[

This is not yet the final intended-branch family-dependent kernel,
but it is the first non-arbitrary \(\Omega_{14}\)+soliton table that can replace the old toy complex kernel insertions.

\section{1. Frozen geometric cell}

We used the exact truncated-octahedral BCC primitive cell in normalized coordinates
\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{14}
=
\left\{
(x,y,z)\in\mathbb R^3:
|x|\le 1,\quad |y|\le 1,\quad |z|\le 1,\quad
|x|+|y|+|z|\le \frac32
\right\}.
}
\]

Its exact volume is
\[
\boxed{
|\Omega_{14}|=4.
}
\]

A direct grid integration with \(161^3\) points gave
\[
|\Omega_{14}|_{\mathrm{num}}=4.03182031,
\]
so the relative geometric discretization error is
\[
\boxed{
\frac{|\,|\Omega_{14}|_{\mathrm{num}}-4\,|}{4}
\approx 7.955\times 10^{-3}.
}
\]

\section{2. Frozen prototype solitonic tensor}

This is the natural polyhedral replacement of the former one-dimensional surrogate overlap factor.

This yields the first non-arbitrary microscopic CP seed on the frozen CKM backend.

\section{1. Frozen exact route}

\section{2. Automatic support extraction}

Thus the channel supports are no longer chosen by hand.

\section{2. What the notes still do not provide}

The notes explicitly say that the following remain conditional:

\item the intended-branch numerical values of the family matrices;
\item the intended-branch blockwise coefficients
\[
\Lambda_{ij}^{(u,d)},\qquad
\Delta_{ij}^{(u,d)},\qquad

\]
\item the genuinely irreducible internal phase source inside
\[
\mathcal C_{AB}^{(f)}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Hence the actual intended branch is not yet fully numerically executed.

This means that one may not yet claim to have extracted the final physical branch rules for all microscopic flavor coefficients from the uploaded notes alone.

\section{3. Correct interpretation of the recent automatic-support run}

In the recent \(\Omega_{14}\)+soliton microscopic run, the support sets were extracted automatically from the family shell basis:

\mathrm{Supp}_{AB}
=

No extra ad hoc toy phase was inserted by hand.

is the first non-arbitrary microscopic CP seed produced on the frozen backend.

This is a real result.
But it is still a prototype result, not yet the fully executed intended branch.

\section{Is the current branch already an actual solution of the nonlinear PDE?}

\section{Short answer}

\[
\boxed{
\text{No, not yet in the strict sense.}
}
\]

What we currently have is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the strongest explicit working microscopic branch}
}
\end{equation}

rather than

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{a fully verified actual nonlinear solution }
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)
\text{ of the complete microscopic TECT PDE.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{1. What is already true}

The reduced infrared Dirac-type PDE form is already fixed:
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\]

Inside the strongest explicit currently available microscopic realization, namely the refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, one may concretely push the full-PDE derivation program.

Thus the project has already reached:

\[
\boxed{
\text{reduced PDE form: closed,}
\qquad
\text{working microscopic branch: explicit.}
}
\]

\section{2. What is \emph{not} yet true}

The notes explicitly state that the full complete microscopic TECT action is not yet fully derived unconditionally.

Equivalently, the actual full microscopic coefficient point
\[
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\]
or
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
has not yet been extracted from the full background-dependent TECT Hessian.

Therefore one may not yet say that the current branch is already the actual final nonlinear PDE branch.

\section{3. The decisive obstruction}

For the actual-branch quantities relevant to the CKM / anisotropy program, the notes state:
\[
W_2=\mathcal F_1[\Psi],\qquad
m_*^2=\mathcal F_2[\Psi],\qquad
g_{\rm eff}=\mathcal F_3[\Psi].
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
(W_2,m_*,g_{\rm eff})
\text{ cannot be computed without }
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x).
}
\]

The notes then explicitly diagnose the situation as:
\[
\boxed{
\text{PDE ✔,\quad functional formulas ✔,\quad numerical scheme ✔,\quad but NOT }\Psi_{\rm actual}(x).
}
\]

So the current obstruction is not algebraic.
It is dynamical:
the actual nonlinear solution itself has not yet been obtained.

\section{4. Correct honest status}

Therefore the correct statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current branch is an explicit working branch / ansatz compatible with the closed constraints,}
}
\]
but not yet

\[
\boxed{
\text{a fully verified actual nonlinear solution of the complete microscopic PDE.}
}
\]

In the language of the notes, this is a strong conditional-closure stage, not yet a final unconditional-complete stage.

\section{5. What would be needed to say “yes”}

To legitimately say that the branch is the actual nonlinear PDE solution, one would need:

\begin{enumerate}
\item solve or numerically construct \(\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)\) from the nonlinear microscopic PDE;
\item verify that the resulting background actually realizes the intended BCC / defect branch;
\item linearize about that solution and construct the periodic Bloch fiber;
\item extract the projected derivative data
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\to H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\to P_*K_iP_*\to (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta);
\]
\item evaluate the actual branch functionals such as \(W_2,m_*,g_{\rm eff}\) on that same solution.
\end{enumerate}

Only after this chain is completed can one promote the current working branch to an actual nonlinear-PDE solution branch.

\section{Final Summary}

The current branch is not yet justified as an actual nonlinear solution of the complete microscopic TECT PDE.

What is already established is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the reduced infrared PDE form is closed,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the refined locked + Class II branch is the strongest explicit working microscopic branch,}
}
\]

but what is still missing is:

\[
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x),
}
\]
namely an actual nonlinear solution of the full microscopic PDE on the intended branch.

Therefore the honest current statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{working branch / ansatz: yes,}
\qquad
\text{actual nonlinear PDE solution: not yet.}
}
\]

The remaining obstruction is dynamical, not conceptual:
the project still needs the actual nonlinear branch solution and the corresponding projected Hessian/Bloch extraction on that same solution.

\section{Actual Nonlinear PDE \(\to\) 12-Patch Shell System \(\to\) 3-Orbit Reduction}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The honest next step is not another abstract theorem and not another scalar-shell rerun.

Starting from the full Class II nonlinear PDE, the correct executable reduction is:

\[
(\Psi, X_i^{\,a})
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\mathcal F_{\rm shell}[A_1,\dots,A_{12}]
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\partial_t A_\alpha
=
-\frac{\partial \mathcal F_{\rm shell}}{\partial \overline{A_\alpha}}.
\]

For a locking axis aligned with one BCC shell direction, the 12 patches split exactly into three symmetry orbits:

\[
\boxed{
\text{axial }(2),\qquad
\text{equatorial }(2),\qquad
\text{oblique }(8).
}
\]

This gives the first exact reduced dynamical system that can actually decide whether the intended BCC branch survives or collapses.

\section{1. Full shell-amplitude system already derived in Math29}

The full Class II shell ansatz is
\[
\boxed{
\Psi(x,t)=\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}A_\alpha(t)e^{iq_0\hat k_\alpha\cdot x},
}
\]
with
\[
\hat k_\alpha\in
\left\{
\frac{(\pm1,\pm1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(\pm1,0,\pm1)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(0,\pm1,\pm1)}{\sqrt2}
\right\}.
\]

The patchwise shell couplings induced by the Class II tensor are
\[
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,3}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}q_0^2 A\,c_\alpha^2,
\]
\[
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,1}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}q_0^2 c_\alpha(Bt_{\alpha1}-Ct_{\alpha2}),
\]
\[
\Gamma_\alpha^{\,2}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}q_0^2 c_\alpha(Bt_{\alpha2}+Ct_{\alpha1}),
\]
where
\[
c_\alpha=\hat n\cdot\hat k_\alpha,
\qquad
t_{\alpha1}=e_1\cdot\hat k_\alpha,
\qquad
t_{\alpha2}=e_2\cdot\hat k_\alpha.
\]

The induced quartic matrix is
\[
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}
=
-\Lambda_A c_\alpha^2c_\beta^2
-
\Lambda_{BC}c_\alpha c_\beta
\Bigl(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta-c_\alpha c_\beta\Bigr),
}
\]
with
\[
\Lambda_A
=
\chi_3\left(\frac{\lambda g_Xq_0^2}{M_X^2}\right)^2A^2,
\qquad
\Lambda_{BC}
=
\chi_\perp\left(\frac{\lambda g_Xq_0^2}{M_X^2}\right)^2(B^2+C^2).
\]

The shell free energy is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm shell}[A]
=
-\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}\sigma_\alpha r_\alpha
+
\frac12\sum_{\alpha,\beta=1}^{12}U_{\alpha\beta}r_\alpha r_\beta,
\qquad
r_\alpha:=|A_\alpha|^2,
}
\]
and the gradient flow is
\[
\boxed{
\partial_t A_\alpha
=
\left(
\sigma_\alpha-\sum_{\beta=1}^{12}U_{\alpha\beta}r_\beta
\right)A_\alpha.
}
\]

This part is already structurally derived in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

\section{2. Choose the locking axis and compute the exact BCC orbit geometry}

Take the anisotropy axis to be aligned with one BCC shell direction:
\[
\hat n=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
e_1=\frac{(1,-1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
e_2=(0,0,1).
\]

Then the 12 BCC shell directions split as follows.

\paragraph{Axial orbit \(\mathcal A\) (2 patches).}
\[
\hat k=\pm\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2}.
\]
For these,
\[
c_\alpha=\pm1,\qquad t_{\alpha1}=0,\qquad t_{\alpha2}=0.
\]

\paragraph{Equatorial orbit \(\mathcal E\) (2 patches).}
\[
\hat k=\pm\frac{(1,-1,0)}{\sqrt2}.
\]
For these,
\[
c_\alpha=0,\qquad t_{\alpha1}=\pm1,\qquad t_{\alpha2}=0.
\]

\paragraph{Oblique orbit \(\mathcal O\) (8 patches).}
\[
\hat k\in
\left\{
\frac{(\pm1,0,\pm1)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(0,\pm1,\pm1)}{\sqrt2}
\right\}.
\]
For these,
\[
c_\alpha=\pm\frac12,
\qquad
t_{\alpha1}=\pm\frac12,
\qquad
t_{\alpha2}=\pm\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
\]

Hence the exact orbit values are
\[
\boxed{
c^2=
\begin{cases}
1 & \alpha\in\mathcal A,\\[4pt]
0 & \alpha\in\mathcal E,\\[4pt]
\frac14 & \alpha\in\mathcal O.
\end{cases}
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
P_2(c_\alpha)=
\begin{cases}
1 & \alpha\in\mathcal A,\\[4pt]
-\frac12 & \alpha\in\mathcal E,\\[4pt]
-\frac18 & \alpha\in\mathcal O.
\end{cases}
}
\]

So the 12-patch system reduces exactly to a \(2+2+8\) orbit decomposition.

\section{3. Exact linear growth rates by orbit}

Assume the symmetric transverse background
\[
\overline s_1=\overline s_2=0,
\qquad
\overline s_3=:s_3.
\]

Then only the \(b=3\) channel contributes at linear order, so
\[
\delta\sigma_\alpha=\overline s_3\,\Gamma_\alpha^{\,3}
=
-\overline s_3\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}q_0^2A\,c_\alpha^2.
\]

Introduce
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\sigma
:=
\overline s_3\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}q_0^2A.
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_\alpha
=
\sigma_0+\eta P_2(c_\alpha)-\Lambda_\sigma c_\alpha^2.
}
\]

Therefore the exact orbitwise growth rates are

\[
\boxed{
\sigma_A=\sigma_0+\eta-\Lambda_\sigma,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_E=\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_O=\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{8}-\frac{\Lambda_\sigma}{4}.
}
\]

So already at linear level the full PDE distinguishes the three BCC orbit classes.

\section{4. Exact orbitwise quartic sums from the \(X\)-sector}

Now impose the orbit-symmetric intensity ansatz
\[
r_\alpha=
\begin{cases}
r_A & \alpha\in\mathcal A,\\
r_E & \alpha\in\mathcal E,\\
r_O & \alpha\in\mathcal O.
\end{cases}
\]

The crucial exact computation is that, for this orbit-symmetric reduction,
the \(\Lambda_{BC}\)-term cancels in the row sums.
Only the axial quartic scale \(\Lambda_A\) survives.

Indeed, for a representative axial patch \(\alpha\in\mathcal A\),
\[
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal A}U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}=-2\Lambda_A,
\qquad
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal E}U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}=0,
\qquad
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal O}U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}=-2\Lambda_A.
\]

For a representative equatorial patch \(\alpha\in\mathcal E\),
\[
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal A}U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}
=
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal E}U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}
=
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal O}U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}
=0.
\]

For a representative oblique patch \(\alpha\in\mathcal O\),
\[
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal A}U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}=-\frac{\Lambda_A}{2},
\qquad
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal E}U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}=0,
\qquad
\sum_{\beta\in\mathcal O}U_{\alpha\beta}^{(X)}=-\frac{\Lambda_A}{2}.
\]

Therefore the class-symmetric shell sums are
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_A^{(X)}=-2\Lambda_A(r_A+r_O),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_E^{(X)}=0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_O^{(X)}=-\frac{\Lambda_A}{2}(r_A+r_O).
}
\]

This is a new exact reduction:
at class-symmetric level, the transverse quartic scale \(\Lambda_{BC}\) drops out of the row sums identically.

\section{5. Reduced \(2+2+8\) shell-amplitude dynamics}

Let the isotropic scalar-shell quartic background be approximated by
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(0)}=u_0\delta_{\alpha\beta}+v_0.
\]

Then, with
\[
R_{\rm tot}=2r_A+2r_E+8r_O,
\]
the orbitwise gradient-flow equations become

\[
\boxed{
\partial_t A_A
=
\Bigl[
\sigma_A-u_0r_A-v_0R_{\rm tot}
+2\Lambda_A(r_A+r_O)
\Bigr]A_A,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\partial_t A_E
=
\Bigl[
\sigma_E-u_0r_E-v_0R_{\rm tot}
\Bigr]A_E,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\partial_t A_O
=
\Bigl[
\sigma_O-u_0r_O-v_0R_{\rm tot}
+\frac{\Lambda_A}{2}(r_A+r_O)
\Bigr]A_O.
}
\]

Equivalently, in intensity form,
\[
\dot r_A
=
2\Bigl[
\sigma_A-u_0r_A-v_0R_{\rm tot}
+2\Lambda_A(r_A+r_O)
\Bigr]r_A,
\]
\[
\dot r_E
=
2\Bigl[
\sigma_E-u_0r_E-v_0R_{\rm tot}
\Bigr]r_E,
\]
\[
\dot r_O
=
2\Bigl[
\sigma_O-u_0r_O-v_0R_{\rm tot}
+\frac{\Lambda_A}{2}(r_A+r_O)
\Bigr]r_O.
\]

This is the first exact reduced nonlinear dynamical system obtained directly from the full Class II shell-amplitude PDE.

\section{6. Consequence}

The actual branch question is no longer:
\[
\text{``does some abstract BCC branch exist?''}
\]
It is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{for the reduced }(r_A,r_E,r_O)\text{ system above, does there exist a stable fixed point with }r_O>0
\text{ and not only }r_A>0?
}
\]

That is the actual nonlinear branch decision problem inherited from the full PDE.

Moreover, because \(\Sigma_E^{(X)}=0\) and \(\Sigma_A^{(X)},\Sigma_O^{(X)}\) depend only on \(\Lambda_A\),
the leading orbit-symmetric stabilization problem is controlled by a very small parameter set:
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_0,\ \eta,\ \Lambda_\sigma,\ u_0,\ v_0,\ \Lambda_A.
}
\]

So the enormous full PDE problem is now reduced to a six-parameter nonlinear orbit system.

\section{Final Summary}

Starting from the full Class II shell-amplitude system already derived in Math29, and aligning the anisotropy axis with one BCC shell direction,
the 12 BCC patches split exactly into three symmetry orbits:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal A\ (2\ \text{axial}),\qquad
\mathcal E\ (2\ \text{equatorial}),\qquad
\mathcal O\ (8\ \text{oblique}).
}
\]

The corresponding exact orbitwise linear growth rates are
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_A=\sigma_0+\eta-\Lambda_\sigma,
\qquad
\sigma_E=\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{2},
\qquad
\sigma_O=\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{8}-\frac{\Lambda_\sigma}{4}.
}
\]

For the Class II quartic matrix, the orbit-symmetric row sums simplify dramatically:
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_A^{(X)}=-2\Lambda_A(r_A+r_O),\qquad
\Sigma_E^{(X)}=0,\qquad
\Sigma_O^{(X)}=-\frac{\Lambda_A}{2}(r_A+r_O).
}
\]

Thus the actual nonlinear branch problem reduces to the exact \(2+2+8\) orbit system
for \((r_A,r_E,r_O)\), and the leading orbit-symmetric stabilization problem depends only on
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_0,\ \eta,\ \Lambda_\sigma,\ u_0,\ v_0,\ \Lambda_A.
}
\]

Therefore the honest next step is no longer an abstract PDE discussion.
It is the nonlinear fixed-point and stability analysis of this six-parameter reduced orbit system.

\section{Derivation of Effective PDE Coefficients from the BCC Discrete Geometry}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The geometric idea is strong, but it must be written with one crucial correction and one explicit assumption.

The correction is that the standard second-order Taylor expansion gives
\[
\sum_{\delta}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
N\Phi+\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4),
\]
not
\[
N\Phi+2\nabla^2\Phi.
\]

The explicit assumption is that the linear local mass is tuned to one half of the total neighbor coupling, which is a BPS-like self-tuning hypothesis rather than a theorem of the BCC geometry alone.

Under those two ingredients, the coefficient set
\[
\alpha=\frac73,\qquad
\beta=\frac{25}{3},\qquad
c=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}},\qquad
w=\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}
\]
does follow cleanly.

\section{1. Discrete BCC shell sets}

Set the cubic lattice constant to \(a=1\).
Use the two geometrically distinguished neighbor shells:

\paragraph{Nearest BCC shell (8 vectors).}
\[
\Delta_1
=
\left\{
\left(\pm\frac12,\pm\frac12,\pm\frac12\right)
\right\}.
\]

\paragraph{Next shell (6 vectors).}
\[
\Delta_2
=
\{(\pm1,0,0),(0,\pm1,0),(0,0,\pm1)\}.
\]

Let the scalar order parameter be \(\Phi(\mathbf r)\).

\section{2. Second-order Taylor expansion}

For any symmetric shell \(\Delta\) with \(\delta\in\Delta \Rightarrow -\delta\in\Delta\),
\[
\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
\Phi(\mathbf r)
+
\delta_i\partial_i\Phi
+
\frac12\delta_i\delta_j\partial_i\partial_j\Phi
+
O(\partial^3).
\]

Summing over the shell and using inversion symmetry,
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta}\delta_i=0,
\]
so the odd term vanishes. Hence
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
|\Delta|\,\Phi(\mathbf r)
+
\frac12
\left(
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta}\delta_i\delta_j
\right)
\partial_i\partial_j\Phi
+
O(\partial^4).
\]

\section{3. Exact second-moment tensors}

\subsection{BCC nearest shell}

For
\[
\Delta_1=\left\{\left(\pm\frac12,\pm\frac12,\pm\frac12\right)\right\},
\]
one has
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\delta_i\delta_j
=
2\,\delta_{ij}.
\]

Indeed, each coordinate contributes
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\delta_x^2
=
8\cdot\frac14
=
2,
\]
and the off-diagonal sums cancel by sign symmetry:
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\delta_x\delta_y
=
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\delta_x\delta_z
=
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\delta_y\delta_z
=
0.
\]

Therefore
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
8\Phi(\mathbf r)+\nabla^2\Phi(\mathbf r)+O(\partial^4).
\]

\subsection{Next shell}

For
\[
\Delta_2=\{(\pm1,0,0),(0,\pm1,0),(0,0,\pm1)\},
\]
one likewise finds
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_2}\delta_i\delta_j
=
2\,\delta_{ij}.
\]

Hence
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_2}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
6\Phi(\mathbf r)+\nabla^2\Phi(\mathbf r)+O(\partial^4).
\]

\subsection{Immediate consequence}

Thus both shells are individually isotropic at second order:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_1:\quad 8\Phi+\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4),
\qquad
\Delta_2:\quad 6\Phi+\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4).
}
\]

This is the correct continuum-limit statement.
It proves exact \(O(\partial^2)\) isotropy of these shell contributions, but by itself it does not prove full all-order isotropy, nor uniqueness of BCC among all possible shells.

\section{4. Discrete stationary equation and continuum reduction}

Take the simplest static discrete equation with two shells:
\[
0
=
-m_0^2\Phi(\mathbf r)
+
J_1\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\bigl[\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)-\Phi(\mathbf r)\bigr]
+
J_2\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_2}\bigl[\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)-\Phi(\mathbf r)\bigr]
-
\gamma \Phi(\mathbf r)^3.
\]

Using the shell expansions above,
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\bigl[\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)-\Phi(\mathbf r)\bigr]
=
\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4),
\]
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_2}\bigl[\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)-\Phi(\mathbf r)\bigr]
=
\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4).
\]

Therefore the continuum equation to second order is
\[
\boxed{
\alpha \nabla^2\Phi+\beta \Phi-\gamma\Phi^3=0,
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=J_1+J_2,
\qquad
\beta=(8J_1+6J_2)-m_0^2.
}
\]

\section{5. Distance-law hypothesis}

Now impose the geometric hopping law
\[
\boxed{
J(d)\propto \frac{1}{d^2}.
}
\]

For the BCC nearest shell,
\[
d_1=\frac{\sqrt3}{2}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
J_1=\frac{1}{d_1^2}=\frac{4}{3},
\]
after choosing the overall normalization constant to be \(1\).

For the next shell,
\[
d_2=1
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
J_2=1.
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=J_1+J_2=\frac43+1=\frac73.
}
\]

Also
\[
8J_1+6J_2
=
8\cdot\frac43+6
=
\frac{32}{3}+6
=
\frac{50}{3}.
\]

\section{6. BPS-like self-tuning assumption}

At this point, the geometry alone does \emph{not} determine \(m_0^2\).
To obtain a specific \(\beta\), one must impose an additional matching rule.

A natural BPS-like self-tuning hypothesis is
\[
\boxed{
m_0^2=\frac12(8J_1+6J_2).
}
\]

Then
\[
\beta
=
(8J_1+6J_2)-m_0^2
=
\frac12(8J_1+6J_2)
=
\frac12\cdot\frac{50}{3}
=
\frac{25}{3}.
\]

So under this hypothesis,
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac73,
\qquad
\beta=\frac{25}{3}.
}
\]

\section{7. Exact kink solution and profile slope}

Restrict to a one-dimensional defect profile \(\Phi=\Phi(\xi)\), where \(\xi\) is the normal coordinate.
Then
\[
\alpha \Phi''+\beta\Phi-\gamma\Phi^3=0.
\]

Take the standard kink ansatz
\[
\Phi(\xi)=\Phi_0\tanh(c\xi).
\]

Using
\[
\frac{d^2}{d\xi^2}\tanh(c\xi)
=
-2c^2\tanh(c\xi)+2c^2\tanh^3(c\xi),
\]
one finds that the equation is solved if and only if
\[
\boxed{
2\alpha c^2=\beta,
\qquad
\gamma \Phi_0^2=\beta.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
c=\sqrt{\frac{\beta}{2\alpha}}.
}
\]

Substituting
\[
\alpha=\frac73,
\qquad
\beta=\frac{25}{3},
\]
gives
\[
\boxed{
c
=
\sqrt{
\frac{25/3}{2\cdot 7/3}
}
=
\sqrt{\frac{25}{14}}
=
\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}}
\approx 1.33630621.
}
\]

Hence the corresponding defect width is
\[
\boxed{
w=\frac{1}{c}
=
\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}
\approx 0.74833148.
}
\]

\section{8. Honest status of the result}

The following part is theorem-level:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact second-moment tensors of the BCC NN shell and the cubic NNN shell;
\item the resulting \(O(\partial^2)\) isotropic continuum coefficient
\[
\alpha=J_1+J_2;
\]
\item the exact kink relation
\[
c=\sqrt{\beta/(2\alpha)}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

The following part is \emph{assumption-level}:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the distance law
\[
J(d)\propto d^{-2};
\]
\item the BPS-like self-tuning rule
\[
m_0^2=\frac12(8J_1+6J_2).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the coefficient set
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac73,\qquad
\beta=\frac{25}{3},\qquad
c=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}},\qquad
w=\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}
}
\]
is not yet a pure geometry theorem.
It is a geometry-plus-matching result.

\section{9. Correct way to use this in the paper}

The right status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{``BCC lattice continuum reduction with a BPS-like self-tuning hypothesis''}
}
\]

not

\[
\boxed{
\text{``final exact first-principles PDE coefficients with no remaining assumption.''}
}
\]

This is still a strong section.
It gives a sharp analytic skeleton for the PDE coefficients and defect thickness,
and it is entirely suitable as a derivational section in the paper, provided the extra assumptions are stated explicitly rather than hidden.

\section{Final Summary}

The proposed BCC-lattice derivation is strong, but it must be written in a mathematically honest way.

The crucial correction is that the standard second-order Taylor expansion yields
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
8\Phi+\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4),
\]
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_2}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
6\Phi+\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4),
\]
not \(8\Phi+2\nabla^2\Phi\) and \(6\Phi+2\nabla^2\Phi\).

With the geometric hopping assumption
\[
J_1=\frac43,\qquad J_2=1,
\]
the continuum kinetic coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=J_1+J_2=\frac73.
}
\]

If one further imposes the BPS-like self-tuning rule
\[
m_0^2=\frac12(8J_1+6J_2),
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\beta=\frac{25}{3}.
}
\]

The exact kink profile
\[
\Phi(\xi)=\Phi_0\tanh(c\xi)
\]
then gives
\[
\boxed{
c=\sqrt{\frac{\beta}{2\alpha}}=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}},
\qquad
w=\frac{1}{c}=\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}.
}
\]

So the coefficient set
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac73,\qquad
\beta=\frac{25}{3},\qquad
c=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}},\qquad
w=\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}
}
\]
is valid as a \emph{geometry-plus-matching} result.

It should be documented in the paper, but not overclaimed as an assumption-free final theorem.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Derivation of Effective PDE Coefficients from the BCC Discrete Geometry}

We now derive a continuum nonlinear field equation directly from the discrete BCC shell geometry.
The purpose of this derivation is not to fit low-energy data, but to isolate the geometric contribution to the effective kinetic coefficient and to identify the additional matching assumption required to fix the local mass scale.

\paragraph{Discrete shell sets.}
Set the cubic lattice constant to \(a=1\).
We retain the two geometrically distinguished shells:
\begin{equation}
\Delta_1
=
\left\{
\left(\pm \frac12,\pm \frac12,\pm \frac12\right)
\right\},
\qquad
|\Delta_1|=8,
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\Delta_2
=
\{(\pm1,0,0),(0,\pm1,0),(0,0,\pm1)\},
\qquad
|\Delta_2|=6.
\end{equation}
Here \(\Delta_1\) is the BCC nearest-neighbor shell and \(\Delta_2\) is the next shell aligned with the cubic axes.

\paragraph{Second-order shell expansion.}
Let \(\Phi(\mathbf r)\) be a slowly varying scalar order parameter.
For any inversion-symmetric shell \(\Delta\), one has
\begin{equation}
\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
\Phi(\mathbf r)
+
\delta_i \partial_i \Phi
+
\frac12 \delta_i\delta_j \partial_i\partial_j \Phi
+
O(\partial^3),
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
|\Delta|\Phi(\mathbf r)
+
\frac12
\left(
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta}\delta_i\delta_j
\right)
\partial_i\partial_j\Phi(\mathbf r)
+
O(\partial^4),
\end{equation}
since the odd term vanishes by \(\delta\leftrightarrow -\delta\).

\paragraph{Exact second-moment tensors.}
For the BCC nearest shell,
\begin{equation}
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\delta_i\delta_j
=
2\,\delta_{ij}.
\end{equation}
Indeed,
\begin{equation}
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\delta_x^2
=
8\cdot \frac14
=
2,
\end{equation}
and by sign symmetry
\begin{equation}
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\delta_x\delta_y
=
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\delta_x\delta_z
=
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\delta_y\delta_z
=
0.
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
8\Phi(\mathbf r)+\nabla^2\Phi(\mathbf r)+O(\partial^4).
\end{equation}

For the next shell,
\begin{equation}
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_2}\delta_i\delta_j
=
2\,\delta_{ij},
\end{equation}
since only the two vectors along a given axis contribute to the diagonal second moment, and off-diagonal terms vanish identically.
Thus
\begin{equation}
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_2}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
6\Phi(\mathbf r)+\nabla^2\Phi(\mathbf r)+O(\partial^4).
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Geometric consequence.}
Both shells are individually isotropic at order \(O(\partial^2)\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
8\Phi+\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4),
\qquad
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_2}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
6\Phi+\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4).
}
\end{equation}
This is the precise continuum-limit statement.
It proves exact second-order isotropy of the retained BCC shell reduction.

\paragraph{Discrete stationary equation.}
Consider the static two-shell discrete field equation
\begin{equation}
0
=
-m_0^2\Phi(\mathbf r)
+
J_1\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\bigl[\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)-\Phi(\mathbf r)\bigr]
+
J_2\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_2}\bigl[\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)-\Phi(\mathbf r)\bigr]
-
\gamma \Phi(\mathbf r)^3.
\end{equation}
Substituting the shell expansions gives
\begin{equation}
0
=
\alpha \nabla^2\Phi
+
\beta \Phi
-
\gamma \Phi^3
+
O(\partial^4),
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha = J_1+J_2,
\qquad
\beta = (8J_1+6J_2)-m_0^2.
}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Distance-law assumption.}
To convert the shell geometry into hard numbers, we impose the first-principles distance law
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J(d)\propto \frac{1}{d^2}.
}
\end{equation}
With unit normalization constant, the shell distances are
\begin{equation}
d_1=\frac{\sqrt3}{2},
\qquad
d_2=1,
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
J_1=\frac{1}{d_1^2}=\frac43,
\qquad
J_2=\frac{1}{d_2^2}=1.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha = J_1+J_2 = \frac43+1 = \frac73.
}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{BPS-like matching assumption.}
At this stage the geometry alone does not determine \(m_0^2\).
To fix \(\beta\), we impose the minimal self-tuning rule
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_0^2=\frac12(8J_1+6J_2).
}
\end{equation}
This is a matching hypothesis, not a pure geometry theorem.
Under this assumption,
\begin{equation}
8J_1+6J_2
=
8\cdot\frac43+6
=
\frac{50}{3},
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
(8J_1+6J_2)-m_0^2
=
\frac12(8J_1+6J_2)
=
\frac{25}{3}.
}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Exact kink profile.}
Restrict now to a one-dimensional defect coordinate \(\xi\), so that
\begin{equation}
\alpha \Phi''(\xi)+\beta \Phi(\xi)-\gamma \Phi(\xi)^3=0.
\end{equation}
Take the standard kink ansatz
\begin{equation}
\Phi(\xi)=\Phi_0\tanh(c\xi).
\end{equation}
Using
\begin{equation}
\frac{d^2}{d\xi^2}\tanh(c\xi)
=
-2c^2\tanh(c\xi)+2c^2\tanh^3(c\xi),
\end{equation}
one finds the consistency conditions
\begin{equation}
2\alpha c^2=\beta,
\qquad
\gamma \Phi_0^2=\beta.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c=\sqrt{\frac{\beta}{2\alpha}}.
}
\end{equation}
Substituting the coefficients above yields
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c
=
\sqrt{\frac{25/3}{2\cdot 7/3}}
=
\sqrt{\frac{25}{14}}
=
\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}}
\approx 1.33630621.
}
\end{equation}
Hence the corresponding defect width is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
w=\frac{1}{c}
=
\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}
\approx 0.74833148.
}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Final coefficient set.}
Under the combination of
(i) exact BCC second-moment isotropy,
(ii) the distance law \(J(d)\propto d^{-2}\),
and
(iii) the BPS-like half-coupling matching condition,
the effective continuum coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac73,
\qquad
\beta=\frac{25}{3},
\qquad
c=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}},
\qquad
w=\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}.
}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Honest status.}
The isotropic second-moment reduction is theorem-level.
The numerical values of \(\alpha,\beta,c,w\) additionally require the explicit assumptions
\[
J(d)\propto d^{-2},
\qquad
m_0^2=\frac12(8J_1+6J_2).
\]
Accordingly, the result should be presented as a geometry-plus-matching derivation, not as an assumption-free final theorem.

\section{Final Summary}

The BCC shell geometry gives an exact second-order isotropic continuum reduction:
\[
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_1}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
8\Phi+\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4),
\qquad
\sum_{\delta\in\Delta_2}\Phi(\mathbf r+\delta)
=
6\Phi+\nabla^2\Phi+O(\partial^4).
\]

For the two-shell discrete stationary equation, this implies
\[
\alpha=J_1+J_2,
\qquad
\beta=(8J_1+6J_2)-m_0^2.
\]

With the geometric hopping law
\[
J(d)\propto d^{-2},
\qquad
J_1=\frac43,
\qquad
J_2=1,
\]
one obtains
\[
\alpha=\frac73.
\]

If one further imposes the BPS-like matching condition
\[
m_0^2=\frac12(8J_1+6J_2),
\]
then
\[
\beta=\frac{25}{3}.
\]

The exact kink profile
\[
\Phi(\xi)=\Phi_0\tanh(c\xi)
\]
then yields
\[
c=\sqrt{\frac{\beta}{2\alpha}}=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}},
\qquad
w=\frac{1}{c}=\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}.
\]

Hence the coefficient set
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac73,\qquad
\beta=\frac{25}{3},\qquad
c=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}},\qquad
w=\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}
}
\]
is rigorously valid as a geometry-plus-matching result.

This section is suitable for inclusion in the paper, provided the second-order Taylor coefficient is written correctly and the matching assumptions are stated explicitly.

\section{Insertion of the BCC-Derived Soliton Slope into the \texorpdfstring{$\Omega_{14}$}{Omega14} CKM Backend}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now insert the BCC-derived profile slope
\[
c=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}},
\qquad
w=\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5},
\]
directly into the frozen \(\Omega_{14}\)+soliton CKM backend.

The purpose is not yet to claim final intended-branch closure,
but to test whether the first non-arbitrary microscopic CP seed persists after replacing the provisional profile scale by the geometry-plus-matching value derived from the BCC discrete PDE reduction.

\section{1. Frozen backend}

The frozen microscopic flavor backend is:
\[
\boxed{
\Omega_{14}\text{ (BCC truncated-octahedral primitive cell)}
\quad+\quad
\theta(\xi)\sim \sech(c\xi),
}
\]
with the same finite-family exact/microscopic architecture
\[
(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d)\to J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}},
\qquad
(\Lambda,\Delta,r)\to \Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}.
\]

The BCC reciprocal background is
\[
\phi_0(\mathbf x)=2A\sum_{a=1}^6 \cos(\mathbf Q_a\cdot \mathbf x),
\]
and the corresponding real-space Wigner--Seitz cell is the 14-faced truncated octahedron \(\Omega_{14}\).

\section{2. Inserted profile scale}

From the BCC discrete shell reduction with the matching assumption discussed previously, the defect-profile slope and width are
\[
\boxed{
c=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}}\approx 1.336306209562,
\qquad
w=\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}\approx 0.748331477355.
}
\]

We identify the polyhedral-solitonic kernel parameters as
\[
\boxed{
\kappa=c,
\qquad
s=w.
}
\]

So the primitive-cell channel kernel becomes
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T}(Q)
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega_{14}|}
\int_{\Omega_{14}} d^3x\;
e^{-iQ\cdot x}\,
\sech^\nu\!\bigl(c(\xi-w/2)\bigr)\,
\sech^2(c\xi)\,
\sech^\nu\!\bigl(c(\xi+w/2)\bigr),
\]
with
\[
\xi=\hat n\cdot x,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,1,0),
\qquad
\nu=1.
\]

\section{3. Exact geometric checks}

The BCC first-shell pair counting remains
\[
\boxed{
N(G_*)=4.
}
\]

This confirms that the shell combinatorics of the frozen BCC backend are unchanged by the profile rescaling.

\section{4. Updated primitive-cell Fourier kernel values}

With \(c=5/\sqrt{14}\) and \(w=\sqrt{14}/5\), the selected kernel values become
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal T}(2,0,0)
\approx
0.4320076904+2.1191\times 10^{-4}i,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal T}(0,2,0)
\approx
0.4320076904+2.1191\times 10^{-4}i,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal T}(2,1,1)
\approx
0.4102219551+5.1410\times 10^{-4}i,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal T}(0,1,-1)
\approx
0.4601956544-1.9042\times 10^{-4}i.
}
\]

Thus the \(\Omega_{14}\)+soliton primitive-cell kernel remains genuinely complex and anisotropic after the BCC-derived profile-scale insertion.

\section{5. Microscopic CP seed after the \(c\)-insertion}

Using the same automatic-support rule
\[
\mathrm{Supp}_{AB}
=
\{\,G-G': c_{A,G}\neq 0,\ c_{B,G'}\neq 0\,\},
\]
and no extra ad hoc phase insertion beyond the polyhedral Fourier phase itself, the prototype exact-family route still gives
\[
\boxed{
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}=0,
}
\]
for the current toy family basis.

However, the microscopic route now gives
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
\approx
-6.111631333675723\times 10^{-6}.
}
\]

Hence the microscopic CP cycle remains nonzero after the BCC-derived profile-scale insertion.

\section{6. Minimal practical sign test}

For the present minimal prototype, the residual insertions were set to zero, so
\[
\boxed{
E_{\mathrm{tot}}=0.
}
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|>E_{\mathrm{tot}}
}
\]
holds automatically, and the practical sign-prediction test passes.

\section{7. Honest status}

This does \emph{not} yet establish final intended-branch CKM closure.

What it does establish is more precise:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the first non-arbitrary microscopic CP seed survives the replacement }
\kappa\to \frac{5}{\sqrt{14}},\ s\to \frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}.
}
\]

So the BCC-derived solitonic slope does not kill the microscopic CP cycle.
Instead, it yields a smaller but still nonzero value:
\[
-1.6575\times 10^{-5}
\;\longrightarrow\;
-6.1116\times 10^{-6}.
\]

Thus the geometric-solitonic backend remains alive after this sharper profile insertion.

\section{8. Interpretation}

The present run should be interpreted as follows.

The \(\Omega_{14}\) geometry is frozen.
The support is extracted automatically from the family shell basis.
The phase is not inserted by hand.
The solitonic width/slope is no longer provisional, but imported from the BCC discrete PDE reduction.

Therefore the remaining frontier is not geometric and not profile-theoretic.
It is the actual intended-branch insertion of the family/flavor-dependent tables
\[
c_{A,G},\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal K}_f(Q),\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal Y}_f(Q),\qquad
g_{AB}^{(f)}.
\]

Only after these are supplied can one meaningfully compare the exact-route value \(J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}\) and the microscopic route \(\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\) on the same physical branch.

\section{Final Summary}

We inserted the BCC-derived defect-profile slope and width
\[
\boxed{
c=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}},
\qquad
w=\frac{\sqrt{14}}{5}
}
\]
directly into the frozen \(\Omega_{14}\)+soliton CKM backend.

The resulting primitive-cell Fourier kernel remains anisotropic and complex, with representative values
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T}(2,0,0)\approx 0.4320076904+2.1191\times10^{-4}i,
\]
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T}(2,1,1)\approx 0.4102219551+5.1410\times10^{-4}i.
\]

With automatic support extraction and no extra ad hoc phase insertion, the microscopic CP predictor becomes
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\approx -6.111631333675723\times10^{-6}.
}
\]

In the minimal prototype with vanishing residual insertions,
\[
E_{\mathrm{tot}}=0,
\]
so the practical sign-prediction test passes:
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|>E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
\]

Therefore the first non-arbitrary microscopic CP seed survives even after replacing the provisional solitonic scale by the BCC-derived value
\[
c=\frac{5}{\sqrt{14}}.
\]

This still does not constitute final intended-branch closure.
But it shows that the geometric-solitonic backend remains nontrivially alive after the sharper BCC profile insertion.

\section{A Single Unified Execution Plan for Completing TECT}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The project feels endless because the same structural content has been revisited through multiple partial front-ends:
carrier reduction, CKM reduction, polyhedral backend design, shell reductions, and PDE discussion.

The correct way to end this is to stop treating these as separate programs.
They must all be subordinated to one common object:

\[
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x),
}
\]
the actual nonlinear microscopic branch solution.

Once \(\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)\) is obtained, every remaining unresolved item becomes a finite extractor problem on the same branch.

Thus the completion strategy should be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{one actual PDE branch}
\;\to\;
\text{one common extractor}
\;\to\;
\text{all remaining certificates}.
}
\]

\section{1. Present honest status}

The current notes already establish that the project is \emph{not} structurally blocked.

\paragraph{Carrier status.}
The carrier-level theorem chain is already closed, and the honest current diagnosis is
\[
\boxed{
\text{proof complete, certificate incomplete.}
}
\]
The remaining task is explicitly stated to be a finite Gate audit:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\quad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\quad
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]

\paragraph{CKM status.}
The flavor/CKM program is already structurally reduced to two finite routes:
\[
(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d)\to J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}},
\qquad
(\Lambda,\Delta,r)\to \Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\to J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{pred}}.
\]
The honest open part is the numerical filling of the intended-branch tables
\[
S,\ M^{(u,d)},\ N^{(u,d)},
\qquad
\Lambda_{ij}^{(u,d)},\ \Delta_{ij}^{(u,d)},\ r_{ij}^{(u,d)},
\]
followed by the final consistency inequality
\[
\left|J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\right|\le E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
\]

\paragraph{Actual-branch obstruction.}
The notes also state explicitly that
\[
\boxed{
(W_2,m_*,g_{\rm eff})\text{ cannot be computed without }\Psi_{\rm actual}(x).
}
\]
So the real bottleneck is no longer theorem structure, but the missing actual nonlinear solution.

\section{2. The central mistake to avoid}

The project must \emph{not} continue by alternating among:
\[
\text{carrier front-end} \leftrightarrow \text{CKM front-end} \leftrightarrow \text{geometry backend changes} \leftrightarrow \text{new toy reductions}.
\]

That mode causes repeated work because each front-end asks for overlapping but differently packaged data.

Instead, every unresolved numerical quantity must be treated as a functional of one common actual branch:
\[
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x).
\]

\section{3. The only nonredundant completion architecture}

The correct architecture is the following.

\subsection{Phase I: actual nonlinear PDE branch}

Solve the actual nonlinear microscopic PDE for the intended branch:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E'[\Psi]=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x).
}
\]

This phase ends only when the solution is numerically accepted under:
\begin{enumerate}
\item grid convergence,
\item time-relaxation convergence,
\item perturbative/Hessian stability,
\item branch-geometry acceptance (intended BCC sector, not one-patch collapse).
\end{enumerate}

No carrier/CKM final claims are allowed before this phase.

\subsection{Phase II: one common extractor}

Construct one common extractor acting on the same \(\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)\):
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak E[\Psi_{\rm actual}]
=
\Bigl(
W_2,\ m_*,\ g_{\rm eff},\
S,\ M^{(f)},\ N^{(f)},\
\Lambda,\ \Delta,\ r,\
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}},\ \eta_{R,\rho},\
\Delta_{00},\ L_*,\
(c_E,c_O),\ (C_E,C_O),\
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}],\
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}],\
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]
\Bigr).
}
\]

This is the key design choice.
All unresolved observables are extracted once, from one branch, using one backend.

\subsection{Phase III: carrier certificate}

After the extractor exists, run the already-closed carrier Gate chain, with no theorem rebuilding:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1}\to \text{Gate 2}\to \text{Gate 3}\to \text{Gate 4}.
}
\]

That means:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\]
\[
|\Delta_{00}\alpha_XL_*A_{G_*}|>|R_N|
\quad\text{or equivalent longitudinal witness},
\]
\[
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0),
\]
\[
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\]

If all pass, the carrier block is complete.

\subsection{Phase IV: CKM certificate}

Using the same extracted branch tables, run the already-closed CKM exact and microscopic routes:
\[
(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d)\to J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}},
\]
\[
(\Lambda,\Delta,r)\to \Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}.
\]

Then test
\[
\boxed{
\left|J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\right|\le E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\]

This is not a new theorem phase.
It is a finite branch execution phase.

\subsection{Phase V: actual anisotropy / hierarchy observables}

Now and only now extract
\[
W_2,\qquad m_*,\qquad g_{\rm eff},
\]
and use them in the already-derived anisotropy formulas such as
\[
Z_{\rm cub}
=
-\frac{g_{\rm eff}^2}{144\pi\,m_*^3}\,\varepsilon_{\rm lock},
\]
or the corresponding actual-branch hierarchy predictors.

This closes the bridge between the actual nonlinear PDE solution and the CKM/hierarchy observables.

\subsection{Phase VI: broader IR TOE completion}

Only after Phases I--V should one return to the broader unresolved sectors:
\[
\text{full gauge-sector emergence},
\qquad
\text{Einstein-type gravity sector},
\qquad
\text{decoupling of extra states},
\qquad
\text{anomaly/unitarity consistency}.
\]

\section{4. Operational freeze rules}

To prevent further repetition, impose the following hard freeze rules.

\paragraph{Rule 1.}
No re-derivation of already closed structural theorems.

\paragraph{Rule 2.}
No switching of microscopic backend after Phase I begins.

\paragraph{Rule 3.}
No separate carrier-only and CKM-only data pipelines.
Both must consume the same extractor output.

\paragraph{Rule 4.}
No new toy branch once \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\) is under construction.

\paragraph{Rule 5.}
Every new computation must answer one of only two questions:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does it help solve }\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)\ ?
}
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\boxed{
\text{Does it help extract one entry of }\mathfrak E[\Psi_{\rm actual}] \ ?
}
\end{equation}

If the answer is no, it is postponed.

\section{5. Immediate executable next step}

The next nonredundant task is therefore unique:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Phase I: build and accept }\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)\text{ on the intended BCC branch.}
}
\]

Concretely, this means:

\begin{enumerate}
\item fix the nonlinear microscopic PDE and energy functional once;
\item choose one intended BCC-symmetric initial condition only;
\item evolve/relax to stationarity;
\item reject one-patch collapse and keep only branch candidates with intended BCC orbit content;
\item accept only solutions stable under grid/time/perturbation tests;
\item freeze the accepted \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\) and never change branch/backend again.
\end{enumerate}

\section{6. Why this plan is final}

This plan ends the repetition problem because it aligns the whole project around one actual object.
Carrier, CKM, anisotropy, and effective observables are no longer treated as competing subprojects.
They become different finite readouts of the same branch solution.

So the project stops being:

\[
\text{theorem} \to \text{toy number} \to \text{new backend} \to \text{theorem again},
\]

and becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)
\to
\mathfrak E[\Psi_{\rm actual}]
\to
\text{carrier certificate + CKM certificate + IR observables}.
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The project should now be forced into a single execution architecture.

The structural reductions are already largely complete:
the carrier theorem chain is closed, and the CKM program is already reduced to a finite exact route and a finite microscopic route.
What is still missing is not another round of structural theory-building, but the actual nonlinear branch and the finite extraction of branch-dependent data.

Therefore the only nonredundant completion plan is:

\[
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\mathfrak E[\Psi_{\rm actual}]
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\text{carrier certificate + CKM certificate + actual observables}.
}
\]

This defines the six phases:

\begin{enumerate}
\item solve the actual nonlinear microscopic PDE for the intended BCC branch;
\item build one common extractor for all remaining unresolved quantities;
\item run the already-closed carrier Gate audit;
\item run the already-closed CKM exact/microscopic consistency audit;
\item extract the actual anisotropy observables \(W_2,m_*,g_{\rm eff}\);
\item only then return to the broader IR TOE sectors.
\end{enumerate}

The key freeze rule is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{no more theorem rebuilding, no more backend switching, no more separate front-ends.}
}
\]

From this point on, every worthwhile computation must either help construct \(\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)\) or help extract one component of \(\mathfrak E[\Psi_{\rm actual}]\).
