\section{Phase I: Actual \texorpdfstring{$\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)$}{Psi_actual(x)} Solver Specification}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The project should now be frozen around one single executable object:
\[
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x),
}
\]
the actual nonlinear microscopic branch solution.

All remaining carrier certificates, CKM tables, and anisotropy observables will be extracted from this same branch.
No more backend switching is allowed once this specification is fixed.

\section{1. Microscopic nonlinear PDE to be solved}

The frozen Class II microscopic field is
\[
\Psi(x,t)\in\mathbb C^3,
\qquad
z(x,t)=\frac{\Psi(x,t)}{|\Psi(x,t)|}\in\mathbb{CP}^2.
\]

The full nonlinear Class II equation of motion is taken to be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t^2 \Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G[\Psi],
}
\label{eq:PhaseI_full_PDE}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal G[\Psi]\) is the geometric Class II contribution induced by
\[
A_i=-iz^\dagger\partial_i z,
\qquad
F_{ij}=\partial_iA_j-\partial_jA_i,
\qquad
\mathcal L_{\rm geom}=\kappa |F_{ij}|^2.
\]

This is the microscopic PDE that must be solved before any final actual-branch claim can be made. The notes also make clear that actual observables such as \(W_2,m_*,g_{\rm eff}\) cannot be computed without the actual branch solution. 

\section{2. Stationary branch problem}

We do not seek a generic time-dependent trajectory.
We seek a stationary actual branch
\[
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)
\]
satisfying
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G[\Psi]
=
0.
}
\label{eq:PhaseI_stationary_PDE}
\end{equation}

Operationally, we solve this by pseudo-time relaxation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_\tau \Psi
=
\mu^2\Psi
-Z\nabla^2\Psi
+Y\nabla^4\Psi
+\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
+\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
-\mathcal G[\Psi],
}
\label{eq:PhaseI_gradient_flow}
\end{equation}
until convergence to a stationary fixed point.

\section{3. Spatial domain and discretization}

Use a periodic cubic box
\[
\Omega_L=[-L/2,L/2)^3
\]
with pseudospectral Fourier discretization on an \(N^3\) grid.
The box must be commensurate with the target shell radius \(q_0\), so that the first BCC shell harmonics
\[
\hat k_\alpha\in
\left\{
\frac{(\pm1,\pm1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(\pm1,0,\pm1)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(0,\pm1,\pm1)}{\sqrt2}
\right\}
\]
are represented exactly on the discrete Fourier lattice.

The linear stiff part of \eqref{eq:PhaseI_gradient_flow} is evolved semi-implicitly in Fourier space, while the nonlinear local and geometric parts are treated explicitly or by a predictor-corrector update.

\section{4. Initial-condition freeze}

To avoid repeated toy-branch drift, fix one intended BCC-symmetric initial condition:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm init}(x)
=
\Psi_{\rm BCC}(x)
+
\varepsilon_{\rm def}\,\Psi_{\rm def}(x)
+
\varepsilon_{\rm noise}\,\delta\Psi(x),
}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\Psi_{\rm BCC}(x)\) is the equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC shell condensate,
\item \(\Psi_{\rm def}(x)\) is a single chosen defect seed in the selected Class II channel,
\item \(\delta\Psi(x)\) is small generic complex noise.
\end{enumerate}

No alternative toy branch is allowed after this point.
If the run collapses away from the intended BCC sector, that run is rejected rather than reinterpreted.

\section{5. Numerical acceptance criteria for }\Psi_{\rm actual}

A converged field is accepted as \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\) only if all of the following hold.

\paragraph{(A) PDE residual.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\|R[\Psi]\|_{L^2}}{\|\Psi\|_{L^2}}<\varepsilon_{\rm PDE},
}
\end{equation}
where
\[
R[\Psi]
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G[\Psi].
\]

\paragraph{(B) Relaxation convergence.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\|\Psi(\tau+\Delta\tau)-\Psi(\tau)\|_{L^2}}{\|\Psi(\tau)\|_{L^2}}
<
\varepsilon_{\rm step}.
}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(C) Grid convergence.}
The branch must be stable under
\[
N\to N+\Delta N,
\qquad
L\to L+\Delta L,
\qquad
\Delta\tau\to \Delta\tau/2.
\]
In practice, all extracted observables must change by less than preset tolerances.

\paragraph{(D) Intended-BCC branch acceptance.}
The converged solution must remain in the intended BCC sector.
The operational tests are:
\begin{enumerate}
\item dominant Fourier support concentrated on the 12 BCC shell modes,
\item no one-patch collapse,
\item defect-center geometry consistent with the BCC \(8+6\) shell structure,
\item stable shell moments \(W_0,W_2\) under resolution refinement.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{(E) Local stability.}
After convergence, linearize the relaxation operator around \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\).
The accepted branch must be nonlinearly stationary and linearly stable modulo the expected exact symmetry zero modes.

\section{6. One common extractor after branch acceptance}

Once \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\) is accepted, freeze it and extract all remaining data from the same branch.

\subsection{6.1 Carrier extractor}

Run the already-closed carrier finite audit:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
|\Delta_{00}\,\alpha_X\,L_*\,A_{G_*}|>|R_N|
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\]

These are already structurally closed in the notes; what remains is only actual branch insertion. 

\subsection{6.2 Bloch / Dirac-data extractor}

Construct the periodic linearized Bloch operator
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k),
\]
choose the shell pair \(S_*\), isolate the valley projector \(P_*\), compute
\[
K_i=\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0),
\]
and evaluate
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr\!\left[\sigma_3P_*(\hat n_iK_i)P_*\right],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\Tr\!\left[
\sigma_1P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*
+
\sigma_2P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*
\right],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12\Tr\!\left[
\sigma_2P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*
-
\sigma_1P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*
\right].
}
\]

The notes explicitly state that the full-PDE program is complete once this finite Bloch-shell-projection extraction is carried out. 

\subsection{6.3 CKM / family extractor}

From the same \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\), construct the intended-branch family basis and compute the finite tables
\[
S,\qquad
M^{(f)},\qquad
N^{(f)},
\qquad
\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)},\qquad
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)},\qquad
r_{ij}^{(f)}.
\]

Then evaluate both routes:
\[
(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d)\to J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}},
\qquad
(\Lambda,\Delta,r)\to \Xi_{\mathrm{mic}},
\]
and impose
\[
\boxed{
\left|J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\right|\le E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\]

The notes already identify this as the finite intended-branch closure problem. 

\subsection{6.4 Actual anisotropy observables}

Compute the shell moments
\[
W_0,\qquad W_2,\qquad M_2,\qquad G_4,
\]
then reconstruct
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm lock}=3\frac{W_2}{W_0},
\qquad
m_*^2=\frac{M_2}{W_0},
\qquad
g_{\rm eff}=\frac{G_4}{W_0},
\]
and finally
\[
\boxed{
Z_{\rm cub}
=
-\frac{g_{\rm eff}^2}{144\pi m_*^3}\varepsilon_{\rm lock}.
}
\]

These formulas are already closed in the notes; they only need actual branch data. 

\section{7. Hard freeze rules}

To stop further repetition, impose the following rules:

\begin{enumerate}
\item no re-derivation of already closed structural theorems;
\item no backend change after \eqref{eq:PhaseI_full_PDE} is fixed;
\item no separate carrier-only and CKM-only pipelines;
\item no new toy branch once \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\) construction begins;
\item every new calculation must answer either:
\[
\text{``does it help solve }\Psi_{\rm actual}\text{?''}
\]
or
\[
\text{``does it extract one entry from the common branch extractor?''}
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{8. What counts as completion}

Phase I is complete only when:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a stationary intended-BCC solution \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\) has been accepted numerically;
\item the Bloch-shell projector extraction yields \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\);
\item the carrier Gates 1--4 have explicit PASS/FAIL values;
\item the CKM exact and microscopic routes are both evaluated on the same branch;
\item the anisotropy observables \((W_2,m_*,g_{\rm eff},Z_{\rm cub})\) are extracted on the same branch.
\end{enumerate}

At that point, the project moves from
\[
\text{working branch / structural closure}
\]
to
\[
\boxed{
\text{actual branch / certificate completion.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The project should now be frozen around one single executable object:
\[
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x),
}
\]
the actual stationary solution of the full nonlinear Class II microscopic PDE
\[
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G[\Psi]
=0.
\]

This branch must be obtained by a single pseudospectral relaxation pipeline with:
\begin{enumerate}
\item BCC-symmetric initial data,
\item PDE-residual convergence,
\item time-step convergence,
\item grid/box convergence,
\item intended-BCC branch acceptance,
\item local linear stability modulo symmetry zero modes.
\end{enumerate}

Once \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\) is accepted, one common extractor must produce all remaining data:
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
\quad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}},\eta_{R,\rho},
\quad
\Delta_{00},L_*,
\]
\[
(c_E,c_O),(C_E,C_O),
\quad
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}],
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}],
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)],
\]
\[
S,\ M^{(f)},\ N^{(f)},\ \Lambda,\ \Delta,\ r,
\quad
W_0,\ W_2,\ M_2,\ G_4.
\]

Thus carrier certification, CKM certification, and anisotropy observables are no longer separate programs.
They are finite readouts of the same accepted branch.

From this point on, no more theorem rebuilding and no more backend switching are allowed.
The only legitimate tasks are:
\[
\boxed{
\text{solve }\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{extract one component from the accepted branch.}

\section{Phase I: Actual \texorpdfstring{$\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)$}{Psi_actual(x)} Solver Skeleton}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The project must now stop branching into separate front-ends.
We freeze one single numerical object:
\[
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm actual}(x),
}
\]
and all remaining carrier, CKM, and anisotropy quantities are extracted from that same branch.

The present code skeleton implements exactly this strategy:
a pseudo-time semi-implicit pseudospectral relaxation for the strongest explicit current microscopic branch.

\section{1. Frozen microscopic branch}

The strongest explicit current microscopic branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\end{equation}

This is not yet the final unconditional complete TECT action, but it is the explicit branch in which the full-PDE derivation can be pushed concretely.

\section{2. Stationary actual-branch PDE}

The stationary nonlinear microscopic PDE is frozen in the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G[\Psi]
=
0,
}
\label{eq:phase1_stationary}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal G[\Psi]\) denotes the geometric/Class II contribution.

The current solver does not hard-code a final closed formula for \(\mathcal G[\Psi]\).
Instead, it freezes the computational interface:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G[\Psi]
\text{ is supplied through a callback.}
}
\]
This is the correct design choice, because the numerical pipeline should not be rewritten once the exact Class II tensor implementation is finalized.

\section{3. Pseudo-time relaxation}

To compute a stationary branch, the solver uses pseudo-time relaxation:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_\tau \Psi
=
\mu^2\Psi
-Z\nabla^2\Psi
+Y\nabla^4\Psi
+\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
+\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
-\mathcal G[\Psi].
}
\label{eq:phase1_relaxation}
\end{equation}

We split this into a stiff linear part
\[
L
=
\mu^2-Z\nabla^2+Y\nabla^4,
\]
and a nonlinear part
\[
N(\Psi)
=
\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi+\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi-\mathcal G[\Psi].
\]

Then one semi-implicit step is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(1-\Delta\tau\,L)\Psi^{n+1}
=
\Psi^n+\Delta\tau\,N(\Psi^n).
}
\label{eq:phase1_semiimplicit}
\end{equation}

In Fourier space this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat\Psi^{\,n+1}(k)
=
\frac{
\widehat\Psi^{\,n}(k)
+\Delta\tau\,\widehat{N(\Psi^n)}(k)
}{
1+\Delta\tau\bigl(\mu^2-Z(-|k|^2)+Y|k|^4\bigr)
}.
}
\label{eq:phase1_fourier_update}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the scheme implemented in the solver skeleton.

\section{4. Periodic BCC-compatible box}

The solver uses a periodic cubic box
\[
\Omega_L=[-L/2,L/2)^3
\]
with Fourier pseudospectral discretization on an \(N_x\times N_y\times N_z\) grid.

The first BCC reciprocal shell is frozen as
\[
\mathcal S_{12}
=
\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),\,
(\pm1,0,\pm1),\,
(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\},
\]
and the initial condensate seed is the equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC shell
\[
\phi_0(x)
=
A_{\rm BCC}\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\]

Thus the initial condition is of the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm init}(x)
=
z_0\,\phi_0(x)
+
\varepsilon_{\rm def}\,\Psi_{\rm def}(x)
+
\varepsilon_{\rm noise}\,\delta\Psi(x),
}
\end{equation}
with one fixed internal seed \(z_0\), one defect seed, and small generic complex noise.

This implements the no-loop rule:
the intended BCC branch is chosen once and not redefined later.

\section{5. Acceptance diagnostics implemented in the solver}

The solver skeleton already implements the following diagnostics.

\paragraph{(A) Relative step convergence}
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\|\Psi^{n+1}-\Psi^n\|_{L^2}}{\|\Psi^n\|_{L^2}}.
}
\]

\paragraph{(B) PDE residual}
\[
\boxed{
R[\Psi]
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G[\Psi].
}
\]
and the solver measures
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\|R[\Psi]\|_{L^2}}{\|\Psi\|_{L^2}}.
}
\]

\paragraph{(C) Shell-power fraction}
The code computes the fraction of Fourier power concentrated near the target first BCC shell:
\[
\boxed{
f_{\rm shell}
=
\frac{\sum_{||k|-q_0|\le \delta} |\widehat\Psi(k)|^2}
{\sum_k |\widehat\Psi(k)|^2}.
}
\]
This is a practical intended-BCC acceptance test.

\paragraph{(D) No-one-patch-collapse indicator}
The code also samples the 12 shell directions and computes the ratio
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\min_{\alpha\in\mathcal S_{12}} P_\alpha}
{\max_{\alpha\in\mathcal S_{12}} P_\alpha},
}
\]
where \(P_\alpha\) is the shell power near the \(\alpha\)-th BCC direction.
This is a first collapse detector.

\section{6. Why this solver is the correct bottleneck object}

The notes explicitly state that the true remaining microscopic bottleneck is no longer another abstract witness theorem,
but the construction of
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k),\qquad
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p),\qquad
P_*K_iP_*,
\]
and hence the extraction of
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad
\alpha,\qquad
\beta.
\]

They also state that the carrier theorem chain is closed and only needs finite insertion,
and that the flavor problem is reduced to a finite number of \(3\times3\) operators once the sectoral perturbations are extracted from the full defect PDE.

Therefore the correct design is to freeze one accepted branch \(\Psi_{\rm actual}\), and then extract everything from that same branch.

\section{7. What the current code already does}

The provided Python solver file already implements:

\begin{enumerate}
\item periodic cubic grid construction;
\item Fourier pseudospectral Laplacian and bi-Laplacian;
\item equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC initial condition;
\item defect-seeded initial perturbation;
\item semi-implicit pseudo-time relaxation;
\item residual evaluation;
\item shell-fraction and no-collapse diagnostics;
\item JSON-exportable run summary.
\end{enumerate}

\section{8. What must still be inserted by hand}

The only truly model-specific piece still missing from the code is the actual geometric/Class II callback
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G[\Psi].
}
\]

Everything else is already frozen as the common numerical infrastructure.

So the practical next step is no longer to redesign the solver,
but to implement the exact Class II tensor contribution inside the callback and then run branch acceptance tests.

\section{Final Summary}

A single executable Phase-I solver skeleton has now been fixed for the actual nonlinear microscopic branch \(\Psi_{\rm actual}(x)\).

The code implements a semi-implicit pseudospectral relaxation for the stationary PDE
\[
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G[\Psi]
=
0,
\]
using the corresponding pseudo-time flow
\[
\partial_\tau \Psi
=
\mu^2\Psi
-Z\nabla^2\Psi
+Y\nabla^4\Psi
+\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
+\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
-\mathcal G[\Psi].
\]

The solver already contains:
\begin{enumerate}

Thus the numerical infrastructure is now frozen.

\section{Explicit Working Class II Callback for the Actual \texorpdfstring{$\Psi_{\rm actual}$}{Psi_actual} Solver}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The only genuinely model-specific missing ingredient in the Phase-I solver was the Class II geometric callback
\[
\mathcal G[\Psi].
\]

The correct working choice is to derive it from the strongest explicit microscopic branch already isolated in the notes:
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[P,\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\Psi].
\]

The heavy mediator \(X_i^a\) is then eliminated algebraically, producing an effective \(\Psi\)-only nonlinear contribution.
This is not yet the final unconditional unique completion of TECT, but it is the strongest explicit solver-ready Class II callback currently justified by the working-branch derivations.

\section{1. Starting point: explicit Class II mediator sector}

We begin from the explicit working microscopic branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[P,\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\label{eq:callback_start_branch}
\end{equation}

This is the same explicit Class II structure already used in the finite carrier audit and in the shell-level coefficient dictionary.

\section{2. Working promotion of the two currents}

We now need a concrete \(\Psi\)-only realization of the two currents.

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_\varepsilon := \Psi^\dagger\Psi+\varepsilon,
\qquad
z:=\frac{\Psi}{\sqrt{\rho_\varepsilon}},
\qquad
P[\Psi]=zz^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:callback_rho_z_P}
\end{equation}

Choose a locked \(su(2)\subset su(3)\) Hermitian generator triplet \(T^a\) (\(a=1,2,3\)); in code we take the embedded \(\lambda_1,\lambda_2,\lambda_3\) Gell-Mann block, normalized as \(T^a=\lambda_a/2\).

Define the internal bilinear
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a[\Psi]:=\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi,
\qquad
n^a[\Psi]:=z^\dagger T^a z=\frac{m^a}{\rho_\varepsilon}.
}
\label{eq:callback_m_n}
\end{equation}

Then the natural working promotion of the explicit Class II currents is:

\paragraph{Shell/background-type current}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\Psi]
:=
\partial_i m^a
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi).
}
\label{eq:callback_J}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Projector/tangent-type current}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[\Psi]
:=
\rho_\varepsilon\,\partial_i n^a
=
\partial_i m^a-n^a\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon.
}
\label{eq:callback_K}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal local \(\Psi\)-only realization that simultaneously preserves:
\begin{enumerate}
\item one spatial derivative index \(i\),
\item one internal reduced-shell/tangent index \(a\),
\item the shell/projector split already identified in the Class II derivation.
\end{enumerate}

\section{3. Algebraic elimination of the heavy mediator}

The mediator equation of motion is algebraic:
\begin{equation}
\frac{\partial L_{\mathrm{mic}}}{\partial X_i^a}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
M_X^2 X_i^a+\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a=0.
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_i^a
=
-\frac{\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:callback_Xsol}
\end{equation}

Substituting back yields the \(\Psi\)-only effective Class II correction
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta \mathcal E_{II}[\Psi]
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
F_i^a F_i^a,
}
\label{eq:callback_deltaE}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
F_i^a
:=
\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\partial_i m^a
-\beta_X n^a\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon.
}
\label{eq:callback_F}
\end{equation}

Thus the effective nonlinear PDE contribution is the Euler--Lagrange derivative of \(\delta\mathcal E_{II}\) with respect to \(\Psi^\dagger\).

\section{4. Variational derivative: explicit solver-ready formula}

Varying \(m^a\), \(\rho_\varepsilon\), and \(n^a=m^a/\rho_\varepsilon\) gives
\[
\delta m^a = \delta\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi,
\qquad
\delta\rho_\varepsilon=\delta\Psi^\dagger\Psi,
\qquad
\delta n^a
=
\delta\Psi^\dagger
\frac{(T^a-n^a\mathbf 1)\Psi}{\rho_\varepsilon}.
\]

From \eqref{eq:callback_F}, one finds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta F_i^a
=
(\partial_i\delta\Psi^\dagger)\,A^a
+
\delta\Psi^\dagger\,B_i^a,
}
\label{eq:callback_dF}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)T^a\Psi
-
\beta_X n^a\Psi,
}
\label{eq:callback_A}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_i^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)T^a(\partial_i\Psi)
-
\beta_X n^a(\partial_i\Psi)
-
\beta_X
\frac{(T^a-n^a\mathbf 1)\Psi}{\rho_\varepsilon}\,
\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon.
}
\label{eq:callback_B}
\end{equation}

Now
\begin{align}
\delta \mathcal E_{II}
&=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
F_i^a\,\delta F_i^a
\nonumber\\
&=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
F_i^a
\Bigl[
(\partial_i\delta\Psi^\dagger)A^a
+
\delta\Psi^\dagger B_i^a
\Bigr].
\end{align}

After integrating by parts,
\begin{equation}
\delta \mathcal E_{II}
=
\int d^3x\;
\delta\Psi^\dagger\,
\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi],
\end{equation}
with the explicit working callback
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\left[
\partial_i\!\bigl(F_i^a A^a\bigr)
-
F_i^a B_i^a
\right].
}
\label{eq:callback_G_final}
\end{equation}

This is the actual formula inserted into the upgraded Phase-I solver.

\section{5. Final stationary PDE used by the solver}

The actual working stationary PDE therefore becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
=
0,
}
\label{eq:callback_stationary_full}
\end{equation}
with \(\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]\) given explicitly by \eqref{eq:callback_G_final}.

The pseudo-time relaxation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_\tau\Psi
=
\mu^2\Psi
-Z\nabla^2\Psi
+Y\nabla^4\Psi
+\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
+\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
-\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi].
}
\label{eq:callback_relax}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Why this is the correct working callback}

This callback is not arbitrary.

First, it is the direct nonlinear promotion of the explicit Class II mediator elimination already isolated in the notes:
\[
\delta N_{ij}^{\,b}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C_{ij}^{ab},
\]
which is exactly the mechanism that renormalizes the shell witness triple.

Second, the shell-level coefficient dictionary already fixed in the notes,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\]
is the downstream projected consequence of this same Class II route.

Third, the notes explicitly state that the remaining microscopic task is the actual evaluation of the background prefactors and overlap integrals in the actual defect background.
So the correct next step is indeed to run the actual solver with the strongest explicit Class II working callback, not to redesign the model again.

\section{7. Honest status}

The formula \eqref{eq:callback_G_final} should be interpreted correctly.

It is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the strongest explicit solver-ready working Class II callback.}
}
\]

It is not yet:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the final unique unconditional constitutive completion of TECT.}
}
\]

That stronger step would require the full constitutive insertion of the background coefficient fields
\[
Z^0(P),\quad
Z^i(P),\quad
M_0(P),\quad
A_i^a(P),\quad
B_{ij}^a(P),\quad
C_i^a(P),\quad
D_{ij}^a(P),
\]
into the full microscopic operator skeleton.

But at the present stage, this is exactly the correct object to freeze and run.

\section{8. Code-level dictionary}

The upgraded solver implements the following code-level map:

\[
\textbt{rho = Psi^\dagger Psi + eps}
\]
\[
\textbt{m[a] = Psi^\dagger T[a] Psi}
\]
\[
\textbt{n[a] = m[a] / rho}
\]
\[
\textbt{F_i[a] = (alphaX+betaX) d_i m[a] - betaX n[a] d_i rho}
\]
\[
\textbt{A[a] = (alphaX+betaX) T[a] Psi - betaX n[a] Psi}
\]
\[
\textbt{B_i[a] = (alphaX+betaX) T[a] d_i Psi - betaX n[a] d_i Psi
- betaX ((T[a]-n[a] I) Psi / rho)\, d_i rho}
\]
\[
\textbt{G = (1/MX2) \sum_{i,a} [ d_i(F_i[a] A[a]) - F_i[a] B_i[a] ]}.
\]

This is the exact working dictionary used in the file
\[
\text{tect\_phase1\_actual\_solver\_with\_classII.py}.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The missing model-specific ingredient of the Phase-I actual solver has now been fixed.

Starting from the strongest explicit microscopic Class II branch
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[P,\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\Psi],
\]
we promoted the shell/current sector to a local \(\Psi\)-only realization
\[
m^a=\Psi^\dagger T^a\Psi,
\qquad
\rho_\varepsilon=\Psi^\dagger\Psi+\varepsilon,
\qquad
n^a=\frac{m^a}{\rho_\varepsilon},
\]
\[
J_i^a=\partial_i m^a,
\qquad
K_i^a=\rho_\varepsilon\partial_i n^a.
\]

Eliminating the heavy mediator yields
\[
\delta\mathcal E_{II}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}F_i^aF_i^a,
\qquad
F_i^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)\partial_i m^a
-\beta_X n^a\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon.
\]

The resulting explicit working callback inserted into the actual solver is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\left[
\partial_i(F_i^aA^a)-F_i^aB_i^a
\right],
}
\]
with
\[
A^a=(\alpha_X+\beta_X)T^a\Psi-\beta_X n^a\Psi,
\]
\[
B_i^a
=
(\alpha_X+\beta_X)T^a(\partial_i\Psi)
-\beta_X n^a(\partial_i\Psi)
-\beta_X\frac{(T^a-n^a\mathbf1)\Psi}{\rho_\varepsilon}\partial_i\rho_\varepsilon.
\]

This is not yet the final unconditional constitutive completion of TECT.
But it is the strongest explicit solver-ready Class II callback presently justified by the working-branch derivations.

Therefore the actual Phase-I PDE is now frozen in explicit code-ready form:
\[
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi
-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi
+\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
=
0.
\]

\section{First Sanity Run of the Phase-I Actual Solver}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

A first explicit sanity run of the actual-branch solver was carried out.

The important conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the solver and the explicit working Class II callback are numerically executable,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the run does not yet converge to an accepted intended-BCC branch.}
}
\]

This is already useful, because it identifies the real bottleneck:
the main failure mode in the present run is not one-patch collapse, but loss of concentration on the intended BCC shell.

\section{1. Run status}

The reduced sanity run gave
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{accepted}=\mathrm{False}.
}
\]

At the final recorded step,
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_step}\approx 1.8219\times 10^{-2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 8.9487\times 10^{-1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 9.6610\times 10^{-2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 7.6253\times 10^{-1}.
}
\]

So the branch is neither stationary enough nor sufficiently concentrated on the intended shell to be accepted.

\section{2. What failed and what did not fail}

The shell-fraction history was
\[
0.3443 \;\to\; 0.2816 \;\to\; 0.2058 \;\to\; 0.1435 \;\to\; 0.0966.
\]

Thus the converged flow is drifting away from the intended BCC shell sector.

However, the orbit-balance indicator remained approximately constant:
\[
0.7621,\ 0.7622,\ 0.7623,\ 0.7624,\ 0.7625.
\]

Therefore the present bottleneck is not dominant one-patch collapse.
Instead, the dominant failure is shell leakage.

\section{3. Immediate diagnosis: shell mismatch in the initial condition}

The current test configuration used
\[
Z=-1,\qquad Y=1,\qquad q_0=1.
\]

But the linear stiff sector
\[
L(k)=\mu^2 - Z(-|k|^2)+Y|k|^4
\]
has its preferred finite shell at
\[
\frac{d}{d(|k|^2)}\bigl[-Z|k|^2+Y|k|^4\bigr]=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
|k|^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y}.
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y}=\frac12,
\qquad
q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}\approx 0.70710678.
}
\]

So the current run was initialized on a shell
\[
q_0=1
\]
that does not coincide with the linearly preferred shell
\[
q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
\]

This immediately explains why the shell fraction decays during relaxation:
the branch is being pulled toward the wrong shell from the outset.

\section{4. Correct next move}

The solver itself should not be redesigned.

The next run should keep the same solver and the same explicit Class II callback, but must enforce
\[
\boxed{
q_0=q_*=\sqrt{-\frac{Z}{2Y}}.
}
\]

For the current coefficients \(Z=-1\), \(Y=1\), this means
\[
\boxed{
q_0=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
}
\]

Only after this shell matching should we interpret the shell-fraction diagnostic as a genuine branch failure rather than a setup mismatch.

\section{5. Operational interpretation}

The present run already established something nontrivial:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit working Class II callback is numerically runnable;
\item the pseudo-spectral relaxation pipeline is stable enough to produce interpretable diagnostics;
\item the current dominant bottleneck is shell retention, not orbit collapse;
\item the immediate cause of shell loss is a mismatch between the seeded shell \(q_0\) and the linear preferred shell \(q_*\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the correct next step is not another theory detour.
It is a matched-shell rerun.

\section{Final Summary}

A first explicit sanity run of the actual Phase-I solver was completed.

The run did not yet yield an accepted intended-BCC branch:
\[
\texttt{accepted}=\mathrm{False},
\qquad
\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 8.95\times 10^{-1},
\qquad
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 9.66\times 10^{-2}.
\]

The shell fraction decayed strongly during relaxation, while the orbit-balance indicator remained stable near \(0.76\).
Thus the dominant failure mode is shell leakage rather than one-patch collapse.

The immediate reason is that the seeded shell \(q_0=1\) was inconsistent with the linearly preferred finite shell:
\[
q_*=\sqrt{-\frac{Z}{2Y}}=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}
\qquad
\text{for } Z=-1,\ Y=1.
\]

Therefore the solver itself should now be frozen and reused without redesign.
The next nonredundant step is the matched-shell rerun
\[
\boxed{
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
}
\]

Only after that rerun can shell loss be interpreted as a genuine branch obstruction rather than a setup mismatch.

\section{Matched-Shell Rerun of the Phase-I Actual Solver}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

A matched-shell rerun was performed with
\[
q_0=q_*=\sqrt{-\frac{Z}{2Y}}=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
keeping the same solver, the same explicit working Class II callback, and the same branch-construction logic.

This rerun is decisive because it separates two possibilities:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the previous shell leakage was merely caused by a mismatch \(q_0\neq q_*\);
\item the deeper problem is that the present working Class II flow itself does not preserve the intended BCC branch.
\end{enumerate}

The result supports the second interpretation.

\section{1. Matched-shell run data}

For
\[
Z=-1,\qquad Y=1,
\]
the preferred linear shell is
\[
\boxed{
q_*=\sqrt{-\frac{Z}{2Y}}=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}\approx 0.707106781187.
}
\]

The rerun used exactly this shell in the initial condition:
\[
\boxed{
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
}
\]

The final diagnostics were
\[

\texttt{accepted}=\mathrm{False},

}

\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 8.17295744114\times 10^{-1},
}

}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 4.21250452902\times 10^{-1}.
}
\]

Thus the branch still fails the intended-BCC acceptance test.

\section{2. Time history}

The shell-fraction history in the matched-shell rerun was
\[
0.07355 \to 0.07023 \to 0.06369 \to 0.05708 \to 0.05082.
\]

So even when the seed is placed directly on the linearly preferred shell, the relaxation still drives the solution away from the intended BCC shell sector.

Hence the branch is not only leaking away from the shell, but also becoming less balanced across the BCC orbit directions.

\section{3. Comparison with the previous sanity run}

The previous run (with \(q_0=1\)) ended near
\[
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 0.0966,
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.7625.
\]

The matched-shell rerun ended near
\[
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 0.0508,
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.4213.
\]

Therefore the matched-shell correction did not cure the branch loss.
If anything, the intended-BCC diagnostics became worse.

\section{4. Interpretation}

This result has a clear meaning.

The hypothesis
\[
\boxed{
\text{``the dominant problem was simply }q_0\neq q_*\text{''}
}
\]
is insufficient.

The actual bottleneck is now better identified as:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the present explicit working Class II callback, together with the current seed protocol, does not preserve the intended BCC shell branch under relaxation.}
}
\]

So the solver infrastructure is not the issue.
The accepted diagnosis is instead:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the solver is numerically runnable;
\item the explicit Class II callback is numerically stable enough to evolve;
\item the present flow does not yet stabilize the intended BCC branch.
\end{enumerate}

\section{5. Consequence for the project plan}

This means the next step is not another shell-value tweak.
The next step must change the branch-preservation mechanism itself.

Concretely, there are now only two meaningful possibilities:

\paragraph{(A) Improve the flow around the same PDE.}
Keep the PDE and callback fixed, but replace the naive initial data by an orbit-symmetric projected seed that enforces the \(2+2+8\) BCC orbit content more rigidly during relaxation.

\paragraph{(B) Improve the actual working Class II constitutive callback.}
Keep the solver fixed, but refine \(\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]\) so that it reproduces the shell-level stabilizing structure that was already derived in the reduced shell-amplitude system.

The present matched-shell test shows that option (A) alone may not be enough, but it is still the cheapest next probe before altering the constitutive callback.

\section{6. Honest project status after this run}

The correct status is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Phase-I solver: alive,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{explicit working Class II callback: executable,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{accepted intended-BCC actual branch: not yet obtained.}
}
\]

So the real bottleneck is finally visible.
It is no longer a vague conceptual obstruction.
It is a specific branch-preservation failure of the current working actual PDE realization.

\section{Final Summary}

A matched-shell rerun was carried out with
\[
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
using the same solver and the same explicit working Class II callback.

The result was still
\[
\texttt{accepted}=\mathrm{False},
\]
with final diagnostics
\[
\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 8.17\times 10^{-1},
\qquad
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 5.08\times 10^{-2},
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 4.21\times 10^{-1}.
\]

Thus the previous shell leakage cannot be explained solely by the mismatch \(q_0\neq q_*\).
The deeper bottleneck is that the current explicit working Class II flow does not preserve the intended BCC branch under relaxation.

This is an important clarification.
The solver is not broken, and the obstruction is no longer vague.
It is now localized to the branch-preservation properties of the present working actual PDE realization.

So the next nonredundant step is not another shell-value tweak.
It is to strengthen the BCC branch-preserving mechanism, either through a more rigid orbit-symmetric seed protocol or through a refined Class II constitutive callback.

\section{Numerical Diagnosis: The Main Problem Is Fourier-Box Incommensurability}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The present solver failure should not yet be interpreted as a genuine physical nonexistence of the intended BCC branch.

There is a more basic numerical inconsistency:
the seeded BCC shell wavevectors are not commensurate with the periodic Fourier box.
Therefore the initial condition is not an exact discrete Fourier mode of the simulation domain, which causes immediate spectral leakage.

Until this is fixed, the shell-fraction diagnostic is not a clean physical criterion.

\section{1. Periodic box Fourier condition}

On the periodic cube
\[
\Omega_L=[-L/2,L/2)^3,
\]
the exact Fourier lattice is
\[
\boxed{
k=\frac{2\pi}{L}(n_x,n_y,n_z),
\qquad
n_x,n_y,n_z\in\mathbb Z.
}
\]

So if one seeds a plane wave
\[
e^{iq\cdot x},
\]
then for it to be an exact mode of the box, every Cartesian component of \(q\) must satisfy
\[
\boxed{
q_j=\frac{2\pi}{L}n_j.
}
\]

\section{2. BCC first-shell commensurability condition}

The target BCC shell directions are
\[
\hat k_\alpha\in
\left\{
\frac{(\pm1,\pm1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(\pm1,0,\pm1)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(0,\pm1,\pm1)}{\sqrt2}
\right\}.
\]

Thus a shell vector is
\[
q_\alpha=q_0\hat k_\alpha.
\]

For example, for
\[
\hat k=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\]
the Cartesian components are
\[
q_x=q_y=\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2},
\qquad
q_z=0.
\]

Hence exact periodicity requires
\[
\boxed{
\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}=\frac{2\pi}{L}m,
\qquad
m\in\mathbb Z.
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
q_0=\frac{2\sqrt2\,\pi}{L}m.
}
\]

This is the exact commensurability condition for the first BCC shell on a periodic box.

\section{3. Why the present runs were inconsistent}

\subsection{Run 1: \(q_0=1\), \(L=16\)}
Then
\[
\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}\approx 0.70710678.
\]
But the Fourier spacing is
\[
\frac{2\pi}{L}=\frac{\pi}{8}\approx 0.39269908.
\]
The ratio is
\[
\frac{q_0/\sqrt2}{2\pi/L}
=
\frac{0.70710678}{0.39269908}
\approx 1.80063,
\]
which is not an integer.

So the seeded BCC shell is not an exact box mode.

\subsection{Run 2: matched-shell \(q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}\), \(L=16\)}
Now
\[
\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}
=
\frac{1/\sqrt2}{\sqrt2}
=
\frac12.
\]
Again
\[
\frac{2\pi}{L}=\frac{\pi}{8}\approx 0.39269908,
\]
so
\[
\frac{q_0/\sqrt2}{2\pi/L}
=
\frac{0.5}{0.39269908}
\approx 1.27324,
\]
which is still not an integer.

Therefore the matched-shell rerun also seeded a noncommensurate shell.

\section{4. Consequence for the shell-fraction diagnostic}

Because the initial field is not built from exact discrete Fourier modes of the box, its power is spread over nearby lattice modes from the very beginning.
This creates artificial shell leakage before the nonlinear dynamics has had any chance to decide the physical branch.

This is exactly what we observed numerically:
the shell fraction was already small at the earliest recorded step.

Thus the present low values of
\[
f_{\rm shell}
\]
cannot yet be interpreted as proof that the physical BCC branch is dynamically absent.

\section{5. What the current diagnostics do tell us}

The diagnostics still separate two effects:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the solver itself is stable enough to evolve and report meaningful residuals;
\item the orbit-balance indicator does not immediately collapse to zero, so the run is not suffering from pure one-patch blow-up;
\item however, the shell-fraction indicator is contaminated by box-shell incommensurability.
\end{enumerate}

So the correct conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the present run is numerically inconclusive about the actual BCC branch.}
}
\]

\section{6. Correct fix: two equivalent options}

\subsection{Option A: keep \(q_*=1/\sqrt2\), change the box}

If one insists on
\[
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
then exact commensurability requires
\[
\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}=\frac12=\frac{2\pi}{L}m
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\boxed{
L=4\pi m.
}
\]

Examples:
\[
L=4\pi\approx 12.56637,
\qquad
L=8\pi\approx 25.13274,
\qquad
L=12\pi\approx 37.69911.
\]

\subsection{Option B: keep the box, change the shell}

If one keeps
\[
L=16,
\]
then the commensurate BCC shell values are
\[
\boxed{
q_0=\frac{2\sqrt2\,\pi}{16}m
=
\frac{\sqrt2\,\pi}{8}m
\approx 0.55536\,m.
}
\]

The first two are
\[
q_0^{(1)}\approx 0.55536,
\qquad
q_0^{(2)}\approx 1.11072.
\]

Then one should tune the linear coefficients so that
\[
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y}=q_0^2.
\]
For example, with \(Y=1\) and \(q_0=q_0^{(1)}\),
\[
\boxed{
Z=-2q_0^2\approx -0.61685.
}
\]

\section{7. Best immediate protocol}

The cleanest next test is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item choose a commensurate box-shell pair \((L,q_0)\);
\item build the initial BCC seed from exact discrete Fourier lattice modes only;
\item then rerun the same solver and the same Class II callback;
\item only after that interpret shell-fraction decay as a real branch-preservation failure.
\end{enumerate}

In short:
\[
\boxed{
\text{fix commensurability first, then judge the physics.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

Yes, there is a genuine numerical setup problem.

The dominant issue is not generic floating-point instability but Fourier-box incommensurability:
the seeded BCC shell was not an exact periodic Fourier mode of the simulation box.

For a periodic cubic box of size \(L\), exact BCC first-shell commensurability requires
\[
\boxed{
\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}=\frac{2\pi}{L}m,\qquad m\in\mathbb Z.
}
\]

Neither of the previous test runs satisfied this condition:
\[
(L,q_0)=(16,1)
\quad\text{and}\quad
(L,q_0)=\left(16,\frac{1}{\sqrt2}\right)
\]
are both noncommensurate.

Therefore the observed shell leakage is numerically contaminated from the start and cannot yet be interpreted as a genuine physical failure of the intended BCC branch.

The correct immediate fix is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{enforce exact box-shell commensurability before drawing any physical conclusion.}
}
\]

The cleanest choice is
\[
\boxed{
L=4\pi m,\qquad q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
}
\]
for some integer \(m\).

\section{First Truly Commensurate Actual-Branch Run}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

A decisive numerical test has now been completed.

Previously, the intended BCC shell was not commensurate with the periodic Fourier box, so shell-fraction decay could not be interpreted physically.
That ambiguity has now been removed.

We performed the first truly commensurate run with
\[
\boxed{
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
}
\]

This run shows that the dominant pathology of the earlier tests was indeed numerical in origin.
The shell fraction is now preserved at \(O(1)\), so the BCC shell itself is no longer being destroyed immediately by the box geometry.

The remaining bottleneck is now clearly shifted to actual relaxation/stationarity and orbit-level stabilization.

\section{1. Exact commensurability}

For a periodic box of size \(L\), exact Fourier modes satisfy
\[
k_j=\frac{2\pi}{L}n_j,\qquad n_j\in\mathbb Z.
\]

For the first BCC shell, a representative direction is
\[
\hat k=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\]
so exact commensurability requires
\[
\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}=\frac{2\pi}{L}m.
\]

With
\[
L=4\pi,\qquad q_0=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
we have
\[
\frac{q_0}{\sqrt2}
=
\frac{1/\sqrt2}{\sqrt2}
=
\frac12
=
\frac{2\pi}{4\pi},
\]
so the shell is exactly commensurate with the box.
This is the first run in which the intended BCC shell is represented by exact box Fourier modes.

\section{2. Numerical outcome}

The run used the same solver and the same explicit working Class II callback as before, changing only the commensurate box-shell pair.

The final diagnostics were
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{accepted}=\mathrm{False},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_step}\approx 1.62788483653\times 10^{-2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 7.80395221121\times 10^{-1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 6.09875844173\times 10^{-1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 4.69634534562\times 10^{-1}.
}
\]

Thus the run is not yet an accepted actual branch, but it is qualitatively different from the previous noncommensurate runs.

\section{3. Comparison with the previous matched-shell noncommensurate run}

In the previous run, the shell value \(q_0=q_*=1/\sqrt2\) was used, but the box size \(L=16\) was noncommensurate.
That run ended near
\[
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 5.08\times 10^{-2},
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 4.21\times 10^{-1}.
\]

The new commensurate run ends near
\[
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 6.10\times 10^{-1},
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 4.70\times 10^{-1}.
\]

So the shell fraction improved by more than an order of magnitude:
\[
\boxed{
0.0508 \;\longrightarrow\; 0.6099.
}
\]

This is the decisive numerical evidence that the earlier shell leakage was dominated by Fourier-box incommensurability.

\section{4. What is now fixed, and what is still open}

The commensurability problem is now fixed.

Therefore the present run can be interpreted more honestly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the intended BCC shell is no longer being artificially destroyed by the periodic box;
\item the explicit working Class II flow can preserve a substantial shell fraction;
\item the remaining failure of acceptance is not shell mismatch but insufficient stationarity and insufficient branch stabilization.
\end{enumerate}

In particular, the two remaining bottlenecks are
\[
\boxed{
\text{high residual/still-evolving flow}
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\text{orbit-level imbalance within the BCC sector.}
}
\]

\section{5. Consequence for the project}

This changes the interpretation of the actual-branch program.

Previously, the first question was:
\[
\text{``is the run numerically contaminated by box-shell mismatch?''}
\]

Now that question is closed.

The correct next question is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{can the commensurate flow be driven to a stationary BCC branch with better orbit symmetry?}
}
\]

That is now the real Phase-I bottleneck.

\section{6. Immediate next move}

The next nonredundant execution step is not another commensurability change.
It is one of the following two:

\begin{enumerate}
\item keep the same commensurate setup and run much longer / with adaptive damping to reduce
\[
\texttt{rel\_step},\ \texttt{rel\_residual};
\]
\item replace the current seed by a rigid \(2+2+8\) orbit-projected BCC seed, so that the relaxation starts closer to the intended orbit-symmetric branch.
\end{enumerate}

Since shell retention is now healthy, the second option is likely the more informative next probe.

\section{Final Summary}

A first truly commensurate actual-branch run has now been completed with
\[
\boxed{
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
}
\]

This removes the major numerical ambiguity present in the earlier runs:
the intended BCC shell is now represented by exact Fourier modes of the periodic box.

The decisive result is that the shell fraction is now preserved at
\[
\boxed{

instead of collapsing to \(O(10^{-2})\) as in the previous noncommensurate matched-shell run.

However, the run is still not accepted:

\qquad

\qquad
\texttt{rel\_step}\approx 0.0163,
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.470.

Therefore the project bottleneck has now moved.
It is no longer shell commensurability.
It is now the actual stabilization of a stationary orbit-symmetric BCC branch under the explicit working Class II flow.

The correct next step is to keep the commensurate setup fixed and improve branch stabilization, most naturally through a \(2+2+8\) orbit-projected seed.

\section{Commensurate Actual Run with a \(2+2+8\) Orbit-Projected Seed}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

A decisive numerical test has now been carried out on the actual-branch solver.

The setup was kept fixed at the first truly commensurate BCC-compatible choice
\[
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
and only the initial condition was changed.

Instead of the earlier equal-amplitude seed, we imposed a rigid orbit-projected \(2+2+8\) BCC decomposition:
\[
\mathcal A\ (2\ \text{axial}),
\qquad
\mathcal E\ (2\ \text{equatorial}),
\qquad
\mathcal O\ (8\ \text{oblique}),
\]
with slightly oblique-enhanced amplitudes at initialization.

The outcome is clear:
the shell is now preserved extremely well, but the orbit symmetry collapses strongly.
Hence the true bottleneck is no longer shell retention.
It is orbit stabilization within the BCC shell sector.

\section{1. Frozen commensurate setup}

The run used the exact box-shell commensurate choice
\[
\boxed{
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
}
\]

Thus the BCC shell vectors
\[
q_\alpha=q_0\hat k_\alpha,
\qquad
\hat k_\alpha\in
\left\{
\frac{(\pm1,\pm1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(\pm1,0,\pm1)}{\sqrt2},
\frac{(0,\pm1,\pm1)}{\sqrt2}
\right\}
\]
are represented by exact Fourier modes of the periodic box.

So, unlike the earlier noncommensurate runs, shell leakage is no longer contaminated by box mismatch.

\section{2. Orbit-projected seed}

Relative to the locking axis
\[
\hat n=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2},
\]
the 12 BCC directions split into the exact three orbits
\[
\mathcal A:\ c_\alpha^2=1 \quad (2\ \text{patches}),
\]
\[
\mathcal E:\ c_\alpha^2=0 \quad (2\ \text{patches}),
\]
\[
\mathcal O:\ c_\alpha^2=\frac14 \quad (8\ \text{patches}).
\]

The initial seed was taken in the rigid orbit form
\[
\Psi_{\rm init}(x)
=
z_0\Bigl(
\phi_A(x)+\phi_E(x)+\phi_O(x)+\varepsilon_{\rm def}\tanh(\kappa \xi)
\Bigr)
+\varepsilon_{\rm noise}\delta\Psi(x),
\]
with orbit amplitudes
\[
A_A=A_{\rm BCC},
\qquad
A_E=0.9\,A_{\rm BCC},
\qquad
A_O=1.1\,A_{\rm BCC}.
\]

So the seed was explicitly designed to resist axial-only collapse and to remain close to the intended orbit-symmetric branch.

\section{3. Numerical result}

The final diagnostics of the run were
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{accepted}=\mathrm{False},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_step}\approx 1.74706158951\times 10^{-2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 7.16146896885\times 10^{-1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 9.43013591291\times 10^{-1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 7.04925114141\times 10^{-2}.
}
\]

So the branch is still not accepted, but the pattern of failure is now completely different.

\section{4. Comparison with the previous commensurate run}

The previous commensurate run with the simpler seed gave approximately
\[
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 0.6099,
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.4696.
\]

The new orbit-projected run gives
\[
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 0.9430,
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.0705.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
0.6099 \;\longrightarrow\; 0.9430
}
\quad\text{for shell fraction,}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
0.4696 \;\longrightarrow\; 0.0705
}
\quad\text{for orbit balance.}
\]

This means the orbit-projected seed strongly stabilizes the shell radius but simultaneously drives the flow toward a highly orbit-imbalanced state.

\section{5. Time-history interpretation}

The shell fraction history remained high:
\[
0.9463 \to 0.9507 \to 0.9493 \to 0.9465 \to 0.9430.
\]

So there is no longer any serious shell leakage.

By contrast, the orbit-balance history remained very low:
\[
0.0726 \to 0.0719 \to 0.0713 \to 0.0708 \to 0.0705.
\]

Thus the evolution is not wandering away from the BCC shell.
It is remaining on the shell while concentrating unequally across the 12 BCC directions.

This is the sharpest diagnosis so far:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the current explicit Class II flow preserves the shell but does not preserve orbit democracy.}
}
\]

\section{6. What this proves}

This run proves three nontrivial things.

First,
\[
\boxed{
\text{the commensurate Fourier box is now correct.}
}
\]

Second,
\[
\boxed{
\text{the intended BCC shell can be retained dynamically at }O(1)\text{ weight.}
}
\]

Third,
\[
\boxed{
\text{the true remaining instability is orbit-level imbalance, not shell loss.}
}
\]

So the numerical bottleneck is now localized much more precisely than before.

\section{7. Consequence for the actual-branch program}

The project should now stop modifying shell scales or box geometry.
Those issues are already settled.

The next nonredundant task is to add an orbit-stabilizing mechanism while keeping the same commensurate setup and the same solver backbone.

Mathematically, the desired branch must satisfy both
\[
f_{\rm shell}\approx O(1)
\]
and
\[
\frac{\min_{\alpha\in\mathcal S_{12}} P_\alpha}{\max_{\alpha\in\mathcal S_{12}} P_\alpha}\not\ll 1.
\]

The current run satisfies the first but fails the second.

Therefore the next phase must target the second condition directly.

\section{8. Correct next move}

The cleanest next step is to keep
\[
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
fixed, and modify the relaxation by one of the following orbit-level controls:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an explicit weak orbit-balancing penalty in the pseudo-time flow,
\item a periodic orbit-projection step after each relaxation block,
\item a reduced \(r_A,r_E,r_O\) feedback rule imported from the shell-amplitude system.
\end{enumerate}

Among these, the most economical next test is a weak orbit-balancing penalty, because it changes only one term in the relaxation while preserving the same PDE backbone.

\section{Final Summary}

The commensurate actual-branch run with a rigid \(2+2+8\) orbit-projected seed has produced the clearest diagnosis so far.

The shell fraction is now extremely high:

so shell retention is no longer the dominant problem.

Thus the numerical bottleneck has now been sharply localized:

}
\]

This means the project has finally passed the shell-retention bottleneck.
The next step is to keep the same commensurate setup fixed and add an orbit-stabilizing mechanism to the relaxation.

So the immediate actual-branch frontier is now:
\[
\boxed{
\text{stationary orbit-symmetric BCC branch stabilization.}
}

\section{Commensurate Actual Run with Weak Orbit-Balancing Penalty}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

A decisive numerical improvement has now been achieved.

Keeping the same commensurate setup
\[
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
and the same explicit working Class II callback, we added only a weak orbit-balancing penalty at the 12 exact BCC shell modes.

This is not yet claimed as a new constitutive physical term in the PDE.
It is a numerical stabilization layer used only to test whether an orbit-symmetric BCC actual branch exists nearby.

The result is clear:
the flow now preserves both the shell and the orbit democracy very well.
The remaining obstruction is no longer branch geometry, but stationarity of the nonlinear PDE.

\section{1. Algorithmic change}

The solver step was modified as follows.

First, one performs the same semi-implicit pseudo-time PDE update:
\[
(1-\Delta\tau\,L)\Psi^{n+1/2}
=
\Psi^n+\Delta\tau\,N(\Psi^n),
\]
with
\[
L=\mu^2-Z\nabla^2+Y\nabla^4,
\qquad
N(\Psi)=\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi+\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi-\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi].
\]

Second, after this PDE step, one applies a weak shell-mode balancing map only on the 12 exact BCC shell coefficients:
\[
\widehat\Psi_\alpha
\;\longmapsto\;
\widehat\Psi_\alpha+\varepsilon_{\rm bal}
\bigl(\overline{\widehat\Psi}-\widehat\Psi_\alpha\bigr),
\qquad
\overline{\widehat\Psi}
=
\frac1{12}\sum_{\beta=1}^{12}\widehat\Psi_\beta,
\]
with
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm bal}=0.08.
\]

So this is a weak orbit-democracy restoring layer on top of the same commensurate Phase-I solver.

\section{2. Numerical outcome}

The final diagnostics of the run were
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{accepted}=\mathrm{False},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_step}\approx 1.73599104746\times 10^{-2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 7.24403020184\times 10^{-1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 9.19631539164\times 10^{-1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 9.01431631278\times 10^{-1}.
}
\]

Thus the run is still not accepted as a final actual branch, but the failure pattern has changed completely.

\section{3. Comparison with the previous orbit-projected run}

The previous commensurate run with only the rigid \(2+2+8\) orbit-projected seed gave
\[
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 0.9430,
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.0705.
\]

The new weak-penalty run gives
\[
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 0.9196,
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.9014.
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{shell retention remains excellent,}
}
\]
while
\[
\boxed{
\text{orbit democracy is now almost fully restored.}
}
\]

Numerically,
\[
0.0705 \;\longrightarrow\; 0.9014
\]
for the orbit-balance indicator.
This is the sharpest improvement obtained so far.

\section{4. Time-history interpretation}

The history tail shows:

\[
\texttt{shell\_fraction}:
0.9438 \to 0.9356 \to 0.9295 \to 0.9248 \to 0.9196,
\]
which remains stably \(O(1)\).

Meanwhile,
\[
\texttt{orbit\_balance}:
0.0897 \to 0.3086 \to 0.5879 \to 0.7897 \to 0.9014.
\]

So the weak balancing layer does not merely freeze the shell.
It actively drives the run toward a much more orbit-symmetric BCC branch.

This is the first run in which both major geometric diagnostics are simultaneously healthy:
\[
\boxed{
f_{\rm shell}\approx O(1),
\qquad
\text{orbit\_balance}\approx O(1).
}
\]

\section{5. What is now solved and what is not}

The following bottlenecks are now effectively removed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item box-shell incommensurability,
\item catastrophic shell leakage,
\item orbit-level collapse inside the retained BCC shell.
\end{enumerate}

The remaining obstruction is almost purely dynamical:
\[

}
\]
is still too large,
and
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_step}\approx 1.74\times 10^{-2}
}
\]
shows that the flow is still evolving.

So the accepted diagnosis is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the branch geometry is under control, but the PDE has not yet relaxed to a stationary fixed point.}
}
\]

\section{6. Honest status of the penalty layer}

This improvement must be described honestly.

The weak orbit-balancing step is currently an algorithmic stabilization device.
It is not yet claimed to be part of the final constitutive microscopic PDE.

Therefore the correct interpretation is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{there exists a nearby orbit-symmetric BCC branch candidate under the present working Class II flow,}
}
\end{equation}
but not yet
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{a final accepted actual branch of the unmodified constitutive PDE.}
}
\end{equation}

Still, this is a major success, because it proves that the project is no longer blocked by branch-geometry instability.

\section{7. Correct next step}

Since the shell and orbit diagnostics are now both healthy, the next nonredundant move is no longer geometric.

The next step must target residual reduction and stationarity:
\begin{enumerate}
\item longer relaxation runs,
\item adaptive time stepping,
\item possibly stronger semi-implicit damping for the stiff nonlinear sector,
\item grid refinement once the coarse-grid stationary trend is confirmed.
\end{enumerate}

In other words, the project has now entered the true fixed-point convergence phase of Phase I.

\section{Final Summary}

A commensurate actual-branch run with a weak orbit-balancing penalty has now produced the clearest numerical status so far.

\section{Staged-Damping Result: Geometry is Under Control, Residual Plateau is the Final Bottleneck}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The latest numerical run changes the status of the actual-branch program in an important way.

Keeping fixed:
\[
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
and using the same weak orbit-balancing penalty, we ran a longer staged-damping relaxation.

The outcome is decisive:
both the shell retention and the orbit symmetry are now excellent,
while the PDE residual remains stuck near a plateau of order \(10^{-1}\).

Therefore the project is no longer blocked by branch geometry.
It is now blocked almost purely by stationary PDE convergence.

\section{1. Setup}

The run used the same commensurate BCC-compatible setup:
\[
\boxed{
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
}
\]

The same \(2+2+8\) orbit-projected seed and the same weak shell-mode orbit-balancing layer were kept.
Only the time step was scheduled in stages:
\[
\Delta\tau:
0.008 \;\to\; 0.006 \;\to\; 0.004 \;\to\; 0.003.
\]

Thus the purpose of the run was not to alter branch geometry, but only to improve relaxation convergence.

\section{2. Final diagnostics}

The final state at step \(80\) gave
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{accepted}=\mathrm{False},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_step}\approx 5.256752\times 10^{-3},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 7.265510\times 10^{-1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 9.183939\times 10^{-1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 9.962593\times 10^{-1}.
}
\]

Hence the branch is still not accepted, but the reason is now highly localized.

\section{3. What has now been effectively solved}

The run shows that the following difficulties are no longer dominant:

\paragraph{(i) Box-shell mismatch.}
This was already eliminated by the commensurate choice \(L=4\pi\), \(q_0=1/\sqrt2\).

\paragraph{(ii) Shell leakage.}
The shell fraction remains stably large:
\[
0.9355,\ 0.9307,\ 0.9280,\ 0.9255,\ 0.9236,\ 0.9216,\ 0.9200,\ 0.9184.
\]

So the branch stays on the intended BCC shell.

\paragraph{(iii) Orbit collapse.}
The orbit-balance indicator improves monotonically:
\[
0.3089 \to 0.5882 \to 0.7900 \to 0.9016 \to 0.9558 \to 0.9805 \to 0.9914 \to 0.9963.
\]

Thus the branch also becomes nearly perfectly orbit-symmetric within the retained shell.

Therefore the geometric part of the actual-branch search is now effectively under control.

\section{4. The true remaining bottleneck}

In sharp contrast, the residual does not decay toward zero:
\[
0.7102,\ 0.6947,\ 0.7018,\ 0.7099,\ 0.7152,\ 0.7200,\ 0.7234,\ 0.7266.
\]

So the flow approaches a shell-preserving, orbit-symmetric state, but not a true stationary solution of the present PDE.
The relative step does decrease,
\[
0.0151 \to 0.0145 \to 0.0108 \to 0.0106 \to 0.00708 \to 0.00704 \to 0.00527 \to 0.00526,
\]
but this only indicates numerical slowing, not actual PDE satisfaction.

Hence the correct diagnosis is now:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the run is approaching a stabilized quasi-branch, but not yet a true stationary PDE fixed point.}
}
\]

\section{5. Interpretation}

This result has two possible explanations.

\paragraph{Possibility A: constitutive mismatch.}
The current explicit working Class II callback
\[
\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi]
\]
may still differ in an essential way from the actual constitutive term required by the intended microscopic branch.
Then the flow can preserve the right shell and orbit geometry without satisfying the true stationary Euler--Lagrange condition.

\paragraph{Possibility B: algorithmic projection artifact.}
The weak orbit-balancing penalty may stabilize a nearby orbit-symmetric branch candidate that is not itself a stationary solution of the unmodified PDE.
Then the penalty helps reveal the nearby branch geometry, but not the true physical fixed point.

In either case, the obstruction is now no longer geometric.
It is a stationary residual obstruction.

\section{6. Correct project status after this run}

The actual-branch program has now reached the following precise status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{shell-retaining BCC branch candidate: yes,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{orbit-symmetric BCC branch candidate: yes,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{accepted stationary PDE solution: not yet.}
}
\]

This is a major narrowing of the frontier.

\section{7. Correct next step}

Because the geometry is now under control, the next nonredundant task is no longer to tune shell or orbit mechanisms.

The next step must directly attack the residual plateau:
\begin{enumerate}
\item remove or soften the penalty after the orbit-symmetric branch has formed, and see whether the branch remains nearby;
\item compare the residual with and without the penalty on the same branch;
\item refine the explicit Class II callback so that the branch geometry and the stationary PDE condition become compatible;
\item only after that attempt longer / finer-grid acceptance runs.
\end{enumerate}

The key point is that the frontier has shifted from branch discovery to constitutive/stationary compatibility.

\section{Final Summary}

The staged-damping run has now isolated the actual bottleneck of the Phase-I program.

With the commensurate setup
\[
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
together with the weak orbit-balancing stabilization, the numerical branch satisfies

\[

\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.9963.
}
\]

So the solver now successfully preserves both the BCC shell and the orbit democracy.
This means the branch-geometry bottlenecks are effectively solved.

However, the residual remains stuck near
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 0.7266,
}
\]
while the relative step only decreases to
\[
\texttt{rel\_step}\approx 5.26\times 10^{-3}.
\]

Therefore the remaining obstruction is no longer geometric.
It is the mismatch between the presently stabilized branch and a true stationary solution of the nonlinear PDE.

The correct current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{orbit-symmetric BCC branch candidate: found,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{accepted stationary actual branch: not yet found.}
}
\]

Hence the next step must attack the residual plateau directly, rather than further modifying shell or orbit geometry.

\section{Penalty Continuation Test: The Orbit-Symmetric BCC Branch Persists Without Penalty}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

A continuation test was performed in which the weak orbit-balancing penalty was gradually turned off while keeping the same commensurate setup
\[

The result is decisive:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-retaining, orbit-symmetric BCC branch does not disappear when the penalty is removed;
\item however, the PDE residual does not relax toward zero and instead drifts upward slightly.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the penalty should now be interpreted as a basin-entry device, not as the source of the branch itself.

\section{Residual Decomposition: The Plateau is Dominated by the Linear Sector}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The residual decomposition has now isolated the true source of the plateau.

On the final unpenalized continuation branch candidate, the relative residual norms are:
\[
\boxed{
\|R_{\rm tot}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 0.7322,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\|R_{\rm lin}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 0.7577,
\qquad
\|R_{\rm loc}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 0.0341,
\qquad
\|R_{\rm Class\,II}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 1.18\times 10^{-5}.
}
\]

Thus the plateau is not dominated by the Class II constitutive term.
It is dominated almost entirely by the linear shell operator.

\section{1. Residual decomposition}

The stationary PDE residual was decomposed as
\[
R[\Psi]
=
R_{\rm lin}+R_{\rm loc}+R_{\rm Class\,II},
\]
with
\[
R_{\rm lin}
=
-\mu^2\Psi+Z\nabla^2\Psi-Y\nabla^4\Psi,
\]
\[
R_{\rm loc}
=
-\lambda |\Psi|^2\Psi-\gamma |\Psi|^4\Psi,
\]
\[
R_{\rm Class\,II}
=
\mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi].
\]

At the final unpenalized continuation state, we found
\[
\|R_{\rm lin}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 0.7577,
\]
\[
\|R_{\rm loc}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 0.0341,
\]
\[
\|R_{\rm Class\,II}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 1.18\times 10^{-5},
\]
while
\[
\|R_{\rm tot}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 0.7322.
\]

Therefore the residual plateau is overwhelmingly linear-sector dominated.

\section{2. Shell-marginality check}

For a shell mode
\[
\Psi\sim e^{iq\cdot x},
\]
the linear operator contributes
\[
\nabla^2\Psi=-q^2\Psi,
\qquad
\nabla^4\Psi=q^4\Psi,
\]
so
\[
R_{\rm lin}
=
\Bigl(
-\mu^2-Zq^2-Yq^4
\Bigr)\Psi.
\]

The present commensurate actual-branch setup uses
\[
Z=-1,
\qquad
Y=1,
\qquad
q_*= \sqrt{-\frac{Z}{2Y}}=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}.
\]

Hence
\[
q_*^2=\frac12,
\qquad
q_*^4=\frac14,
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\rm lin}(q_*)
=
-\mu^2+\frac14.
}
\]

With the current skeleton choice
\[
\mu^2=1,
\]
this gives
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\rm lin}(q_*)=-\frac34=-0.75.
}
\]

This agrees strikingly with the observed residual scale
\[
\|R_{\rm lin}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 0.7577.
\]

So the plateau is not mysterious.
It is the direct consequence of a shell-mass mismatch in the linear sector.

\section{3. Immediate consequence}

To make the preferred shell marginal at linear order, one must impose
\[
\mathcal L_{\rm lin}(q_*)=0.
\]

This yields
\[
-\mu^2+\frac14=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\boxed{
\mu^2=\frac14.
}
\]

Equivalently, in the general \((Z,Y,q_*)\) notation,
\[
\boxed{
\mu^2
=
-Zq_*^2-Yq_*^4.
}
\]

For the present fixed values \(Z=-1\), \(Y=1\), \(q_*=1/\sqrt2\), this is exactly
\[
\boxed{
\mu^2_{\rm crit}=\frac14.
}
\]

\section{4. Interpretation}

This changes the project diagnosis substantially.

Previously, the residual plateau seemed to suggest a possible incompatibility between the current explicit Class II callback and the stationary PDE.

But the actual decomposition shows:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the dominant obstruction is not } \mathcal G^{(II)}[\Psi],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{it is the arbitrary skeleton choice } \mu^2=1.
}
\]

Thus the next move is not to redesign the Class II constitutive callback.
It is to retune the linear mass parameter so that the retained BCC shell is actually marginal at linear order.

\section{5. Updated project status}

The actual Phase-I status is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{commensurate shell retention: solved,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{orbit-symmetric branch survival: solved,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{residual plateau source: identified,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{remaining task: linear mass retuning } \mu^2\to \mu^2_{\rm crit}.
}
\]

So the bottleneck is no longer vague and no longer geometric.
It is a single scalar mismatch in the linear sector.

\section{6. Correct next step}

The immediate nonredundant next computation is therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\mu^2: 1 \;\longrightarrow\; \frac14
}
\]
with all other ingredients frozen:
\[
L=4\pi,\qquad q_0=q_*=\frac1{\sqrt2},
\qquad
Z=-1,\qquad Y=1,
\]
and the same continuation branch protocol.

Only after that retuned run should we re-evaluate whether the stationary actual branch is reached.

\section{Final Summary}

The residual plateau has now been cleanly diagnosed.

On the final unpenalized continuation branch candidate,
\[
\|R_{\rm tot}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 0.7322,
\]
but the decomposition shows
\[
\boxed{
\|R_{\rm lin}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 0.7577,
\qquad
\|R_{\rm loc}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 0.0341,
\qquad
\|R_{\rm Class\,II}\|_{\rm rel}\approx 1.18\times 10^{-5}.
}
\]

Therefore the plateau is dominated almost entirely by the linear sector.

For the retained shell
\[
q_*=\frac1{\sqrt2},
\]
with
\[
Z=-1,\qquad Y=1,
\]
the linear shell coefficient is
\[
\mathcal L_{\rm lin}(q_*)=-\mu^2+\frac14.
\]

The present skeleton choice \(\mu^2=1\) therefore gives
\[
\mathcal L_{\rm lin}(q_*)=-\frac34,
\]
which matches the observed plateau scale.

So the next step is now sharply determined:
\[
\boxed{
\mu^2 \to \mu^2_{\rm crit}=\frac14.
}
\]

The project is no longer blocked by shell geometry, orbit symmetry, or an obviously dominant Class II inconsistency.
The remaining obstruction is a linear mass mismatch in the actual solver skeleton.

\section{Linear-Sector Retuning Test in the Actual Branch Program}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

A light but decisive continuation comparison was carried out on the actual-branch solver.

The setup was kept fixed at the commensurate BCC-compatible values
\[
L=4\pi,
\qquad
q_0=q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
together with the same penalty-continuation schedule.
Only the linear mass parameter was changed:
\[
\mu^2:1\longrightarrow \frac14.
\]

The result confirms that the previously identified shell-marginality diagnosis was correct.

\section{1. Why \texorpdfstring{$\mu^2=\frac14$}{mu2=1/4} is the critical value}

For a shell mode
\[
\Psi\sim e^{iq\cdot x},
\]
the linear stationary operator contributes
\[
R_{\rm lin}
=
-\mu^2\Psi+Z\nabla^2\Psi-Y\nabla^4\Psi
=
\bigl(-\mu^2-Zq^2-Yq^4\bigr)\Psi.
\]

With the frozen solver values
\[
Z=-1,\qquad Y=1,
\qquad q_*= \sqrt{-\frac{Z}{2Y}}=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
we have
\[
q_*^2=\frac12,
\qquad
q_*^4=\frac14.
\]

Hence the shell-marginality condition
\[
-\mu^2-Zq_*^2-Yq_*^4=0
\]
becomes
\[
-\mu^2+\frac12-\frac14=0,
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\mu^2_{\rm crit}=\frac14.
}
\]

Thus \(\mu^2=\frac14\) is not an arbitrary retune.
It is the unique linear value that makes the retained shell marginal.

\section{2. Continuation comparison}

\qquad\text{versus}\qquad

\to

\to

\qquad

\section{3. Main conclusion}

for the total residual, and

\boxed{

0.9264 \to 0.9261,

\section{4. Updated bottleneck diagnosis}
