\section{Exact Reduced Program for the Rigorous Extraction of the Backend Numbers}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now stop the broad numerical scan of the backend point
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)
\]
and replace it by a finite analytic extraction program.

The key idea is to move from a direct search in the PDE parameter space
to an exact reduced shell-amplitude theory induced by the Class II \(X\)-sector.
The remaining numerical task must then be only the finite evaluation of a small set of projected coefficients.

\section{1. Minimal honest shell-amplitude system}

The correct reduced starting point is the inter-patch-coupled shell-amplitude equation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_t A_\alpha
=
\Bigl(\sigma_0+\eta P_2^\alpha\Bigr)A_\alpha
-u|A_\alpha|^2A_\alpha
-v\Bigl(\sum_\beta |A_\beta|^2\Bigr)A_\alpha
-\kappa\Bigl(\sum_\beta M_{\alpha\beta}|A_\beta|^2\Bigr)A_\alpha.
}
\label{eq:reduced_shell_system}
\end{equation}

Here:
\[
P_2^\alpha=P_2(\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha),
\qquad
M_{\alpha\beta}\sim (\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2,
\]
and the five coefficients
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_0,\qquad \eta,\qquad u,\qquad v,\qquad \kappa
}
\]
are the true reduced unknowns.

Thus the problem is no longer to scan directly over
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma),
\]
but to extract a finite reduced coefficient set.

\section{2. Stationary intensity equations}

Write
\[
r_\alpha:=|A_\alpha|^2.
\]
For stationary amplitudes with fixed phases, \eqref{eq:reduced_shell_system} reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
0
=
\sigma_0+\eta P_2^\alpha
-u r_\alpha
-v\sum_\beta r_\beta
-\kappa\sum_\beta M_{\alpha\beta}r_\beta,
\qquad
\alpha=1,\dots,12.
}
\label{eq:stationary_intensity_system}
\end{equation}

This is the exact finite algebraic system whose critical points determine the actual BCC branch basin.

\section{3. BCC-symmetric quartic reduction}

By BCC symmetry, the quartic coupling matrix is specified by only four numbers:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d,\qquad U_{\rm opp},\qquad U_\perp,\qquad U_{\rm obl}.
}
\label{eq:quartic_four_numbers}
\end{equation}
The corresponding row sum is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R
=
U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+8U_{\rm obl}.
}
\label{eq:row_sum_R_exact}
\end{equation}

Then the one-patch branch has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm 1patch}=\frac{\sigma}{U_d},
\qquad
\mathcal F_{\rm 1patch}=-\frac{\sigma^2}{2U_d},
}
\label{eq:one_patch_exact}
\end{equation}
while the equal-amplitude 12-patch BCC branch has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{\rm BCC}=\frac{\sigma}{R},
\qquad
\mathcal F_{\rm BCC}=-6\frac{\sigma^2}{R}.
}
\label{eq:BCC_patch_exact}
\end{equation}

Therefore the sharp energetic criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm BCC}<\mathcal F_{\rm 1patch}
\iff
R<12U_d.
}
\label{eq:sharp_BCC_criterion}
\end{equation}

This converts the branch-selection problem into an exact algebraic inequality.

\section{4. Orbit reduction}

Because the axis-locked branch naturally splits the shell into
\[
2+2+8,
\]
we may reduce the 12 amplitudes to three orbit variables:
\[
A_A,\qquad A_E,\qquad A_O.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
r_A=|A_A|^2,\qquad r_E=|A_E|^2,\qquad r_O=|A_O|^2.
\]

Then the full stationary system \eqref{eq:stationary_intensity_system} reduces to a \(3\times 3\) algebraic critical-point problem
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\partial \mathcal F_{\rm orb}}{\partial r_A}=0,
\qquad
\frac{\partial \mathcal F_{\rm orb}}{\partial r_E}=0,
\qquad
\frac{\partial \mathcal F_{\rm orb}}{\partial r_O}=0.
}
\label{eq:orbit_stationary_system}
\end{equation}

The backend numbers are then no longer selected by brute-force PDE scanning, but by the critical point of this reduced orbit free energy.

\section{5. Final finite extraction task}

Once the reduced formulas are fixed, the only remaining numerical task is the finite projection of the coefficients
\[
\sigma_0,\qquad \eta,\qquad u,\qquad v,\qquad \kappa
\]
or equivalently
\[
U_d,\qquad U_{\rm opp},\qquad U_\perp,\qquad U_{\rm obl}
\]
from the intended BCC branch of the microscopic TECT/Class II system.

At that point, the backend point
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)
\]
is not searched for directly.
It is obtained as the induced stationary critical point of the reduced amplitude theory.

\section{6. Immediate roadmap}

The rigorous backend program is therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Psi,X_i^{\,a})
\Longrightarrow
\mathcal F_{\rm shell}[A_1,\dots,A_{12}]
\Longrightarrow
\mathcal F_{\rm orb}(r_A,r_E,r_O)
\Longrightarrow
(r_A,r_E,r_O)_{\rm crit}
\Longrightarrow
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)_{\rm backend}.
}
\end{equation}

So the next step is not another parameter scan.
It is the explicit derivation of \(\mathcal F_{\rm orb}\) and its stationary equations.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact Orbit Free Energy for the Backend-Extraction Program}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now perform the second step of the rigorous backend program.

The direct numerical scan over
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)
\]
is replaced by an exact reduced orbit free energy on the retained BCC shell.
The key point is that the \(12\)-patch quartic interaction reduces to only four coupling numbers,
\[
U_d,\qquad U_{\rm opp},\qquad U_\perp,\qquad U_{\rm obl},
\]
and the axis-locked branch reduces further to the \(2+2+8\) orbit variables
\[
r_A,\qquad r_E,\qquad r_O.
\]

This turns the backend-extraction problem into a finite algebraic critical-point problem.

\section{1. Starting point: the honest reduced shell-amplitude system}

We start from the minimal inter-patch shell system
\begin{equation}
\partial_t A_\alpha
=
\Bigl(\sigma_0+\eta P_2^\alpha\Bigr)A_\alpha
-
\sum_{\beta=1}^{12}
U_{\alpha\beta}\,|A_\beta|^2 A_\alpha,
\qquad
\alpha=1,\dots,12,
\label{eq:shell_amp_start}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
U_{\alpha\beta}
=
u\,\delta_{\alpha\beta}
+
v
+
\kappa\,M_{\alpha\beta}.
\label{eq:Uab_definition}
\end{equation}

We assume the BCC shell
\[
\hat k_\alpha\in \mathcal S_{12},
\]
with locking axis
\[
\hat n=\frac{(1,1,0)}{\sqrt2}.
\]

The Legendre anisotropy values are then
\begin{equation}
P_2(\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha)
=
\begin{cases}
1, & \alpha\in A \quad (2\ \text{axial patches}),\\[1mm]
-\frac12, & \alpha\in E \quad (2\ \text{equatorial patches}),\\[1mm]
-\frac18, & \alpha\in O \quad (8\ \text{oblique patches}).
\end{cases}
\label{eq:P2_orbit_values}
\end{equation}

Hence the effective linear coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A=\sigma_0+\eta,\qquad
\sigma_E=\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{2},\qquad
\sigma_O=\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{8}.
}
\label{eq:sigma_AEO}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Exact four-number reduction of the quartic matrix}

By shell symmetry, the quartic kernel \(U_{\alpha\beta}\) takes only four values, depending on the relation of \(\beta\) to \(\alpha\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d,\qquad U_{\rm opp},\qquad U_\perp,\qquad U_{\rm obl}.
}
\label{eq:four_Us}
\end{equation}
Here:
\[
U_d:\ \beta=\alpha,
\qquad
U_{\rm opp}:\ \hat k_\beta=-\hat k_\alpha,
\qquad
U_\perp:\ \hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta=0,
\qquad
U_{\rm obl}:\ |\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta|=\frac12.
\]

Thus the full \(12\times12\) quartic matrix is specified by only the four numbers in \eqref{eq:four_Us}.

\section{3. Orbit counting for the \(2+2+8\) split}

Let
\[
N_A=2,\qquad N_E=2,\qquad N_O=8.
\]
For the orbit-symmetric ansatz
\begin{equation}
r_\alpha=
\begin{cases}
r_A, & \alpha\in A,\\
r_E, & \alpha\in E,\\
r_O, & \alpha\in O,
\end{cases}
\qquad
r_I:=|A_I|^2,
\label{eq:orbit_ansatz}
\end{equation}
the ordered pair counts are exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{AA}=2U_d+2U_{\rm opp},
\qquad
C_{EE}=2U_d+2U_{\rm opp},
}
\label{eq:C_AA_EE}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{AE}=4U_\perp,
\qquad
C_{AO}=16U_{\rm obl},
\qquad
C_{EO}=16U_{\rm obl},
}
\label{eq:C_AE_AO_EO}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{OO}=8U_d+8U_{\rm opp}+16U_\perp+32U_{\rm obl}.
}
\label{eq:C_OO}
\end{equation}

These are exact consequences of the cuboctahedral BCC shell combinatorics.

\section{4. Exact orbit free energy}

The reduced free energy whose gradient reproduces the stationary version of \eqref{eq:shell_amp_start} is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal F
=
-\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12} \sigma_\alpha r_\alpha
+\frac12\sum_{\alpha,\beta=1}^{12}U_{\alpha\beta}r_\alpha r_\beta.
\label{eq:F_12patch}
\end{equation}

Under the orbit ansatz \eqref{eq:orbit_ansatz}, this becomes
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm orb}(r_A,r_E,r_O)
}
&=
-2\sigma_A r_A
-2\sigma_E r_E
-8\sigma_O r_O
\nonumber\\[1mm]
&\quad
+\bigl(U_d+U_{\rm opp}\bigr)\bigl(r_A^2+r_E^2\bigr)
+4U_\perp r_A r_E
\nonumber\\[1mm]
&\quad
+16U_{\rm obl}(r_A+r_E)r_O
+\bigl(4U_d+4U_{\rm opp}+8U_\perp+16U_{\rm obl}\bigr)r_O^2.
\label{eq:F_orb_exact}
\end{align}

This is the exact \(2+2+8\) orbit free energy.

\section{5. Exact stationary equations}

Taking derivatives of \eqref{eq:F_orb_exact}, we obtain the stationary orbit system
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A
=
\bigl(U_d+U_{\rm opp}\bigr)r_A
+
2U_\perp r_E
+
8U_{\rm obl}r_O,
}
\label{eq:stat_A}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_E
=
2U_\perp r_A
+
\bigl(U_d+U_{\rm opp}\bigr)r_E
+
8U_{\rm obl}r_O,
}
\label{eq:stat_E}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_O
=
2U_{\rm obl}(r_A+r_E)
+
\bigl(U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+4U_{\rm obl}\bigr)r_O.
}
\label{eq:stat_O}
\end{equation}

Thus the full \(12\)-patch stationary problem has been reduced exactly to a \(3\times3\) algebraic system.

\section{6. Sum/difference reduction and closed-form solution}

Define
\begin{equation}
S:=r_A+r_E,
\qquad
\Delta_r:=r_A-r_E.
\label{eq:S_Delta_def}
\end{equation}

Subtracting \eqref{eq:stat_E} from \eqref{eq:stat_A} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_r
=
\frac{\sigma_A-\sigma_E}{U_d+U_{\rm opp}-2U_\perp}
=
\frac{3\eta/2}{U_d+U_{\rm opp}-2U_\perp}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_r_exact}
\end{equation}

Adding \eqref{eq:stat_A} and \eqref{eq:stat_E}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp\bigr)S
+
16U_{\rm obl}r_O
=
2\sigma_0+\frac{\eta}{2}.
}
\label{eq:S_eq}
\end{equation}

Equation \eqref{eq:stat_O} becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2U_{\rm obl}S
+
\bigl(U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+4U_{\rm obl}\bigr)r_O
=
\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{8}.
}
\label{eq:rO_eq}
\end{equation}

Introduce
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A:=U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp,
\qquad
\mathcal B:=16U_{\rm obl},
\qquad
\mathcal C:=2U_{\rm obl},
\qquad
\mathcal D:=U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+4U_{\rm obl}.
\label{eq:ABCD_def}
\end{equation}
Then \eqref{eq:S_eq}--\eqref{eq:rO_eq} read
\begin{equation}
\mathcal A S+\mathcal B r_O = 2\sigma_0+\frac{\eta}{2},
\qquad
\mathcal C S+\mathcal D r_O = \sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{8}.
\label{eq:two_by_two_system}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S
=
\frac{
\left(2\sigma_0+\frac{\eta}{2}\right)\mathcal D
-
\mathcal B\left(\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{8}\right)
}{
\mathcal A\mathcal D-\mathcal B\mathcal C
},
}
\label{eq:S_solution}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_O
=
\frac{
\mathcal A\left(\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{8}\right)
-
\mathcal C\left(2\sigma_0+\frac{\eta}{2}\right)
}{
\mathcal A\mathcal D-\mathcal B\mathcal C
}.
}
\label{eq:rO_solution}
\end{equation}

Finally,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_A=\frac{S+\Delta_r}{2},
\qquad
r_E=\frac{S-\Delta_r}{2}.
}
\label{eq:rA_rE_solution}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact orbit critical point is obtained in closed algebraic form.

\section{7. Specialization to the explicit kernel \texorpdfstring{$M_{\alpha\beta}=(\hat k_\alpha\cdot\hat k_\beta)^2$}{M=(k.k)^2}}

For the explicit angular kernel
\begin{equation}
M_{\alpha\beta}=(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2,
\label{eq:M_dot2}
\end{equation}
the four quartic numbers become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d=u+v+\kappa,
\qquad
U_{\rm opp}=v+\kappa,
\qquad
U_\perp=v,
\qquad
U_{\rm obl}=v+\frac{\kappa}{4}.
}
\label{eq:U_classes_uvk}
\end{equation}

Then the row sum
\begin{equation}
R:=U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+8U_{\rm obl}
\label{eq:R_def}
\end{equation}
reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R=u+12v+4\kappa.
}
\label{eq:R_uvk}
\end{equation}

The one-patch and equal-amplitude 12-patch BCC branches satisfy
\begin{equation}
r_{\rm 1patch}=\frac{\sigma}{U_d},
\qquad
\mathcal F_{\rm 1patch}=-\frac{\sigma^2}{2U_d},
\label{eq:1patch_energy}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
r_{\rm BCC}=\frac{\sigma}{R},
\qquad
\mathcal F_{\rm BCC}=-6\frac{\sigma^2}{R}.
\label{eq:BCC_energy}
\end{equation}

Therefore the sharp BCC stability criterion
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm BCC}<\mathcal F_{\rm 1patch}
\iff
R<12U_d
\]
becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
11u+8\kappa>0.
}
\label{eq:sharp_u_k_criterion}
\end{equation}

This is an exact closed criterion for avoiding one-patch collapse in the explicit reduced theory.

\section{8. Orbit free energy directly in \texorpdfstring{$(u,v,\kappa)$}{(u,v,kappa)} variables}

Substituting \eqref{eq:U_classes_uvk} into \eqref{eq:F_orb_exact}, we obtain
\begin{align}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm orb}(r_A,r_E,r_O)
}
&=
-2\sigma_A r_A
-2\sigma_E r_E
-8\sigma_O r_O
\nonumber\\[1mm]
&\quad
+\bigl(u+2v+2\kappa\bigr)\bigl(r_A^2+r_E^2\bigr)
+4v\,r_A r_E
\nonumber\\[1mm]
&\quad
+\bigl(16v+4\kappa\bigr)(r_A+r_E)r_O
+\bigl(4u+32v+12\kappa\bigr)r_O^2.
\label{eq:F_orb_uvk}
\end{align}

The stationary equations are then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A
=
(u+2v+2\kappa)r_A
+
2v\,r_E
+
(8v+2\kappa)r_O,
}
\label{eq:stat_A_uvk}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_E
=
2v\,r_A
+
(u+2v+2\kappa)r_E
+
(8v+2\kappa)r_O,
}
\label{eq:stat_E_uvk}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_O
=
\left(2v+\frac{\kappa}{2}\right)(r_A+r_E)
+
(u+8v+3\kappa)r_O.
}
\label{eq:stat_O_uvk}
\end{equation}

The orbit splitting becomes especially simple:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_r
=
\frac{3\eta/2}{u+2\kappa}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_r_uvk}
\end{equation}

Thus the axial-equatorial splitting is controlled only by \(u\) and \(\kappa\), while the isotropic background \(v\) drops out completely.

\section{9. Consequence for the backend numbers}

At this point the backend-extraction problem is no longer a broad scan in
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma).
\]
Instead, it has been reduced to the finite extraction of the reduced coefficients
\[
u,\qquad v,\qquad \kappa,\qquad \sigma_0,\qquad \eta
\]
from the intended microscopic BCC branch.

Once these are computed, the critical point
\[
(r_A,r_E,r_O)
\]
is fixed analytically by \eqref{eq:S_solution}, \eqref{eq:rO_solution}, and \eqref{eq:rA_rE_solution}, and the backend numbers follow from the induced stationary branch.

So the next step is not another brute-force search.
It is the explicit microscopic projection of
\[
u,\ v,\ \kappa,\ \sigma_0,\ \eta.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The backend-extraction problem has now been reduced exactly to a finite orbit free-energy problem.

The quartic shell interaction is specified by only four numbers
\[
U_d,\qquad U_{\rm opp},\qquad U_\perp,\qquad U_{\rm obl},
\]
and the axis-locked \(12\)-patch shell reduces to the \(2+2+8\) orbit variables
\[
r_A,\qquad r_E,\qquad r_O.
\]

The exact orbit free energy is
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm orb}(r_A,r_E,r_O),
\]
and its stationary equations reduce to a closed \(3\times3\) algebraic system.
In sum/difference variables,
\[
S=r_A+r_E,\qquad \Delta_r=r_A-r_E,
\]
the critical point is obtained explicitly in closed form.

For the explicit kernel
\[
M_{\alpha\beta}=(\hat k_\alpha\cdot\hat k_\beta)^2,
\]
the sharp BCC stability condition becomes
\[
\boxed{
11u+8\kappa>0.
}
\]

Moreover, the axial-equatorial orbit splitting is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_r=\frac{3\eta/2}{u+2\kappa},
}
\]
so the isotropic coefficient \(v\) drops out of the orbit splitting entirely.

Therefore the remaining backend problem is no longer a broad numerical scan.
It is the finite microscopic extraction of
\[
u,\qquad v,\qquad \kappa,\qquad \sigma_0,\qquad \eta,
\]
after which the orbit critical point and the induced backend numbers are fixed analytically.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Microscopic Projection Formulas for the Reduced Backend Coefficients}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

We now perform the third step of the rigorous backend program.

The numerical search over
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)
\]
must be replaced by explicit microscopic projection formulas on the intended BCC branch.
The task is to project the microscopic quadratic and quartic operators onto the retained shell basis and thereby extract the reduced coefficients
\[
\sigma_0,\qquad \eta,\qquad u,\qquad v,\qquad \kappa.
\]

Once these coefficients are known, the orbit critical point
\[
(r_A,r_E,r_O)
\]
is fixed analytically by the exact reduced theory derived in the previous step.

\section{1. Intended BCC shell basis}

Let the intended microscopic background be the actual BCC branch
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{BCC}}(x),
\]
with shell radius
\[
|k|=q_*.
\]
Choose the \(12\) shell directions
\[
\hat k_\alpha\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}},
\qquad
\alpha=1,\dots,12,
\]
and an adapted shell basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varphi_\alpha(x)
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\mathrm{Vol}(\Omega)}}
\,\xi_\alpha\,
e^{iq_*\hat k_\alpha\cdot x},
\qquad
\xi_\alpha^\dagger\xi_\alpha=1,
}
\label{eq:shell_basis_varphi}
\end{equation}
where \(\Omega\) is the unit cell and \(\xi_\alpha\) denotes the internal polarization / Bloch factor of the retained branch.

All reduced coefficients will now be extracted by projection onto the finite basis \(\{\varphi_\alpha\}\).

\section{2. Quadratic projection: extracting the linear shell data}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{mic}}^{(2)}
:=
\left.
\frac{\delta^2 \mathcal F_{\mathrm{mic}}}{\delta\Psi^\dagger\,\delta\Psi}
\right|_{\Psi=\Psi_{\mathrm{BCC}}}
}
\label{eq:H2_mic_def}
\end{equation}
be the microscopic quadratic Hessian on the intended BCC branch.

Define the shell-projected quadratic matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{\alpha\beta}
=
\int_\Omega d^3x\;
\overline{\varphi_\alpha(x)}\,
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{mic}}^{(2)}\,
\varphi_\beta(x).
}
\label{eq:H2_shell_matrix}
\end{equation}

At the reduced orbit level, the first quantity needed is the shell-diagonal part
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_\alpha:=H^{(2)}_{\alpha\alpha}.
}
\label{eq:h_alpha_def}
\end{equation}

The reduced shell free energy begins as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
-\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12} h_\alpha r_\alpha
+\frac12\sum_{\alpha,\beta=1}^{12}U_{\alpha\beta}r_\alpha r_\beta
+\cdots,
\qquad
r_\alpha:=|A_\alpha|^2.
\label{eq:F_shell_basic}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact projection formulas for \texorpdfstring{$\sigma_0$}{sigma0} and \texorpdfstring{$\eta$}{eta}}

Let
\[
P_2^\alpha:=P_2(\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha),
\]
with the axis-locked orbit values
\begin{equation}
P_2^\alpha=
\begin{cases}
1, & \alpha\in A,\\[1mm]
-\dfrac12, & \alpha\in E,\\[1mm]
-\dfrac18, & \alpha\in O.
\end{cases}
\label{eq:P2_values_projection}
\end{equation}

The reduced linear coefficients are defined by the exact projection
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_\alpha=\sigma_0+\eta P_2^\alpha+h_\alpha^{\mathrm{rem}},
}
\label{eq:h_decomp}
\end{equation}
where \(h_\alpha^{\mathrm{rem}}\) is the part orthogonal to the \(\{1,P_2\}\) sector.

The orthogonal projection onto \(\{1,P_2\}\) gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_0
=
\frac1{12}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12} h_\alpha,
}
\label{eq:sigma0_projection}
\end{equation}
because
\[
\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}P_2^\alpha=0.
\]

Next,
\[
\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}(P_2^\alpha)^2
=
2\cdot 1^2
+
2\cdot\left(\frac12\right)^2
+
8\cdot\left(\frac18\right)^2
=
\frac{21}{8}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta
=
\frac{\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12} P_2^\alpha\, h_\alpha}
{\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}(P_2^\alpha)^2}
=
\frac{8}{21}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12} P_2^\alpha\, h_\alpha.
}
\label{eq:eta_projection}
\end{equation}

Thus \(\sigma_0\) and \(\eta\) are obtained exactly by finite projection of the microscopic quadratic Hessian.

\section{4. Orbit-average form of the same formulas}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A:=\frac12\sum_{\alpha\in A}h_\alpha,
\qquad
\sigma_E:=\frac12\sum_{\alpha\in E}h_\alpha,
\qquad
\sigma_O:=\frac18\sum_{\alpha\in O}h_\alpha.
}
\label{eq:sigma_orbit_means}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A=\sigma_0+\eta,
\qquad
\sigma_E=\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{2},
\qquad
\sigma_O=\sigma_0-\frac{\eta}{8}.
}
\label{eq:sigma_AEO_recalled}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta=\frac{2}{3}(\sigma_A-\sigma_E),
\qquad
\sigma_0=\frac{\sigma_A+2\sigma_E}{3},
}
\label{eq:eta_sigma0_from_AE}
\end{equation}
and consistency predicts
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_O=\frac{\sigma_A+3\sigma_E}{4}.
}
\label{eq:sigma_O_consistency}
\end{equation}

Equation \eqref{eq:sigma_O_consistency} is the exact internal check that the linear shell data is exhausted by the \((\sigma_0,\eta)\) truncation.

\section{5. Quartic projection: extracting the shell-coupling matrix}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_{\mathrm{mic}}^{(4)}
:=
\left.
\frac{\delta^4 \mathcal F_{\mathrm{mic}}}
{\delta\Psi^\dagger\,\delta\Psi^\dagger\,\delta\Psi\,\delta\Psi}
\right|_{\Psi=\Psi_{\mathrm{BCC}}}
}
\label{eq:Gamma4_mic_def}
\end{equation}
denote the microscopic four-point vertex on the intended branch.

Instead of writing all tensor indices explicitly, define the reduced quartic shell free energy by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(4)}
=
\frac12\sum_{\alpha,\beta=1}^{12}
U_{\alpha\beta}\,r_\alpha r_\beta.
}
\label{eq:F4_shell_Uab}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}
=
\frac{\partial^2 \mathcal F_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(4)}}{\partial r_\alpha\,\partial r_\beta}.
}
\label{eq:Uab_from_F4}
\end{equation}

This definition is exact and removes all normalization ambiguity.
The remaining task is therefore to compute the finite matrix \(U_{\alpha\beta}\) from the microscopic projected quartic vertex.

\section{6. Exact class averages \texorpdfstring{$U_d,U_{\rm opp},U_\perp,U_{\rm obl}$}{Ud,Uopp,Uperp,Uobl}}

The BCC shell geometry implies that each ordered pair \((\alpha,\beta)\) belongs to exactly one of four classes:

\[
\beta=\alpha,
\qquad
\beta=\bar\alpha,
\qquad
\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta=0,
\qquad
|\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta|=\frac12.
\]

Define the corresponding ordered-pair sets
\[
\mathcal C_d,\qquad
\mathcal C_{\rm opp},\qquad
\mathcal C_\perp,\qquad
\mathcal C_{\rm obl}.
\]

Their cardinalities are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\mathcal C_d|=12,\qquad
|\mathcal C_{\rm opp}|=12,\qquad
|\mathcal C_\perp|=24,\qquad
|\mathcal C_{\rm obl}|=96.
}
\label{eq:pair_counts}
\end{equation}

The class-averaged quartic numbers are therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d
=
\frac1{12}\sum_{(\alpha,\beta)\in\mathcal C_d} U_{\alpha\beta},
}
\label{eq:Ud_proj}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\rm opp}
=
\frac1{12}\sum_{(\alpha,\beta)\in\mathcal C_{\rm opp}} U_{\alpha\beta},
}
\label{eq:Uopp_proj}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\perp
=
\frac1{24}\sum_{(\alpha,\beta)\in\mathcal C_\perp} U_{\alpha\beta},
}
\label{eq:Uperp_proj}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\rm obl}
=
\frac1{96}\sum_{(\alpha,\beta)\in\mathcal C_{\rm obl}} U_{\alpha\beta}.
}
\label{eq:Uobl_proj}
\end{equation}

Thus the full \(12\times12\) quartic matrix has been reduced to four finite projected numbers.

\section{7. Exact inversion to \texorpdfstring{$u,v,\kappa$}{u,v,kappa}}

For the reduced kernel ansatz
\begin{equation}
U_{\alpha\beta}
=
u\,\delta_{\alpha\beta}
+
v
+
\kappa(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2,
\label{eq:kernel_uvk_again}
\end{equation}
the four class values are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d=u+v+\kappa,
\qquad
U_{\rm opp}=v+\kappa,
\qquad
U_\perp=v,
\qquad
U_{\rm obl}=v+\frac{\kappa}{4}.
}
\label{eq:UdUoppUperpUobl_uvk}
\end{equation}

These relations can be inverted exactly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v=U_\perp,
}
\label{eq:v_exact}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\kappa=4\bigl(U_{\rm obl}-U_\perp\bigr),
}
\label{eq:kappa_exact}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u=U_d-U_{\rm opp}=U_d-4U_{\rm obl}+3U_\perp.
}
\label{eq:u_exact}
\end{equation}

So \(u,v,\kappa\) are exact finite functions of the projected quartic class averages.

\section{8. Consistency defect of the \texorpdfstring{$(u,v,\kappa)$}{(u,v,kappa)} truncation}

The explicit kernel ansatz \eqref{eq:kernel_uvk_again} predicts the relation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\rm opp}=4U_{\rm obl}-3U_\perp.
}
\label{eq:kernel_consistency_relation}
\end{equation}

Hence define the quartic truncation defect
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm ker}
:=
U_{\rm opp}-4U_{\rm obl}+3U_\perp.
}
\label{eq:Delta_ker}
\end{equation}

If
\[
\Delta_{\rm ker}=0,
\]
then the quartic shell matrix is exactly representable by the \((u,v,\kappa)\) kernel.
If
\[
\Delta_{\rm ker}\neq 0,
\]
then the reduced kernel family must be enlarged.

Thus \(\Delta_{\rm ker}\) is the exact self-consistency test of the present reduced ansatz.

\section{9. Final extraction map}

The full coefficient-extraction map is now exact:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{mic}}^{(2)}
\Longrightarrow
h_\alpha
\Longrightarrow
(\sigma_0,\eta),
}
\label{eq:quadratic_extract_map}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_{\mathrm{mic}}^{(4)}
\Longrightarrow
U_{\alpha\beta}
\Longrightarrow
(U_d,U_{\rm opp},U_\perp,U_{\rm obl})
\Longrightarrow
(u,v,\kappa).
}
\label{eq:quartic_extract_map}
\end{equation}

Therefore the remaining backend problem is no longer a scan.
It is the finite computation of:
\[
h_\alpha,
\qquad
U_{\alpha\beta},
\qquad
\Delta_{\rm ker}.
\]

Once these are inserted, the orbit critical point
\[
(r_A,r_E,r_O)
\]
is fixed analytically by the reduced equations already derived.

\section{10. Consequence for the backend numbers}

The old scan variables
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)
\]
should now be regarded only as surrogate coordinates of the stationary branch.
The fundamental reduced inputs are instead
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_0,\qquad \eta,\qquad u,\qquad v,\qquad \kappa.
}
\]

Thus the next step is not a further search in \((\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)\),
but the explicit microscopic evaluation of the finite shell projections in
\eqref{eq:H2_shell_matrix} and \eqref{eq:Uab_from_F4}.

\section{Final Summary}

The backend-extraction problem has now been reduced to explicit finite microscopic projection formulas.

From the microscopic quadratic Hessian on the intended BCC branch,
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{mic}}^{(2)},
\]
one computes the shell-diagonal numbers
\[
h_\alpha
=
\langle \varphi_\alpha,\mathcal H_{\mathrm{mic}}^{(2)}\varphi_\alpha\rangle,
\]
and projects them onto the \(\{1,P_2\}\) basis to obtain
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_0=\frac1{12}\sum_\alpha h_\alpha,
\qquad
\eta=\frac{8}{21}\sum_\alpha P_2^\alpha h_\alpha.
}
\]

From the microscopic four-point vertex,
\[
\Gamma_{\mathrm{mic}}^{(4)},
\]
one computes the quartic shell matrix
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}
=
\frac{\partial^2 \mathcal F_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(4)}}{\partial r_\alpha\,\partial r_\beta},
\]
and then the four BCC class averages
\[
U_d,\qquad U_{\rm opp},\qquad U_\perp,\qquad U_{\rm obl}.
\]

These determine the reduced kernel coefficients exactly:
\[
\boxed{
v=U_\perp,\qquad
\kappa=4(U_{\rm obl}-U_\perp),\qquad
u=U_d-U_{\rm opp}=U_d-4U_{\rm obl}+3U_\perp.
}
\]

The additional quantity
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm ker}=U_{\rm opp}-4U_{\rm obl}+3U_\perp
}
\]
is the exact self-consistency defect of the \((u,v,\kappa)\) truncation.

Therefore the remaining backend problem is no longer a numerical scan.
It is the finite microscopic evaluation of
\[
h_\alpha,\qquad U_{\alpha\beta},\qquad \Delta_{\rm ker},
\]
after which the reduced orbit critical point is fixed analytically.

\section{Concrete Insertion Recipe for the Exact Backend Numbers}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The reduced theory is now complete.
What remains is not another scan, but the explicit insertion of the actual intended BCC branch into the projection formulas.

The goal is to compute
\[
h_\alpha,\qquad U_{\alpha\beta},
\]
from the same microscopic BCC background
\[
\Psi_{\rm BCC}(x),
\]
and then obtain
\[
\sigma_0,\qquad \eta,\qquad u,\qquad v,\qquad \kappa
\]
by finite class averaging and exact algebraic inversion.

\section{1. Fix the background once and for all}

Take the numerically selected actual branch background
\[
\Psi_{\rm BCC}(x)
\]
as the reference stationary state of the microscopic TECT/Class II system:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\delta \mathcal F_{\rm mic}}{\delta \Psi^\dagger}\Big|_{\Psi=\Psi_{\rm BCC}}=0.
}
\label{eq:background_stationary}
\end{equation}

Operationally, this is the branch already identified inside the commensurate BCC shell basin.
All projections below must be evaluated on this \emph{same} background.
This matches the explicit intended-branch extraction philosophy already fixed in the project notes. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\section{2. Define the shell perturbation family}

Let the retained shell basis be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varphi_\alpha(x)
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\mathrm{Vol}(\Omega)}}\,
\xi_\alpha\,e^{iq_*\hat k_\alpha\cdot x},
\qquad
\alpha=1,\dots,12,
}
\label{eq:retained_shell_basis}
\end{equation}
with the BCC shell directions \(\hat k_\alpha\) and adapted internal vectors \(\xi_\alpha\).

Introduce the finite shell-deformed field
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi[x;A]
=
\Psi_{\rm BCC}(x)
+
\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12} A_\alpha\,\varphi_\alpha(x).
}
\label{eq:Psi_deformed}
\end{equation}

Then define the reduced shell free energy by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal F_{\rm shell}(A,\bar A)
:=
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}\!\big[\Psi[x;A]\big]
-
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_{\rm BCC}].
}
\label{eq:F_shell_definition}
\end{equation}

This is the unique object from which all reduced coefficients are extracted.

\section{3. Quadratic projection by shell Hessian}

The microscopic quadratic Hessian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\rm mic}^{(2)}
=
\left.
\frac{\delta^2 \mathcal F_{\rm mic}}
{\delta \Psi^\dagger\,\delta \Psi}
\right|_{\Psi=\Psi_{\rm BCC}}.
}
\label{eq:H2_mic_again}
\end{equation}

The exact shell-projected quadratic matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{\alpha\beta}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial^2 \mathcal F_{\rm shell}}
{\partial \overline{A_\alpha}\,\partial A_\beta}
\right|_{A=0}
=
\int_\Omega d^3x\;
\overline{\varphi_\alpha(x)}\,
\mathcal H_{\rm mic}^{(2)}\,
\varphi_\beta(x).
}
\label{eq:H2_projected_exact}
\end{equation}

The shell-diagonal data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_\alpha:=H^{(2)}_{\alpha\alpha}.
}
\label{eq:h_alpha_again}
\end{equation}

From these, the linear reduced coefficients are obtained by the exact projection formulas
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_0=\frac1{12}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12} h_\alpha,
}
\label{eq:sigma0_again}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta
=
\frac{8}{21}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}P_2^\alpha\,h_\alpha,
}
\label{eq:eta_again}
\end{equation}
with
\[
P_2^\alpha=P_2(\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha).
\]

\section{4. Quartic projection by intensity derivatives}

The reduced quartic energy is defined from the shell free energy expansion
\begin{equation}
\mathcal F_{\rm shell}
=
-\sum_\alpha h_\alpha r_\alpha
+
\frac12\sum_{\alpha,\beta}U_{\alpha\beta}r_\alpha r_\beta
+O(r^3),
\qquad
r_\alpha:=|A_\alpha|^2.
\label{eq:F_shell_r_expand}
\end{equation}

The exact quartic shell matrix is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial^2 \mathcal F_{\rm shell}^{(4)}}
{\partial r_\alpha\,\partial r_\beta}
\right|_{r=0}.
}
\label{eq:Uab_exact_from_r}
\end{equation}

A practical insertion rule is to define the one- and two-patch deformed backgrounds
\begin{equation}
\Psi_\alpha(x;r)
=
\Psi_{\rm BCC}(x)+\sqrt r\,\varphi_\alpha(x),
\label{eq:onepatch_deform}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{\alpha\beta}(x;r,s)
=
\Psi_{\rm BCC}(x)+\sqrt r\,\varphi_\alpha(x)+\sqrt s\,\varphi_\beta(x).
\label{eq:twopatch_deform}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_\alpha
=
-
\left.
\frac{\partial}{\partial r}
\Bigl[
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_\alpha(\cdot;r)]
-
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_{\rm BCC}]
\Bigr]
\right|_{r=0},
}
\label{eq:h_alpha_from_r}
\end{equation}
while the off-diagonal quartic coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}
=
\left.
\frac{\partial^2}{\partial r\,\partial s}
\Bigl[
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_{\alpha\beta}(\cdot;r,s)]
-
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_{\rm BCC}]
\Bigr]
\right|_{r=s=0}.
}
\label{eq:Uab_from_rs}
\end{equation}

Thus the quartic matrix is obtained by finite intensity derivatives around the same intended branch.

\section{5. Finite-difference implementation formulas}

If automatic differentiation is unavailable, the required quantities can be computed by symmetric finite differences.

For small \(r=\varepsilon^2\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_\alpha
\approx
-
\frac{
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_\alpha(\cdot;\varepsilon^2)]
-
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_{\rm BCC}]
}{\varepsilon^2},
}
\label{eq:h_alpha_fd}
\end{equation}
to leading order.

For \(\alpha\neq\beta\), define
\[
\Delta_{\alpha\beta}(\varepsilon)
:=
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_{\alpha\beta}(\cdot;\varepsilon^2,\varepsilon^2)]
-
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_\alpha(\cdot;\varepsilon^2)]
-
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_\beta(\cdot;\varepsilon^2)]
+
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_{\rm BCC}].
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}
\approx
\frac{\Delta_{\alpha\beta}(\varepsilon)}{\varepsilon^4}.
}
\label{eq:Uab_fd}
\end{equation}

Similarly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\alpha}
\approx
2\,
\frac{
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_\alpha(\cdot;2\varepsilon^2)]
-2\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_\alpha(\cdot;\varepsilon^2)]
+\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_{\rm BCC}]
}{\varepsilon^4}.
}
\label{eq:Uaa_fd}
\end{equation}

These formulas reduce the coefficient extraction to finite energy evaluations on a small set of shell perturbations.

\section{6. Class averaging on the BCC shell}

Once \(U_{\alpha\beta}\) is computed, define the four class averages
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d
=
\frac1{12}\sum_{(\alpha,\beta)\in\mathcal C_d}U_{\alpha\beta},
\qquad
U_{\rm opp}
=
\frac1{12}\sum_{(\alpha,\beta)\in\mathcal C_{\rm opp}}U_{\alpha\beta},
}
\label{eq:UdUopp_reinsert}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\perp
=
\frac1{24}\sum_{(\alpha,\beta)\in\mathcal C_\perp}U_{\alpha\beta},
\qquad
U_{\rm obl}
=
\frac1{96}\sum_{(\alpha,\beta)\in\mathcal C_{\rm obl}}U_{\alpha\beta}.
}
\label{eq:UperpUobl_reinsert}
\end{equation}

This compresses the entire quartic shell matrix to four finite numbers.

\section{7. Exact inversion to the kernel coefficients}

For the reduced kernel
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}
=
u\,\delta_{\alpha\beta}
+
v
+
\kappa(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2,
\]
the exact inversion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v=U_\perp,
\qquad
\kappa=4(U_{\rm obl}-U_\perp),
\qquad
u=U_d-U_{\rm opp}=U_d-4U_{\rm obl}+3U_\perp.
}
\label{eq:uvk_inversion_final}
\end{equation}

Thus the reduced quartic kernel is obtained by explicit finite class averaging.

\section{8. Exact self-consistency defect}

The \((u,v,\kappa)\) truncation predicts
\begin{equation}
U_{\rm opp}=4U_{\rm obl}-3U_\perp.
\label{eq:opp_relation_again}
\end{equation}
Hence define the exact truncation defect
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm ker}:=
U_{\rm opp}-4U_{\rm obl}+3U_\perp.
}
\label{eq:Delta_ker_again}
\end{equation}

This is the decisive internal check:
\[
\Delta_{\rm ker}=0
\]
means the reduced kernel is exactly captured by \((u,v,\kappa)\);
otherwise the quartic ansatz must be enlarged.

\section{9. Final output of the insertion step}

After the finite projection, the reduced orbit theory is fully determined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\sigma_0,\eta,u,v,\kappa,\Delta_{\rm ker}).
}
\label{eq:final_output_projection}
\end{equation}

Then the exact reduced stationary solution
\[
(r_A,r_E,r_O)
\]
follows analytically from the orbit equations already derived in the previous step.

So the backend numbers are no longer found by search.
They are induced by the finite projected coefficients of the intended microscopic BCC branch.

\section{10. Practical execution order}

The actual practical order is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm BCC}
\Longrightarrow
h_\alpha
\Longrightarrow
(\sigma_0,\eta),
}
\label{eq:order1}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{\rm BCC}
\Longrightarrow
U_{\alpha\beta}
\Longrightarrow
(U_d,U_{\rm opp},U_\perp,U_{\rm obl})
\Longrightarrow
(u,v,\kappa,\Delta_{\rm ker}),
}
\label{eq:order2}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\sigma_0,\eta,u,v,\kappa)
\Longrightarrow
(r_A,r_E,r_O)_{\rm crit}
\Longrightarrow
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)_{\rm backend}.
}
\label{eq:order3}
\end{equation}

This is the explicit completion of the rigorous backend-extraction program.

\section{Final Summary}

The backend-extraction program is now fully explicit.

The remaining task is to evaluate the microscopic shell free energy
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm shell}(A,\bar A)
=
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}\!\big[\Psi_{\rm BCC}+\sum_\alpha A_\alpha\varphi_\alpha\big]
-
\mathcal F_{\rm mic}[\Psi_{\rm BCC}]
\]
on the intended BCC branch.

From the shell Hessian,
\[
H^{(2)}_{\alpha\beta}
=
\frac{\partial^2 \mathcal F_{\rm shell}}
{\partial \overline{A_\alpha}\partial A_\beta}\Big|_{A=0},
\]
one obtains
\[
h_\alpha
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\sigma_0,\eta.
\]

From the quartic shell expansion,
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm shell}^{(4)}
=
\frac12\sum_{\alpha,\beta}U_{\alpha\beta}r_\alpha r_\beta,
\]
one obtains
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
(U_d,U_{\rm opp},U_\perp,U_{\rm obl})
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
(u,v,\kappa).
\]

The exact inversion is
\[
\boxed{
v=U_\perp,\qquad
\kappa=4(U_{\rm obl}-U_\perp),\qquad
u=U_d-U_{\rm opp}=U_d-4U_{\rm obl}+3U_\perp.
}
\]

The truncation defect
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm ker}=U_{\rm opp}-4U_{\rm obl}+3U_\perp
}
\]
is the exact self-consistency test of the reduced kernel.

Therefore the backend problem has now been reduced completely to a finite insertion task on the intended BCC branch, after which the reduced orbit critical point is fixed analytically.

\section{Executable Backend Projection Extractor}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The backend-extraction program is now no longer only formal.
An executable projection extractor has been fixed.

Its purpose is to reconstruct the current best confirmed BCC branch,
project the microscopic residual response onto the retained \(12\)-patch shell basis,
and extract the reduced coefficient data
\[
h_\alpha,\qquad U_{\alpha\beta},
\qquad
(\sigma_0,\eta),
\qquad
(U_d,U_{\rm opp},U_\perp,U_{\rm obl}),
\qquad
(u,v,\kappa,\Delta_{\rm ker}).
\]

\section{1. Background reconstruction}

The extractor first reconstructs the current best confirmed branch
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62)
\]
in the commensurate BCC box
\[
L=4\pi,\qquad q_*=\frac{1}{\sqrt2},
\]
using the same continuation schedule that produced the best confirmed actual-branch basin.

The resulting field is taken as the intended branch background
\[
\Psi_{\rm BCC}(x).
\]

\section{2. Shell basis and projected residual amplitudes}

The retained shell basis is
\[
\varphi_\alpha(x)
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\mathrm{Vol}(\Omega)}}\,\xi_\alpha e^{iq_*\hat k_\alpha\cdot x},
\qquad
\alpha=1,\dots,12.
\]

Since the current solver exposes the stationary residual
\[
R[\Psi],
\]
the projection is performed through
\[
\Pi_\alpha[\delta\Psi]
=
\langle \varphi_\alpha,\delta\Psi\rangle_\Omega.
\]

Then the effective linear shell coefficients are extracted through
\[
h_\alpha
=
-\Re\left[
\frac{\Pi_\alpha R[\Psi_{\rm BCC}+\varepsilon \varphi_\alpha]}{\varepsilon}
\right].
\]

This gives the shell-diagonal linear data needed for
\[
\sigma_0,\qquad \eta.
\]

\section{3. Quadratic projection to \texorpdfstring{$\sigma_0,\eta$}{sigma0, eta}}

With
\[
P_2^\alpha=P_2(\hat n\!\cdot\!\hat k_\alpha),
\]
the reduced linear coefficients are obtained by
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_0=\frac1{12}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}h_\alpha,
\qquad
\eta=\frac{8}{21}\sum_{\alpha=1}^{12}P_2^\alpha h_\alpha.
}
\]

Thus the axial/equatorial/oblique orbit splitting is read directly from the microscopic background.

\section{4. Quartic projection to \texorpdfstring{$U_{\alpha\beta}$}{Uab}}

The effective quartic shell matrix is extracted from the intensity dependence of the projected residual.

Let
\[
\Psi_{\beta}=\Psi_{\rm BCC}+\epsilon \varphi_\beta.
\]
Then, using a small linear probe in the \(\alpha\) direction,
\[
h_\alpha^{(\beta)}
=
-\Re\left[
\frac{\Pi_\alpha R[\Psi_\beta+\delta \varphi_\alpha]}{\delta}
\right].
\]

The quartic matrix is then estimated by
\[
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}
\approx
\frac{h_\alpha-h_\alpha^{(\beta)}}{\epsilon^2}.
}
\]

This is the practical residual-based realization of the reduced shell quartic projection.

\section{5. BCC class averages and kernel inversion}

From the computed \(U_{\alpha\beta}\), the BCC class averages are formed:
\[
U_d,\qquad U_{\rm opp},\qquad U_\perp,\qquad U_{\rm obl}.
\]

These are then inverted to the reduced kernel coefficients by
\[
\boxed{
v=U_\perp,
\qquad
\kappa=4(U_{\rm obl}-U_\perp),
\qquad
u=U_d-U_{\rm opp}.
}
\]

The kernel-consistency defect is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm ker}=U_{\rm opp}-4U_{\rm obl}+3U_\perp.
}
\]

Hence the output of the extractor is exactly
\[
\boxed{
(\sigma_0,\eta,u,v,\kappa,\Delta_{\rm ker}).
}
\]

\section{6. Meaning of the extractor}

This extractor should be interpreted as follows:

\begin{enumerate}
\item It does not perform another broad parameter search.
\item It starts from the already confirmed best BCC branch.
\item It converts that branch into the reduced shell/orbit theory coefficients.
\item It provides the finite data needed to decide whether the current reduced kernel truncation is self-consistent.
\end{enumerate}

So the backend problem is now genuinely reduced to a finite projection computation.

\section{Final Summary}

The rigorous backend program has now reached an executable stage.

An explicit projection-extractor script has been fixed, whose role is to:

\[
\Psi_{\rm BCC}
\Longrightarrow
h_\alpha
\Longrightarrow
(\sigma_0,\eta),
\]
\[
\Psi_{\rm BCC}
\Longrightarrow
U_{\alpha\beta}
\Longrightarrow
(U_d,U_{\rm opp},U_\perp,U_{\rm obl})
\Longrightarrow
(u,v,\kappa,\Delta_{\rm ker}).
\]

The current implementation is residual-based, because the present solver family exposes the stationary residual \(R[\Psi]\) rather than an independent microscopic free-energy functional.

Therefore the resulting coefficients should be interpreted as the effective reduced coefficient set of the current solver family around the best confirmed actual BCC branch.

This is still a major step: the backend problem has now been converted from a parameter-search problem into a finite projection-extraction problem.

\section{Actual Projection Output and Immediate Theoretical Consequence}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The projection extractor has now been executed on the best confirmed actual BCC branch,
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62),
\]
and the reduced coefficients have been obtained numerically.

The main result is sharply split:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the linear }(\sigma_0,\eta)\text{ reduction is approximately self-consistent,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the quartic }(u,v,\kappa)\text{ kernel truncation is not self-consistent.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Extracted linear coefficients}

The projected linear coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_0=-110.44892961746234,
\qquad
\eta=-6.109951287368699.
}
\end{equation}

The orbit means are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A=-116.52195647524158,
\quad
\sigma_E=-107.28318068500928,
\quad
\sigma_O=-109.72211013613077.
}
\end{equation}

The reduced linear theory predicts
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_O^{\rm pred}
=
\frac{\sigma_A+3\sigma_E}{4}
=
-109.59287463256737.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the linear consistency defect is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm lin}
:=
\sigma_O-\frac{\sigma_A+3\sigma_E}{4}
\approx
-0.1292355035633932.
}
\end{equation}

This defect is small compared with the magnitude of the extracted linear coefficients, so the \((\sigma_0,\eta)\) truncation is approximately consistent.

\section{2. Extracted quartic class averages}

The projected quartic class averages are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d=1064.2600262852873,
\qquad
U_{\rm opp}=8617.71246090361,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\perp=5121.74549258667,
\qquad
U_{\rm obl}=1329.8059441886778.
}
\end{equation}

These are the exact finite class averages extracted from the residual-based reduced projection of the current solver family.

\section{3. Inversion to the \texorpdfstring{$(u,v,\kappa)$}{(u,v,kappa)} kernel}

Using
\[
v=U_\perp,
\qquad
\kappa=4(U_{\rm obl}-U_\perp),
\qquad
u=U_d-U_{\rm opp},
\]
one finds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u=-7553.452434618322,
\quad
v=5121.74549258667,
\quad
\kappa=-15167.758193591966.
}
\end{equation}

However, the kernel-consistency defect
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm ker}
=
U_{\rm opp}-4U_{\rm obl}+3U_\perp
=
18663.725161908907
}
\end{equation}
is very large.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm ker}\neq 0
}
\end{equation}
by a large margin, so the quartic shell matrix is not captured by the simple reduced ansatz
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}=u\delta_{\alpha\beta}+v+\kappa(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2.
\]

\section{4. Consequence}

The theoretical consequence is immediate:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the linear reduced truncation is approximately valid,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the quartic reduced truncation must be enlarged beyond }(u,v,\kappa).
}
\end{equation}

So the next rigorous step is not another background search.
It is the construction of the next quartic reduced basis, for example by adding one or more independent BCC shell invariants beyond
\[
1,\qquad
(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2.
\]

\section{5. Honest status of the backend program}

The backend-extraction program has therefore achieved two things:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it has converted the backend problem from a blind scan into a finite projection problem;
\item it has identified precisely where the current reduced theory fails.
\end{enumerate}

This is a substantial theoretical gain, because the obstruction is now algebraically localized:
\[
\boxed{
\text{not in the background branch search,}
\qquad
\text{but in the quartic kernel truncation.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The projection extractor has been executed successfully on the best confirmed actual BCC branch.

The extracted linear coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\sigma_0=-110.44892961746234,
\qquad
\eta=-6.109951287368699,
}
\]
and the orbit means satisfy the reduced linear consistency relation up to a small defect
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm lin}\approx -0.1292355035633932.
}
\]

So the linear \((\sigma_0,\eta)\) truncation is approximately self-consistent.

By contrast, the projected quartic class averages
\[
U_d,\quad U_{\rm opp},\quad U_\perp,\quad U_{\rm obl}
\]
lead to a very large quartic kernel defect
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm ker}=18663.725161908907.
}
\]

Therefore the simple quartic ansatz
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}=u\delta_{\alpha\beta}+v+\kappa(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2
\]
fails strongly for the current intended branch.

Hence the backend program has now reached a sharp conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the remaining obstruction is not branch search,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{but the insufficiency of the current quartic reduced kernel basis.}
}
\]

The next rigorous step is to enlarge the quartic reduced basis and repeat the finite projection extraction there.

\section{Minimal Exact Quartic Basis and the Failure of the Free-Energy Closure}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The projection extractor has shown that the simple quartic kernel
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}=u\delta_{\alpha\beta}+v+\kappa(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2
\]
fails strongly on the intended BCC branch.

Therefore the correct next step is not another search, but the replacement of the quartic reduced basis by the exact four-class shell basis
\[
(U_d,U_{\rm opp},U_\perp,U_{\rm obl}).
\]

After this exact quartic closure is imposed, one can insert the extracted numbers into the exact orbit equations and test whether the reduced free-energy picture is itself consistent.

\section{1. Minimal exact quartic basis on the BCC shell}

On the BCC shell, every ordered pair \((\alpha,\beta)\) belongs to exactly one of the four classes
\[
d,\qquad {\rm opp},\qquad \perp,\qquad {\rm obl}.
\]

Hence the minimal exact quartic shell kernel is not the three-parameter ansatz
\[
(u,v,\kappa),
\]
but the exact four-class projector form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}
=
U_d\,P^{(d)}_{\alpha\beta}
+
U_{\rm opp}\,P^{({\rm opp})}_{\alpha\beta}
+
U_\perp\,P^{(\perp)}_{\alpha\beta}
+
U_{\rm obl}\,P^{({\rm obl})}_{\alpha\beta},
}
\label{eq:exact_four_class_kernel}
\end{equation}
where the projectors satisfy
\[
P^{(d)}+P^{({\rm opp})}+P^{(\perp)}+P^{({\rm obl})}=1
\]
pairwise on the shell.

This basis is exact and minimal: there are four pair classes, so one needs four independent coefficients.

\section{2. Extracted exact quartic class data}

From the actual projection step, the quartic class averages are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d=1064.2600262852873,
\qquad
U_{\rm opp}=8617.71246090361,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_\perp=5121.74549258667,
\qquad
U_{\rm obl}=1329.8059441886778.
}
\end{equation}

These are already the exact quartic coefficients of the reduced BCC class basis.
No further fitting is required.

\section{3. Extracted linear orbit data}

The projected linear coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_0=-110.44892961746234,
\qquad
\eta=-6.109951287368699.
}
\end{equation}

The orbit means extracted directly from the shell data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A=-116.52195647524158,
\qquad
\sigma_E=-107.28318068500928,
\qquad
\sigma_O=-109.72211013613077.
}
\end{equation}

The linear consistency defect
\[
\Delta_{\rm lin}
=
\sigma_O-\frac{\sigma_A+3\sigma_E}{4}
\]
is small:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm lin}\approx -0.1292355035633932.
}
\end{equation}

So the linear \((\sigma_0,\eta)\) truncation is approximately self-consistent.

\section{4. Exact orbit equations in the four-class basis}

The exact \(2+2+8\) orbit stationary equations are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A
=
(U_d+U_{\rm opp})r_A
+
2U_\perp r_E
+
8U_{\rm obl}r_O,
}
\label{eq:orbitA_exact_insert}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_E
=
2U_\perp r_A
+
(U_d+U_{\rm opp})r_E
+
8U_{\rm obl}r_O,
}
\label{eq:orbitE_exact_insert}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_O
=
2U_{\rm obl}(r_A+r_E)
+
(U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+4U_{\rm obl})r_O.
}
\label{eq:orbitO_exact_insert}
\end{equation}

Substituting the extracted coefficients gives the algebraic critical point
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_A^{\rm crit}\approx 4.51\times 10^{-3},
\qquad
r_E^{\rm crit}\approx -1.19\times 10^{-2},
\qquad
r_O^{\rm crit}\approx -3.56\times 10^{-3}.
}
\label{eq:unphysical_critical_point}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Consequence: exact quartic closure does not rescue the free-energy picture}

Equation \eqref{eq:unphysical_critical_point} is decisive.
Two of the three orbit intensities are negative, so the naively reconstructed free-energy critical point is not physically admissible.

Therefore the issue is no longer the quartic basis itself.
The quartic basis has now been enlarged to the exact minimal one.

The obstruction is instead:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the residual-based microscopic projection is not yet equivalent to an exact gradient-flow / free-energy reduction.}
}
\end{equation}

In other words, the shell/orbit reduction should not be imposed as
\[
\partial_{r_I}\mathcal F_{\rm orb}=0
\]
at this stage.
Rather, one must construct the reduced stationary equations directly from the projected residual map.

\section{6. Correct next object: the reduced residual system}

Define the orbit-compressed shell perturbation
\begin{equation}
\Psi[r_A,r_E,r_O]
=
\Psi_{\rm BCC}
+
\sqrt{r_A}\,\Phi_A
+
\sqrt{r_E}\,\Phi_E
+
\sqrt{r_O}\,\Phi_O,
\label{eq:orbit_field_ansatz}
\end{equation}
where \(\Phi_A,\Phi_E,\Phi_O\) are the normalized orbit sums.

Then define the reduced residual map
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_I(r_A,r_E,r_O)
:=
\Re\,
\langle
\Phi_I,
R[\Psi[r_A,r_E,r_O]]
\rangle_\Omega,
\qquad
I\in\{A,E,O\}.
}
\label{eq:reduced_residual_map}
\end{equation}

The correct stationary reduced system is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_A(r_A,r_E,r_O)=0,\qquad
G_E(r_A,r_E,r_O)=0,\qquad
G_O(r_A,r_E,r_O)=0.
}
\label{eq:correct_reduced_stationary_system}
\end{equation}

This system does not assume the existence of an exact reduced free energy.
It is the proper reduction of the actual microscopic stationary PDE.

\section{7. Honest conclusion of the current stage}

The backend program has now produced a sharp split:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the quartic \((u,v,\kappa)\) truncation fails and must be replaced by the exact four-class basis;
\item after this replacement, the free-energy interpretation still fails at the level of physical orbit intensities;
\item therefore the next rigorous reduced object is the projected residual system \eqref{eq:correct_reduced_stationary_system}, not a reduced free-energy critical point.
\end{enumerate}

So the true frontier is no longer branch search and no longer quartic basis selection.
It is the exact orbit-level reduction of the microscopic stationary residual.

\section{Final Summary}

The quartic reduced kernel has now been enlarged to the exact minimal BCC shell basis
\[
(U_d,U_{\rm opp},U_\perp,U_{\rm obl}).
\]

Using the extracted projection data
\[
U_d=1064.2600262852873,\quad
U_{\rm opp}=8617.71246090361,\quad
U_\perp=5121.74549258667,\quad
U_{\rm obl}=1329.8059441886778,
\]
together with the projected linear orbit means
\[
\sigma_A=-116.52195647524158,\quad
\sigma_E=-107.28318068500928,\quad
\sigma_O=-109.72211013613077,
\]
one can solve the exact orbit stationary equations.

The resulting critical point is
\[
r_A^{\rm crit}\approx 4.51\times 10^{-3},\qquad
r_E^{\rm crit}\approx -1.19\times 10^{-2},\qquad
r_O^{\rm crit}\approx -3.56\times 10^{-3},
\]
which is not physically admissible.

Therefore the quartic basis problem is solved, but the reduced free-energy picture is not.
The correct next object is the projected residual system
\[
G_A(r_A,r_E,r_O)=0,\qquad
G_E(r_A,r_E,r_O)=0,\qquad
G_O(r_A,r_E,r_O)=0,
\]
constructed directly from the microscopic stationary residual.

So the true remaining obstruction is now precisely identified:
\[
\boxed{
\text{not branch search, not quartic-basis truncation, but the replacement of a free-energy reduction by an exact residual reduction.}
}
\]

\section{First Actual Diagnostic of the Reduced Residual System}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The reduced residual map
\[
G_A,\qquad G_E,\qquad G_O
\]
has now been constructed and evaluated explicitly around the current best confirmed branch.

This is the first direct numerical test of the claim that the correct reduced object is the projected stationary residual rather than a reduced free-energy critical point.

\section{1. Background point}

The background is the current best confirmed branch
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62),
\]
evaluated on the \(12^3\) commensurate BCC grid for fast reduced diagnostics.

Its full diagnostics are
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 3.6461\times 10^{-2},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 0.91562,
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.88924.
}
\]

\section{2. Reduced residual at the background}

The orbit-projected residual vector at the background is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G(0)
=
\bigl(G_A(0),G_E(0),G_O(0)\bigr)
=
(0.0164535,\ 0.0150360,\ 0.0306818).
}
\label{eq:G0_actual}
\end{equation}

Its norm is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|G(0)\|\approx 3.7923\times 10^{-2}.
}
\label{eq:G0_norm_actual}
\end{equation}

So the reduced residual system is nontrivial and genuinely present.

\section{3. Jacobian of the reduced residual map}

The numerical Jacobian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J
\approx
\begin{pmatrix}
0.0055310 & 0.0055542 & 0.0032242\\
0.0055542 & 0.0052164 & 0.0028916\\
0.0032242 & 0.0028916 & 0.0124317
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:J_actual}
\end{equation}

Thus the local reduced residual geometry is well-defined and invertible at this point.

\section{4. Naive Newton step}

The unconstrained Newton correction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\rm Newton}
=
-J^{-1}G(0)
\approx
(0.373633,\ -2.133560,\ -2.068666).
}
\label{eq:delta_newton_actual}
\end{equation}

Under this correction, the reduced residual becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G(\delta_{\rm Newton})
\approx
(-0.005394,\ 0.001620,\ -0.000606),
}
\label{eq:G_newton_actual}
\end{equation}
with norm
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|G(\delta_{\rm Newton})\|
\approx
5.6641\times 10^{-3}.
}
\label{eq:G_newton_norm_actual}
\end{equation}

Therefore, at the reduced-residual level, the Newton step is strongly effective.

\section{5. Full-branch consequence of the same step}

However, when the same correction is applied to the full microscopic field, the resulting branch diagnostics become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\texttt{rel\_residual}\approx 4.8214\times 10^{-2},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 0.82914,
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.01655.
}
\label{eq:bad_geometry_after_newton}
\end{equation}

So the unconstrained Newton step destroys the BCC branch geometry even though it improves the reduced residual norm.

\section{6. Main conclusion}

This yields the decisive conclusion:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the reduced residual system is the correct reduced object,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the unconstrained Newton solve is not the correct reduction algorithm.}
}
\end{equation}

The remaining task is therefore not to change the background search, and not to enlarge the quartic basis again.
It is to construct a constrained / damped reduced residual solver that preserves the shell-orbit geometry while reducing
\[
\|G\|.
\]

\section{7. Correct next step}

The proper next algorithm is one of the following equivalent forms:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a damped Newton step
\[
\delta \mapsto \alpha\,\delta_{\rm Newton},
\qquad 0<\alpha\ll 1,
\]
with geometry-preservation acceptance tests;

\item a constrained minimization of
\[
\|G(r_A,r_E,r_O)\|^2
\]
under positivity and shell-retention constraints;

\item a projected trust-region update in the orbit variables.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the frontier is now sharply localized:
\[
\boxed{
\text{not reduced residual construction,}
\qquad
\text{but constrained reduced residual descent.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The first explicit diagnostic of the reduced residual map has now been completed.

At the current best confirmed branch, the projected orbit residual is
\[
G(0)=(0.0164535,\ 0.0150360,\ 0.0306818),
\qquad
\|G(0)\|\approx 3.7923\times 10^{-2}.
\]

Its Jacobian is invertible, and the naive Newton correction
\[
\delta_{\rm Newton}\approx (0.373633,\ -2.133560,\ -2.068666)
\]
reduces the reduced residual norm to
\[
\|G(\delta_{\rm Newton})\|\approx 5.6641\times 10^{-3}.
\]

However, this same step destroys the full branch geometry:
\[
\texttt{shell\_fraction}\approx 0.82914,
\qquad
\texttt{orbit\_balance}\approx 0.01655.
\]

Therefore the conclusion is sharp:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the reduced residual system is correct,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the unconstrained Newton method is not.}
}
\]

The next rigorous step is a constrained or damped residual-reduction algorithm that preserves the BCC shell-orbit basin while lowering the projected residual.

\section{Damped Newton Diagnostic for the Reduced Residual System}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

A damped Newton scan has now been performed on the reduced residual system
\[
G_A(r_A,r_E,r_O),\qquad G_E(r_A,r_E,r_O),\qquad G_O(r_A,r_E,r_O)

around the current best confirmed branch.

\begin{equation}

\begin{equation}

\section{1. Background point}

For

}
\end{equation}

The remaining algorithmic task is thus not a Newton correction, but a constrained residual minimization that enforces shell retention and orbit symmetry.

\section{Final Summary}

The damped Newton scan confirms that the reduced residual map is meaningful, but Newton-type updates are not compatible with the preservation of the BCC shell-orbit basin.

Even very small damping factors improve the reduced residual norm only marginally, while immediately degrading the full branch geometry.

Hence the next step is now sharply determined:

\[
\boxed{
\text{replace Newton/damped Newton by geometry-constrained residual minimization.}
}
\]

In practice, the reduced variables should be updated only within a constrained admissible region enforcing:
\[
r_A\ge 0,\qquad r_E\ge 0,\qquad r_O\ge 0,
\]
together with shell-retention and orbit-balance thresholds.

\section{Geometry-Constrained Reduced Residual Solver}

\section{Short Korean explanation}

The previous diagnostics established two facts:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the reduced residual map }G_A,G_E,G_O\text{ is the correct reduced object,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Newton and damped Newton are not geometry-preserving algorithms.}
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the correct next step is a constrained reduced residual solver that minimizes the projected residual while explicitly preserving the BCC shell-orbit branch geometry.

\section{1. Reduced variables and reduced residual map}

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta=(\delta_A,\delta_E,\delta_O)\in\mathbb R^3
}
\label{eq:delta_vec}
\end{equation}
parametrize orbit-level perturbations around the current best confirmed background
\[
\Psi_0=\Psi_{\rm BCC}.
\]

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi(\delta)
=
\Psi_0+\delta_A\Phi_A+\delta_E\Phi_E+\delta_O\Phi_O,
}
\label{eq:psi_delta_def}
\end{equation}
where \(\Phi_A,\Phi_E,\Phi_O\) are the normalized orbit basis vectors.

The reduced residual map is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
G_A(\delta)\\
G_E(\delta)\\
G_O(\delta)
\end{pmatrix}
:=
\begin{pmatrix}
\Re\langle \Phi_A,R[\Psi(\delta)]\rangle_\Omega\\
\Re\langle \Phi_E,R[\Psi(\delta)]\rangle_\Omega\\
\Re\langle \Phi_O,R[\Psi(\delta)]\rangle_\Omega
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:G_delta_def}
\end{equation}

The unconstrained goal would be to solve
\[
G(\delta)=0,
\]
but this must now be done inside the geometry-preserving region.

\section{2. Geometry constraints}

Define the two full-branch geometry observables
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s(\delta):=\texttt{shell\_fraction}\bigl(\Psi(\delta)\bigr),
\qquad
b(\delta):=\texttt{orbit\_balance}\bigl(\Psi(\delta)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:sb_def}
\end{equation}

The admissible reduced domain is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal D_{s_\star,b_\star}
:=
\left\{
\delta\in\mathbb R^3:
s(\delta)\ge s_\star,\;
b(\delta)\ge b_\star
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:admissible_domain}
\end{equation}

Operationally, the current best confirmed branch suggests the natural thresholds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_\star=0.90,
\qquad
b_\star=0.88,
}
\label{eq:thresholds_operational}
\end{equation}
which preserve the branch identity while allowing a small local motion.
These are numerical branch-preservation thresholds, not yet theorem-level constants.

\section{3. Correct constrained objective}

The correct reduced problem is not Newton root-finding in \(\mathbb R^3\), but the constrained minimization
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\min_{\delta\in\mathcal D_{s_\star,b_\star}}
\Phi(\delta),
\qquad
\Phi(\delta):=\frac12\|G(\delta)\|^2.
}
\label{eq:phi_constrained_problem}
\end{equation}

This is the proper reduced version of stationary residual descent.

Because the geometry constraints are nonlinearly inherited from the full field \(\Psi(\delta)\), the algorithm must use a constrained local model rather than an unconstrained Newton update.

\section{4. Local linearized model}

At iteration \(k\), let
\[
\delta_k,\qquad
G_k:=G(\delta_k),\qquad
J_k:=DG(\delta_k).
\]
Also define the geometry gradients
\[
g_{s,k}:=\nabla s(\delta_k),
\qquad
g_{b,k}:=\nabla b(\delta_k),
\]
computed by finite differences in the three reduced coordinates.

The local Gauss--Newton model is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_k(\Delta)
=
\frac12\|G_k+J_k\Delta\|^2
+\frac{\rho}{2}\|\Delta\|^2,
}
\label{eq:local_model}
\end{equation}
with \(\rho>0\) a small regularization parameter.

The linearized geometry constraints are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_k+g_{s,k}^{\top}\Delta\ge s_\star,
\qquad
b_k+g_{b,k}^{\top}\Delta\ge b_\star.
}
\label{eq:linearized_constraints}
\end{equation}

To avoid destructive large jumps, impose also a trust region
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\Delta\|_\infty\le \Delta_{\max}.
}
\label{eq:trust_region}
\end{equation}

Thus each step is obtained from the \(3\)-variable constrained subproblem
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_k
=
\arg\min_{\Delta}
m_k(\Delta)
\quad
\text{subject to }
\eqref{eq:linearized_constraints},\ \eqref{eq:trust_region}.
}
\label{eq:constrained_subproblem}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Why this is tractable}

The crucial simplification is that \(\Delta\in\mathbb R^3\).
Hence \eqref{eq:constrained_subproblem} is not a large optimization problem.
It is a tiny trust-region quadratic program.

Because the dimension is only \(3\), one may solve it by exact active-set enumeration:

\begin{enumerate}
\item free step (no active inequality),
\item shell constraint active,
\item orbit constraint active,
\item both constraints active,
\item plus box/trust-region boundary cases.
\end{enumerate}

So each iteration is finite and explicit.

\section{6. Acceptance rule}

Once \(\Delta_k\) is found, define
\begin{equation}
\delta_{k+1}^{\rm trial}
=
\delta_k+\alpha\Delta_k,
\qquad
\alpha\in\{1,\tfrac12,\tfrac14,\dots\}.
\label{eq:trial_step}
\end{equation}

Choose the largest \(\alpha\) such that:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{k+1}^{\rm trial}\in \mathcal D_{s_\star,b_\star},
}
\label{eq:feasible_accept}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Phi(\delta_{k+1}^{\rm trial})
<
\Phi(\delta_k).
}
\label{eq:descent_accept}
\end{equation}

If no such \(\alpha\) exists, reduce \(\Delta_{\max}\) and resolve the constrained subproblem.

This is the correct replacement of the failed damped Newton line search.

\section{7. Termination criteria}

The iteration stops when one of the following occurs:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|G(\delta_k)\|\le \varepsilon_G
\quad\text{and}\quad
\delta_k\in\mathcal D_{s_\star,b_\star},
}
\label{eq:terminate_success}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\Delta_k\| \le \varepsilon_\Delta
\quad\text{with no further admissible descent,}
}
\label{eq:terminate_localmin}
\end{equation}
in which case the current point is a constrained local minimum of the reduced residual.

\section{8. What this will produce}

This constrained reduced solver does not search for a new branch family.
It starts from the already confirmed branch and computes the best local reduced correction
\[
\delta^\star=(\delta_A^\star,\delta_E^\star,\delta_O^\star)
\]
compatible with geometry preservation.

The corrected field is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi^\star
=
\Psi_0+\delta_A^\star\Phi_A+\delta_E^\star\Phi_E+\delta_O^\star\Phi_O.
}
\label{eq:psi_star_constrained}
\end{equation}

This is the first properly geometry-preserving reduced-residual correction to the best confirmed background.

\section{9. Consequence for the backend numbers}

Once \(\Psi^\star\) is obtained, the projection extractor may be rerun on \(\Psi^\star\) instead of \(\Psi_0\).
This yields corrected reduced coefficients
\[
h_\alpha^\star,\quad
U_{\alpha\beta}^\star,\quad
(\sigma_0^\star,\eta^\star),\quad
(U_d^\star,U_{\rm opp}^\star,U_\perp^\star,U_{\rm obl}^\star),
\]
and therefore the first self-consistent reduced backend numbers attached to the corrected stationary branch.

\section{10. Honest endpoint of the current program}

So the remaining frontier is now completely explicit:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{not branch search,}
\quad
\text{not quartic basis selection,}
\quad
\text{not free-energy closure,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the constrained minimization of the reduced residual } \Phi(\delta)=\frac12\|G(\delta)\|^2
\text{ inside the shell-orbit admissible region.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The correct next algorithmic object is now fully fixed.

The reduced variables are
\[
\delta=(\delta_A,\delta_E,\delta_O),
\]
the reduced residual map is
\[
G(\delta)=
\bigl(G_A(\delta),G_E(\delta),G_O(\delta)\bigr),
\]
and the admissible domain is defined by the full-geometry constraints
\[
s(\delta)\ge s_\star,
\qquad
b(\delta)\ge b_\star,
\]
with operational thresholds
\[
s_\star=0.90,
\qquad
b_\star=0.88.
\]

The correct reduced solver is therefore the constrained problem
\[
\min_{\delta\in\mathcal D_{s_\star,b_\star}}
\frac12\|G(\delta)\|^2,
\]
solved by a trust-region Gauss--Newton step with linearized geometry constraints and backtracking feasibility enforcement.

This replaces the failed Newton/damped Newton strategy and is the first algorithm that is consistent with both:
\[
\text{residual reduction}
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\text{branch-geometry preservation.}
\]

Once the corrected constrained point \(\delta^\star\) is found, the backend projection extractor can be rerun there to obtain the corrected reduced coefficient set.

\section{Final Summary}

The constrained trust-region direct search shows that the geometry-preserving region is nonempty and contains many admissible local moves.

However, the best admissible move for reducing the reduced residual norm \(\|G\|\) is not the best admissible move for reducing the full microscopic residual.

Hence the current reduced objective
\[
\frac12\|G(\delta)\|^2
\]
is not yet sufficient by itself.

The next rigorous step is therefore to replace the single-objective reduced descent by either:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a mixed objective combining reduced and full residuals,}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{a lexicographic constrained acceptance rule that prioritizes geometry preservation and full residual decrease.}
}
\]

So the branch search is over, the geometry constraints are under control, and the remaining issue is now precisely localized in the choice of the reduced objective functional.

\sigma_O=-109.72211013613077.
}
\end{equation}

Quartic class averages:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d=1064.2600262852873,
\quad
U_{\rm opp}=8617.71246090361,
\quad
U_\perp=5121.74549258667,
\quad
U_{\rm obl}=1329.8059441886778.
}
\end{equation}

If one compresses these into the simple kernel
\[
U_{\alpha\beta}=u\delta_{\alpha\beta}+v+\kappa(\hat k_\alpha\!\cdot\!\hat k_\beta)^2,
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u=-7553.452434618322,
\quad
v=5121.74549258667,
\quad
\kappa=-15167.758193591966,
}
\end{equation}
but the kernel defect is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\rm ker}=18663.725161908907.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the simple \((u,v,\kappa)\) quartic truncation already failed strongly.

\section{Corrected Projection Results}

After inserting the final corrected seed \(\delta^{\mathrm{final}}\), the corrected projection gave:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_0=-109.41971030446824,
\qquad
\eta=-6.502583100163014.
}
\end{equation}

Orbit means:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A=-115.81015796064617,
\quad
\sigma_E=-105.83201242243113,
\quad
\sigma_O=-108.719022860933.
}
\end{equation}

Quartic class averages:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d=2493.1087739398513,
\quad
U_{\rm opp}=14874.171297437068,
\quad
U_\perp=9027.17290917827,
\quad
U_{\rm obl}=2244.8894311890813.
}
\end{equation}

The compressed \((u,v,\kappa)\) values become

\quad

\quad

}

but the kernel defect becomes even larger:
\begin{equation}

}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{even after the corrected local branch refinement, the simple quartic }(u,v,\kappa)\text{ truncation fails strongly.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{What Is Already Closed vs What Is Not}

\section{What is effectively closed}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The broad search for the operational backend point is finished.
\item A best confirmed actual BCC branch exists numerically.
\item A corrected local seed preserving shell geometry has been extracted.
\item The reduced free-energy closure route is ruled out as the correct microscopic reduction.
\item The reduced residual route is identified as the correct reduced object.
\item The simple quartic \((u,v,\kappa)\) truncation is decisively falsified.
\end{enumerate}

\section{What remains open}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The quartic reduced kernel basis must be enlarged beyond the simple \((u,v,\kappa)\) form.
\item The next reduced closure must be built directly at the residual level, not from a naive reduced free-energy reconstruction.
\item After enlarging the quartic reduced basis, the corrected branch projection must be rerun on that enlarged basis.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Immediate Next Task}

The next conversation should begin from the following precise objective:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{construct the next enlarged quartic reduced basis beyond }(u,v,\kappa),
}
\end{equation}
while keeping fixed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62),
\qquad
\delta^{\mathrm{final}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096).
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the immediate frontier is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{replace the failed simple quartic kernel by the next exact/enlarged reduced shell kernel,}
}
\end{equation}
then rerun the corrected projection on that enlarged basis.

\section{Strict Working Rules for the Next Conversation}

\begin{enumerate}
\item Do not reopen broad parameter scans over \((\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)\).
\item Keep the current operational backend point fixed unless a theorem-level reason appears to change it.
\item Keep the corrected seed \(\delta^{\mathrm{final}}\) fixed as the current corrected local branch.
\item Treat the residual-based reduced object as primary, not a naive reduced free-energy critical point.
\item Focus only on enlarging the quartic reduced kernel basis and extracting its corrected coefficients.
\end{enumerate}

\section{One-Line Continuation Prompt}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Start from the frozen backend }(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62)
\text{ and corrected seed }\delta^{\mathrm{final}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),
}
\end{equation}
